Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Using the Hadith of the Musii to Establish Prayer Obligations: A Hanafi Perspective
Expansion on the use of the hadith of the musii to define prayer obligations, addressing a madhhab dispute on khabar wahid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school uses the hadith of the musii (a khabar wahid) to confirm obligations in prayer, and distinguish this from the view that khabar wahid cannot establish fard independently.

Core Idea
A solitary hadith cannot create a new obligation, but it confirms and details what is already indicated by definitive proofs.

The hadith of the musii, where the Prophet taught a man who prayed incorrectly, is a cornerstone for deriving the obligations of prayer. However, this hadith is a khabar wahid (solitary report), which raises questions about its evidentiary weight. In this lesson, we explore how the Hanafi school navigates this issue, using the hadith to confirm obligations that already have Qur'anic or mutawatir support, while rejecting its ability to establish entirely new obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its content
Read the full hadith of the musii as quoted in the passage. Note the specific actions commanded by the Prophet: ablution, facing qibla, takbir, recitation, bowing, prostration, etc.
The hadith is found in Sahih Muslim and Bukhari, narrated by Abu Huraira.
2
Understand how jurists used the hadith
Jurists deduced obligation for mentioned acts (command implies wujub) and non-obligation for unmentioned acts (context of teaching limits obligations to what is taught).
The command 'if' (idha) plus imperative is a standard indicator of obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Recognize the objection: khabar wahid cannot establish fard
Some commentators argue that since this hadith is a solitary report, it cannot by itself make anything obligatory (fard). This is a legitimate usul position.
Recall that in Hanafi theory, fard requires qat'i evidence; wajib can be from zanni.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The author defends that Hanafis do not use the hadith independently; they use it to confirm obligations already supported by definitive texts. The hadith's indication is qat'i (clear obligation) even if its transmission is zanni.
This is like saying 'fard by transmission and reason'—the hadith confirms what reason or other texts already indicate.
5
Apply to a specific element: salam or opening supplication
Hanafis do not consider salam as fard because it is not in the hadith and lacks a definitive proof. This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf (practical outcome) of the dispute.
Other schools may have different rulings based on other evidence.

طرداً وعكساً. وقال بعض الشارحين : رداً لاستدلالهم والحق أن هذا خبر واحد لا يفيد فرضية شيء أصلاً. أقول : الاستدلال منهم صحيح، أما على قول الشافعي ومالك فظاهر لأنهما يريان إثبات الفرض بخبر الواحد، وأما على مذهبنا فكذلك لأن مثل هذا الاستدلال أعني به الاستدلال بنفس مفهوم النص الغير القطعي على إثبات فرضية شيء إذا كان دلالته عليه قطعياً شائع كثير فيما بين العلماء وإن لم يكن ذلك مستقلاً في إثباته لعدم قطعية ثبوته ويقصدون بذلك تأكيد مضمون القطعي به. ألا ترى أنهم يقولون في كثير من المواضع في كتبهم لإثبات فرضية شيء أنه فرض بالنقل والعقل،
And the correct view, as mentioned by Imam Najm al-Din in his Tafsir and al-Nawawi in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, is that what is meant by it is the Kaaba, so it is the qibla, as indicated by most ahadith, including what is in Sahih Muslim from al-Bara: 'We prayed with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) towards Jerusalem for sixteen or seventeen months, then we were turned towards the Kaaba.' And the point in mentioning the Sacred Mosque while intending the Kaaba, as in al-Kashshaf, is to indicate that what is obligatory for the absent person is the direction. And from the Sunnah, many include his statement (peace be upon him) to the person who prayed badly: 'When you stand for prayer, perform ablution properly, then face the qibla and say takbir.' Narrated by Muslim. And its commentary is connected... His statement: 'When you stand for prayer, perform ablution...' and the complete hadith is what is mentioned in the two Sahihs with their chain to Abu Huraira (may Allah be pleased with him) that a man entered the mosque while the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was sitting in a corner of the mosque, prayed, then came and greeted the Prophet (peace be upon him). The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'And upon you be peace. Go back and pray, for you have not prayed.' So he went back and prayed as he had prayed, then came and greeted him. He said: 'And upon you be peace. Go back and pray, for you have not prayed.' He did that three times. Then the man said: 'By Him Who sent you with the truth, I cannot do better than this, so teach me.' He said: 'When you stand for prayer, perform ablution properly, then face the qibla and say takbir. Then recite what is easy of the Quran while standing. Then bow until you are at ease in bowing. Then rise until you are straight. Then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration. Then rise until you are at ease sitting. Then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration. Then rise until you are standing straight. Then do that throughout your prayer.' The jurists used this hadith to deduce the obligation of what is mentioned in it, whether it is done in prayer or outside it, and the non-obligation of what is not mentioned in it in prayer. As for the obligation of what is mentioned in it, it is because he was commanded to do it, and the command indicates obligation as known in usul. As for the non-obligation of what is not mentioned in it in prayer, it is because the context is that of teaching prayer and defining its pillars, which necessitates limiting the obligations to what is mentioned therein, lest there be a delay in clarification at the time of need, which is not permissible. The detail is that he (peace be upon him) commanded him in this hadith to perform ablution, face the qibla, say takbir, recite what is easy of the Quran, bow, rise from it, the first prostration, rise from it, the second prostration, and rise from it. So the command indicates the obligation of these things. And his statement 'until you are at ease in bowing' and 'until you are at ease' and 'until you are at ease sitting' and 'until you are standing straight' indicates the obligation of proper execution of the pillars. This is what is mentioned in the hadith. As for their deduction of the non-obligation of what is not mentioned in it, among them are: they deduced the non-obligation of the opening supplication because it is not mentioned in it; some Malikis deduced the non-obligation of the tashahhud for that reason; and some Hanafis deduced the non-obligation of the salam for that reason. The discussions of the jurists on this have been extensive, both positively and negatively. And one commentator said, in refutation of their deduction: 'The truth is that this is a solitary report (khabar wahid) which does not establish the obligation of anything at all.' I say: Their deduction is correct. As for the view of al-Shafi'i and Malik, it is obvious because they hold that obligation can be established by a solitary report. As for our madhhab, it is similarly so, because such deduction — I mean deduction by the very concept of a non-definitive text to establish the obligation of something, if its indication is definitive — is common among scholars, even if it is not independent in establishing it due to the lack of definitiveness in its transmission. They intend by that to confirm the content of the definitive. Do you not see that they say in many places in their books, to establish the obligation of something, that it is obligatory by transmission and reason?
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling regarding the qibla and the use of the hadith of the musii (the person who prayed badly) to determine the obligations of prayer. The author begins by clarifying that 'the Sacred Mosque' in the Qur'an refers specifically to the Kaaba, not the entire sanctuary, as stated by Imam Najm al-Din and al-Nawawi. The qibla for one who is absent is the direction (jiha). The hadith of the musii is then cited in full. Jurists have used this hadith to deduce the obligation of the acts mentioned (like facing the qibla, takbir, recitation, bowing, prostration, etc.) and the non-obligation of what is not mentioned (like opening supplication, tashahhud, salam). The author defends the Hanafi position that although this hadith is a khabar wahid (solitary report), it can be used to confirm obligations that are already supported by definitive texts (Qur'an or mutawatir Sunnah), not to establish new obligations independently. The commentator's objection that a khabar wahid cannot establish any fard is refuted by noting that such reports are used in conjunction with definitive proofs. The key principle is that acts mentioned in the hadith that also have Qur'anic support become obligations, while acts not mentioned but lacking definitive support are not made obligatory by this hadith alone. This explains why the Hanafis do not consider the opening supplication, tashahhud, and salam as obligatory, as they are not in the hadith and lack other definitive evidence.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators at any level of the chain, not reaching tawatur.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that is established by a definitive proof (qat'i) such as Qur'an or mutawatir Sunnah.
المسيء صلاته (al-musii salatahu): The person who prayed badly, whose hadith is used to derive obligations of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, why is the salam (greeting at end of prayer) not considered obligatory (fard)?
A) Because the hadith of the musii does not mention it, and no definitive text supports its obligation.
B) Because it is makruh to say salam.
C) Because the Qur'an prohibits it.
D) Because the Prophet never said salam in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the hadith of the musii to confirm the obligations of prayer, but does not rely on it alone to establish new fard acts; rather, it complements definitive evidence.

Facing the Qibla: Exact Spot vs Direction
Distinction between the requirement for a Makkan to face the exact Kaaba and for others to face its direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla for a Makkan who can see the Kaaba versus one who cannot, and apply the relied-upon view to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Facing the exact Kaaba is required only for those who see it; others must face its direction.

The obligation of facing the qibla is unconditional, but the degree of precision required depends on the person's location and ability. In this passage, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the distinction between a person in Makkah (al-Makki) and others, and between those who can see the Kaaba and those who cannot. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the ruling and recognizing where scholarly difference exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of persons
The passage divides people into two categories: the Makkan (al-Makki) and non-Makkan (al-afaqi or al-ghayr). Within the Makkan, there is a further distinction between one who sees the Kaaba and one who does not.
2
Determine the obligation for each category
For the Makkan who sees the Kaaba, the obligation is to face the exact spot (isabat al-ayn). For the non-Makkan (and, by the preferred view, the Makkan who does not see it), the obligation is to face the direction (jiha).
The direction is defined as the side that aligns with the Kaaba or its airspace, either exactly or approximately.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
A stricter view from al-Kafi holds that even a Makkan who does not see the Kaaba must face the exact spot if obstacles were removed. The author considers this weak and presents the preferred view (al-mukhtar) from al-Tanjis: only the one who sees the Kaaba requires the exact spot.
This disagreement affects how one rules for a Makkan praying inside a building.
4
Understand the rationale for the distinction
The distinction is based on ability to achieve certainty (al-qudra 'ala al-yaqin). Those who can see the Kaaba can be certain of the exact direction; others cannot, so only the direction is required.
This reflects the principle that obligations are based on capacity.
5
Apply to a given scenario
Take a scenario: a person in the courtyard of the Masjid al-Haram cannot see the Kaaba due to a pillar. According to the preferred view, he must only face the direction, not the exact spot. His prayer is valid even if he is not exactly aligned.
This is because he does not have direct sight, so he is like the non-Makkan for this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إصابة جهتها والخائف يصلي إلى أي جهة قدر ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة تحرى وإن أخطأ الإجماع عليه. وفي عدة الفتاوى : الكعبة إذا رفعت عن مكانها لزيارة أصحاب الكرامة ففي تلك الحالة جازت صلاة المتوجهين إلى أرضها قوله : (فللمكي فرضه إصابة عينها) أي عين القبلة بمعنى الكعبة للقدرة على اليقين أطلق في المكي فشمل من كان بمعاينتها ومن لم يكن حتى لو صلى مكي في بيته ينبعي أن يصلي بحيث لو أزيلت الجدران يقع استقباله على شطر الكعبة بخلاف الآفاقي فإنه لو أزيلت الموانع لا يشترط أن يقع استقباله على عين الكعبة لا محالة. كذا في الكافي وهو ضعيف. قال في الدراية : من كان بينه وبين الكعبة حائل الأصح أنه كالغائب، ولو كان الحائل أصلياً كالجبل كان له أن يجتهد والأولى أن يصعده ليصل إلى اليقين. وفي التنجيس : من كان بمعاينة الكعبة فالشرط إصابة عينها، ومن لم يكن بمعاينتها فالشرط إصابة جهتها وهو المختار وفي فتح القدير : وعندي في جواز التحري مع إمكان صعوده إشكال لأن المصير إلى الدليل الظني وترك القاطع مع إمكانه لا يجوز. وما أقرب قوله الكتاب : والاستخبار فوق التحري فإذا امتنع المصير إلى الظني لإمكان ظني أقوى منه فكيف يترك اليقين مع إمكانه للظن؟ قوله : (ولغيره إصابة (جهتها أي لغير المكي فرضه إصابة جهتها وهو الجانب الذي إذا توجه إليه الشخص يكون مسامتاً للكعبة أو لهوائها إما تحقيقاً بمعنى أنه لو فرض خط من تلقاء وجهه على زواية قائمة إلى الأفق يكون ماراً على الكعبة أو هوائها، وإما تقريباً بمعنى أن يكون ذلك منحرفاً عن الكعبة أو هوائها انحرافاً لا تزول به المقابلة بالكلية بأن بقي شيء من
Hitting its direction. And the fearful one prays towards any direction he is able. And the one for whom the qibla is ambiguous performs ijtihad (estimation), and if he errs, there is consensus upon it. And in several fatawa: If the Kaaba is lifted from its place due to the visit of the people of karamah (spiritual miracles), in that situation the prayer of those facing its ground is valid. His statement: 'For the Makkan, his obligation is to hit its exact location' i.e., the exact qibla meaning the Kaaba, because he is able to have certainty. He spoke broadly about the Makkan, so it includes both the one who sees it and the one who does not. Even if a Makkan prays in his house, he should pray such that if the walls were removed, his facing would be towards the exact direction of the Kaaba. Unlike the non-Makkan, for if obstacles were removed, it is not required that his facing necessarily be towards the exact Kaaba. This is in al-Kafi, but it is weak. It is said in al-Diraya: The one who has a barrier between himself and the Kaaba, the correct view is that he is like the absent one. And if the barrier is original like a mountain, he may perform ijtihad, and it is better to climb it to reach certainty. And in al-Tanjis: The one who sees the Kaaba, the condition is hitting its exact site; the one who does not see it, the condition is hitting its direction. This is the chosen view. And in Fath al-Qadir: I have doubt about permissibility of ijtihad when climbing is possible, because resorting to a probable evidence while leaving the definitive while possible is not permissible. And how close is his statement in the book: And inquiry is above ijtihad. So when resorting to the probable is prevented due to the possibility of a stronger probable, how can one leave certainty while it is possible for probability? His statement: 'And for other than the Makkan, it is to hit its direction' i.e., for non-Makkan, his obligation is to hit its direction, which is the side that when a person faces it, he is aligned with the Kaaba or its air, either exactly meaning that if a line is assumed from the direction of his face at a right angle to the horizon, it passes over the Kaaba or its air, or approximately meaning that it is deviated from the Kaaba or its air by a deviation that does not completely remove correspondence, such that something of
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the obligation of facing the qibla. It begins by stating that the fearful person (e.g., in danger) may pray in any direction he can. If the qibla is ambiguous, he must make ijtihad (attempt to determine it); if he errs, his prayer is valid by consensus. The discussion then moves to the distinction between a person in Makkah (al-Makki) and one outside (al-afaqi or al-ghayr). For the Makkan, the obligation is to face the exact Kaaba (ayn al-Kaaba) because he can achieve certainty, either by sight or by knowing the direction precisely. Even if he is in his house with walls blocking direct sight, he must face a place such that if the walls were removed, he would be facing the exact Kaaba. This view from al-Kafi is considered weak by the author. The preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that whoever actually sees the Kaaba must face its exact spot; whoever does not see it (even if in Makkah but with obstacles) must only face the direction (jiha). For those outside Makkah (al-afaqi), the obligation is to face the direction (jiha) — i.e., a side that is aligned with the Kaaba or its air, either exactly (by being on a line that passes through the Kaaba) or approximately (by being within a range that the deviation does not remove facing altogether, as long as some part of the face is towards the Kaaba's air). The author also discusses the case of a barrier like a mountain: if one can climb it to gain certainty, he should do so, and it is problematic to resort to ijtihad when certainty is possible. This reflects the principle that one should not leave a definitive evidence for a probable one.

Key Terms
المكي (al-Makki): The person who is in Makkah, whether or not he can see the Kaaba directly.
جهة (jiha): The direction of the Kaaba; a side that when faced, the person is aligned with the Kaaba or its air, either exactly or approximately.
إصابة العين (isabat al-'ayn): Hitting the exact physical location of the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view in this passage, what is the condition for a person in Makkah who cannot see the Kaaba?
A) He must face the exact Kaaba, because he is in Makkah.
B) He must face the direction (jiha) of the Kaaba.
C) He cannot pray until he moves to see the Kaaba.
D) He must perform ijtihad and face his best guess, regardless of direction.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the obligation to face the exact Kaaba applies only to those who directly see it; all others, including Makkans who cannot see it, are required to face its direction (jiha).

The Meccan's Obligation: Facing the Exact Ka'ba
Explains obligation of Meccan to face exact Ka'ba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Meccan regarding qibla and distinguish between facing the exact Ka'ba (ʿayn) and facing its direction (jiha).

Core Idea
The Meccan must face the exact Ka'ba because he can achieve certainty.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq clarifies a key fiqh distinction: for residents of Mecca, the obligation to face the qibla is stricter than for others. While a non-Meccan need only face the direction of the Ka'ba, a Meccan must arrange his prayer so that he is directly facing the Ka'ba itself, even if he cannot see it. The text explores this ruling and the disagreements among Hanafi scholars about its application when obstacles exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the direction of prayer (qibla) for a Meccan. The ruling is that it is fard to face the exact Ka'ba (ʿayn) because he is capable of certainty.
This is stricter than for a non-Meccan, who only needs to face the general direction (jiha).
2
Examine the scope of 'Meccan'
The text notes that 'Meccan' includes both those who see the Ka'ba and those who do not (e.g., inside a house). The obligation remains the same: to pray such that if walls were removed, he would be directly facing the Ka'ba.
This is based on the general capacity for certainty, not actual sight.
3
Trace the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: the Meccan is capable of knowing the exact location of the Ka'ba with certainty, so it is obligatory to use that knowledge. The text contrasts this with the non-Meccan, who can only rely on probability (ẓann) and thus faces the direction.
The proof is not a direct text from Quran or Sunnah but a logical derivation from the principle of certainty.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Al-Kāfī holds that even a Meccan with obstacles must face the exact ʿayn (so that if walls were removed, he would be facing it). This is deemed weak. Al-Dirāya states that anyone with an obstacle is treated like an absent person, allowed to perform ijtihād (taḥarrī).
The muftā bihī, from al-Tanjīs, distinguishes: one who sees the Ka'ba must face ʿayn; one who does not see it must face jiha.
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
Al-Tanjīs' view is chosen (mukhtār). Fath al-Qādir raises a methodological objection: if one can climb to attain certainty, it is not permissible to rely on conjecture. This strengthens the view that a Meccan with a removable obstacle should seek certainty.
The preferred position is that seeing the Ka'ba triggers the obligation of ʿayn; otherwise, jiha suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فللمكي فرضه إصابة عينها) أي عين القبلة بمعنى الكعبة للقدرة على اليقين أطلق في المكي فشمل من كان بمعاينتها ومن لم يكن حتى لو صلى مكي في بيته ينبغي أن يصلي بحيث لو أزيلت الجدران يقع استقباله على شطر الكعبة بخلاف الآفاقي فإنه لو أزيلت الموانع لا يشترط أن يقع استقباله على عين الكعبة لا محالة. كذا في الكافي وهو ضعيف. قال في الدراية : من كان بينه وبين الكعبة حائل الأصح أنه كالغائب، ولو كان الحائل أصلياً كالجبل كان له أن يجتهد والأولى أن يصعده ليصل إلى اليقين. وفي التنجيس : من كان بمعاينة الكعبة فالشرط إصابة عينها، ومن لم يكن بمعاينتها فالشرط إصابة جهتها وهو المختار وفي فتح القدير : وعندي في جواز التحري مع إمكان صعوده إشكال لأن المصير إلى الدليل الظني وترك القاطع مع إمكانه لا يجوز. وما أقرب قوله الكتاب : والاستخبار فوق التحري فإذا امتنع المصير إلى الظني لإمكان ظني أقوى منه فكيف يترك اليقين مع إمكانه للظن؟
He said: (For the Meccan, his obligation is to face the exact Ka'ba) meaning the exact qibla, i.e., the Ka'ba, because he is capable of certainty. He makes it general for the Meccan, including both the one who sees it and the one who does not, to the extent that if a Meccan prays in his house, he must pray in such a way that if the walls were removed, his facing would be towards the direction of the Ka'ba, unlike the non-Meccan, for if obstacles were removed, it is not necessarily required that his facing be exactly towards the Ka'ba. Thus in al-Kafi, but it is weak. In al-Diraya: Whoever has an obstacle between him and the Ka'ba, the correct view is that he is like the absent person (gha'ib). If the obstacle is original like a mountain, he may perform ijtihad, and it is better to climb it to attain certainty. In al-Tanjees: Whoever sees the Ka'ba, the condition is facing the exact Ka'ba; whoever does not see it, the condition is facing its direction, and that is the chosen view. In Fath al-Qadir: I see an issue in permitting ijtihad when climbing is possible, because resorting to a probabilistic proof while leaving a definitive one when possible is not permissible. And how close is the statement of the book: 'Seeking information is above ijtihad; so if resorting to the probabilistic is prohibited due to the possibility of a stronger probabilistic, how can one leave certainty for conjecture?'
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) discussing the obligation of facing the exact Ka'ba for the Meccan (resident of Mecca). The commentator clarifies that the term 'Meccan' includes both those who can see the Ka'ba directly and those who cannot (e.g., inside a house). For a Meccan, the obligation is to face the exact Ka'ba, meaning that if obstacles were removed, he would be directly facing it. This contrasts with the non-Meccan, for whom facing the direction (jiha) suffices. The commentator cites several sources: al-Kafi (which he deems weak), al-Diraya (which treats anyone with an obstacle as an absent person, allowing ijtihad), and al-Tanjees (which distinguishes between one who sees the Ka'ba and one who does not). Finally, Fath al-Qadir raises a methodological objection: if one can climb to attain certainty, it is not permissible to rely on conjecture (zann). The passage ends with a quote from the main text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) emphasizing that seeking information (istikhbar) is superior to ijtihad, so certainty should not be abandoned for conjecture.

Key Terms
المكي (al-makki): The resident of Mecca, whether or not he can see the Ka'ba.
العين (al-'ayn): The exact Ka'ba itself, as opposed to its direction.
التحري (al-tahari): Ijtihad to determine the qibla direction when uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the muftā bihī position in this passage, what is the condition for a Meccan who can see the Ka'ba?
A) He may perform ijtihad (taḥarrī) if he wishes
B) He must face the exact Ka'ba (ʿayn)
C) He must face the direction (jiha) only
D) He is not required to face the qibla

Key Takeaway
For a Meccan, the obligation is to face the exact Ka'ba (ʿayn) when able; for a non-Meccan or a Meccan who cannot see it, facing the direction (jiha) suffices.

Fard Requires Qat'i Proof: The Case of Ta‘dīl al-Arkān
Argues that fard cannot be established by ahad hadith alone, only by qat'i texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that fard rulings require qat'i texts and apply it to determine whether an act like ta'dil al-arkan is fard or sunna.

Core Idea
Fard cannot be proven by khabar al-wahid; it must be grounded in a qat'i text.

In this passage, al-Qurmani articulates a foundational Hanafi usul principle: obligation (fard) is not established by isolated hadith reports alone; it requires a definitive text (nass qat'i). He applies this principle to a disputed issue in prayer—the status of ta'dil al-arkan (proper alignment of limbs). By aligning with the Quran's commands to bow and prostrate, the basic acts are fard, but the extra refinement of alignment is not. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the methodological rule
Al-Qurmani states that a fard ruling can only be established by a qat'i text (Quran or mutawatir hadith). Khabar al-wahid can support a ruling if it aligns with a qat'i text, but cannot independently make something fard.
2
Apply the rule to the basic prayer acts
The acts of facing qibla, takbir, recitation, bowing, and prostration are fard because they are explicitly commanded in the Quran (e.g., 2:144, 74:3, 73:20, 22:77). These are qat'i texts.
3
Examine the case of ta'dil al-arkan
The command to repeat prayer for leaving ta'dil comes from a khabar al-wahid. This hadith does not align with the absolute Quranic command to 'bow' and 'prostrate' because it adds a condition (proper alignment) beyond the minimum required.
The Quranic commands are general: bowing means bending the back, prostrating means lowering the body.
4
Understand the usul reasoning
Making ta'dil al-arkan fard based on a khabar al-wahid would be an addition (ziyada) to the Quranic command. In Hanafi usul, an addition to a text is considered abrogation (naskh), and a khabar al-wahid cannot abrogate the Quran.
This is a key principle: 'al-ziyada 'ala al-nass naskh.'
5
State the practical implication
Therefore, ta'dil al-arkan is not fard; it is sunna. Leaving it does not invalidate the prayer, but it is recommended to perform it for completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و مقصودهم من إيراد العقل تقوية مضمون النص من الكتاب والسنة بالقياس وإن لم يكن القياس مستقلاً لإثبات الفرض، وخبر الواحد فوق القياس لما عرف في موضعه فبالطريق الأولى أن يصح الاستدلال به على فرضية شيء تقوية للنص القطعي . فإذا تقرر هذا فانظر بعد ذلك فمهما تجده من مفهوم هذا الحديث وقع موافقاً للدليل القطعي فقل بفرضيته، وما لم تجده موافقاً لذلك لا تقل بفرضيته لأن الفرض لا يثبت بخبر الواحد فالأمر باستقبال القبلة والتكبير والقراءة والركوع والسجود وقع موافقاً للنص القطعي وهو قوله تعالى فول وجهك شطر المسجد الحرام وربك فكير كل فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن واركعوا واسجدوا فتكون هذه الأشياء فرضاً والأمر بإعادة الصلاة لترك تعديل الأركان لم يكن موافقاً للنص القطعي بل وقع مخالفاً لإطلاقه فلا يكون تعديل الأركان فرضاً . بيانه أن الله تعالى أمر بالركوع وهو انحناء الظهر وبالسجود وهو الانخفاض لغة فتتعلق الركنية بالأدنى فيهما لأن الأمر بالفعل لا يقتضي الدوام، ويتعلق الكمال بالسنية لئلا يلزم نسخ الكتاب بخبر الواحد إذ الزيادة نسخ على ما عرف في الأصول اهـ كلام القرماني.
And their purpose in presenting reason is to strengthen the content of the text from the Book and Sunnah through analogy, even if analogy is not independent to prove obligation. And the report of a single transmitter (khabar al-wahid) is above analogy, as is known in its place. So by a fortiori reasoning, it is valid to use it as evidence for the obligation of something to strengthen a definitive text. So if this is established, then look: whatever you find from the meaning of this hadith that agrees with a definitive proof, then say it is obligatory; and whatever you do not find agreeing with that, then do not say it is obligatory, because obligation is not established by a khabar al-wahid. So the command to face the qibla, to say takbir, to recite, to bow, and to prostrate agrees with the definitive text, i.e., His words: 'So turn your face toward al-Masjid al-Haram' (2:144), 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3), 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (73:20), 'Bow and prostrate' (22:77). So these things are obligatory. The command to repeat prayer for leaving the adjustment of the pillars (ta'dil al-arkan) does not agree with the definitive text; rather, it contradicts its absoluteness. So adjustment of the pillars is not obligatory. The explanation is that Allah commanded bowing, which is bending the back, and prostration, which is lowering; thus, the integral (rukn) is attached to the minimum in both because the command for an act does not necessitate continuity, and perfection is attached to recommended (sunna) status, lest abrogation of the Book by a khabar al-wahid occur, since addition is abrogation as is known in usul. End of the words of al-Qurmani.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a methodological excursus by al-Qurmani on how to determine whether an act is fard (obligatory). The central argument is that a fard ruling must be supported by a qat'i (definitive) text (Quran or mutawatir hadith). A khabar al-wahid (single-transmitter hadith) cannot establish obligation independently, but it can support a ruling if it aligns with a qat'i text. The author applies this to prayer: the acts of facing qibla, takbir, recitation, bowing, and prostration are fard because they are explicitly commanded in the Quran. However, the command to repeat prayer for omitting ta'dil al-arkan (proper posture) comes from a khabar al-wahid and does not align with the absolute command, so ta'dil al-arkan is not fard but rather sunna. The reasoning is that the verses command bowing and prostrating in a general sense, and the minimum that qualifies is the rukn; anything beyond that is recommended. Making it obligatory would be an addition (ziyada) which amounts to abrogation (naskh) of the Quran by a non-qat'i source, which is impermissible. This is a key Hanafi usul principle.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching the level of tawatur.
النص القطعي (al-nass al-qat'i): A text that is definitive in both transmission and meaning, like the Quran and mutawatir hadith.
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): Proper alignment of the limbs in prayer, such as straightening the back in ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is ta'dil al-arkan not fard?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because the hadith commanding it contradicts a qat'i text by adding a requirement
C) Because it is physically impossible
D) Because it is not a pillar of prayer

Key Takeaway
Ta'dil al-arkan is sunna, not fard, because making it fard would abrogate the Quranic command by a non-qat'i text.

Facing the Qibla Direction (Jiha) for Non-Meccans: Precision and Tolerance
Defines 'jiha' and its tolerance for non-Meccan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of jiha (direction) for the non-Meccan, explain the difference between precise and approximate alignment, and apply the tolerance principle to determine valid facing.

Core Idea
For the non-Meccan, facing the direction suffices, and slight deviation is tolerated based on distance.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of 'jiha' (direction) as it applies to the non-Meccan's obligation to face the qibla. The commentator expands on the base text from Kanz al-Daqaiq, clarifying that the requirement is not to face the exact Ka'ba but its direction, with tolerance increasing with distance. Understanding this definition is crucial for correctly performing prayer away from Mecca.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and commentator's task
Recognize that the base text states 'and for other than him, facing its direction' and the commentator defines what 'direction' means.
The base matn is by al-Nasafi, the commentary by Ibn Nujaym.
2
Define 'jiha' as the side aligned with the Ka'ba or its airspace
The commentator explains that jiha is the side facing which the person is aligned (musamat) with the Ka'ba or its airspace.
Alignment can be precise or approximate.
3
Distinguish between precise (tahqiq) and approximate (taqrib) alignment
Precise: a line from the face at a right angle passes through the Ka'ba or its air. Approximate: slight deviation that does not completely remove facing.
Tolerance is due to distance; what removes facing at close range may not at far.
4
Explain the tolerance principle
The text illustrates with a line example: moving many leagues laterally does not change facing; scholars place countries on the same line (samt).
The key is that facing is not lost; deviation that still leaves part of the face aligned is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولغيره إصابة (جهتها أي لغير المكي فرضه إصابة جهتها وهو الجانب الذي إذا توجه إليه الشخص يكون مسامتاً للكعبة أو لهوائها إما تحقيقاً بمعنى أنه لو فرض خط من تلقاء وجهه على زواية قائمة إلى الأفق يكون ماراً على الكعبة أو هوائها، وإما تقريباً بمعنى أن يكون ذلك منحرفاً عن الكعبة أو هوائها انحرافاً لا تزول به المقابلة بالكلية بأن بقي شيء من مع سطح الوجه مسامتاً لها لأن المقابلة إذا وقعت في مسافة بعيدة لا تزول بما تزول به من الانحراف لو كانت في مسافة قريبة ويتفاوت ذلك بحسب تفاوت البعد وتبقى المسامتة انتقال مناسب لذلك البعد، فلو فرض مثلاً خط تلقاء من وجه المستقبل للكعبة على التحقيق في بعض البلاد وخط آخر يقطعه على زاويتين قائمتين من جانب يمين المستقبل وشماله لا تزول تلك المقابلة بالانتقال إلى اليمين والشمال على ذلك الخط بفراسخ كثيرة، ولهذا وضع العلماء قبله بلد وبلدين وبلاد على سمت واحد
He said: (And for other than him, facing its direction) i.e., for the non-Meccan, his obligation is to face its direction, which is the side that, when a person faces it, he is aligned with the Ka'ba or its air, either precisely meaning that if a line from his face at a right angle to the horizon passes through the Ka'ba or its air, or approximately meaning that it deviates from the Ka'ba or its air by a deviation that does not completely remove the facing, such that some of the surface of the face remains aligned because when the facing occurs at a great distance, it is not lost by the deviation that would lose it at a short distance, and it varies according to the difference in distance, and the alignment remains a suitable transition for that distance. For example, if we suppose a line from the face of the one facing the Ka'ba exactly in some country, and another line cutting it at right angles from the right and left sides, that facing is not lost by moving right or left on that line by many leagues. Therefore, the scholars placed before him one, two, or multiple countries on the same line.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'jiha' (direction) as it applies to the non-Meccan's obligation to face the qibla. The commentator distinguishes between precise alignment (tahqiq) where an imaginary line from the face passes directly through the Ka'ba or its airspace, and approximate alignment (taqrib) where slight deviation is tolerated as long as it does not completely remove the facing. The tolerance increases with distance: what would be a significant deviation at close range is negligible at far distances. The example with lines illustrates that moving laterally by many leagues does not change the alignment. This is why scholars designate entire countries as being on the same 'direction' (samt). This definition is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position that for the non-Meccan, facing the direction suffices, not the exact Ka'ba.

Key Terms
الجهة (al-jiha): The direction of the Ka'ba; the side that aligns with it, either precisely or approximately.
المسامتة (al-musamatat): Alignment; being directly in line with the Ka'ba or its airspace.
السمت (al-samt): The line or direction; multiple places on the same samt share the same qibla direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does a slight deviation from the exact Ka'ba invalidate the prayer for a non-Meccan according to this passage?
A) Yes, any deviation invalidates
B) No, as long as the facing is not completely lost
C) Only if the deviation is intentional
D) It depends on the distance to Mecca

Key Takeaway
The non-Meccan must face the direction of the Ka'ba, not the exact structure, and slight deviation is permitted as long as alignment is not lost, with greater tolerance at greater distances.

Prayer when Ka'ba Is Lifted: Affirming Karamat al-Awliya
A ruling about prayer direction when the Ka'ba is lifted, used to affirm karamat al-awliya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer direction when the Ka'ba is lifted and explain how this ruling affirms karamat al-awliya.

Core Idea
If the Ka'ba is lifted by a saint's miracle, pray facing its former place — this ruling confirms karamat al-awliya.

This passage presents a specific fatwa: if the Ka'ba is miraculously lifted from its place, those on the ground must pray facing the earth where it stood, not the airborne structure. Al-Ramli notes that this ruling, transmitted from al-Utabiyya, is explicit evidence for the reality of karamat al-awliya (miracles of saints), refuting false claims that Abu Hanifa denied them. The text also clarifies that the phrase 'he should pray' (yanbaghi) implies obligation (wujub), not mere recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the ruling
What is the extraordinary scenario presented? What is the legal ruling for those on the ground?
The Ka'ba is lifted from its place; the ruling is to pray facing its original location.
2
Understand the implication for karamat
How does this ruling serve as evidence for karamat al-awliya? Who does it refute?
Al-Ramli states it is 'explicit' (sarih) evidence, refuting those who deny karamat or attribute that denial to Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the linguistic nuance
What does 'yanbaghi' (should) mean in this context? How does it relate to the obligation level?
The commentator clarifies that 'yanbaghi' here is interpreted as wajib (obligatory), not just recommended.
4
Recognize the refutation
Why does this passage refute claims that Abu Hanifa denied karamat? What is the logical connection?
The very existence of a ruling based on a miraculous event presupposes that such events can occur, affirming karamat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الكعبة إذا رفعت عن مكانها الخ قال الرملي وفي التتارخانية نقل هذه المسألة عن العتابية، وهذا صريح في كرامات الأولياء فيرد به على من نسب أمامنا إلى القول بعدمها. قوله : (ينبغي أن يصلي الخ) أي ينبغي أن يصلي وجوباً بحيث، أو التقدير ينبغي أن يقال يجب أن يصلي.
He said: (The Ka'ba, if it is lifted from its place...). Al-Ramli said: In al-Tatarkhaniyya, this issue is transmitted from al-Utabiyya, and this is explicit regarding the miracles of the saints (karamat al-awliya), and it refutes those who attribute to our imam the denial of them. He said: (He should pray...) i.e., he should pray obligatorily such that, or it is estimated that it should be said: he must pray.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This short passage deals with a specific fatwa: if the Ka'ba is miraculously lifted from its place (for the visit of awliya), then those on the ground may pray facing the Ka'ba's former location (the earth). Al-Ramli notes that this ruling, transmitted from al-Utabiyya, is clear evidence for the reality of karamat al-awliya (miracles of saints). It refutes those who falsely claim that Abu Hanifa denied such miracles. The second part comments on the phrase 'he should pray' (yanbaghi an yusalliya), clarifying that it implies obligation (wujub), not mere recommendation. This underscores the importance of facing the qibla even in extraordinary circumstances.

Key Terms
كرامات الأولياء (karamat al-awliya): Miracles performed by God through righteous saints, distinct from the miracles of prophets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That the Ka'ba cannot be moved
B) That karamat al-awliya are real
C) That prayer is invalid without facing the Ka'ba
D) That ijtihad is not allowed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on prayer when the Ka'ba is lifted affirms the reality of saintly miracles (karamat al-awliya) and underscores the obligation to face the original qibla direction.

Practical Methods to Determine Qibla Direction
Lists practical astronomical methods for qibla determination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four solar methods and three stellar methods for determining qibla direction as described in the Hanafi tradition, and apply the region-specific instructions for the Pole Star.

Core Idea
The Pole Star (al-Qutb) is the strongest evidence for Qibla, but its placement varies by region.

Determining the correct direction for prayer is essential for the validity of salah. While mosques have mihrabs, travelers and those in new areas need practical methods. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq offers a range of techniques using the sun and stars, with special attention to the Pole Star and its region-specific application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four solar methods
The passage lists four ways using the sun at specific times: shortest day sunrise, noon, afternoon when shadows double, and sunset. Each method involves aligning the sun with a part of the face or ear.
These methods are likely calibrated for the latitude of Iraq/Persia.
2
Locate the stellar methods
Three stellar methods are given: facing the Scorpion constellation one month before Mihrajan, using the Little Dipper on the right ear with a slight left lean, and the Pole Star method with regional instructions.
The Pole Star is explicitly called the strongest evidence.
3
Understand regional variations for the Pole Star
The Pole Star's placement differs by region: behind the right ear for Kufa/Baghdad etc., on the left shoulder for Egypt, on the right shoulder for Iraq (again?), opposite the left side for Yemen, and behind for Syria.
The text mentions both 'Iraq' and 'Kufa/Baghdad' groups, which may overlap.
4
Recognize the practical scope
These methods are practical for travelers and are based on the author's geographical context. The passage notes there are other opinions, indicating a rich scholarly tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المبتغى : في معرفة الجهة أربعة أوجه أحدها في أقصر يوم من السنة وقت طلوع الشمس فاجعل عين الشمس عند مطلعها على رأس أذنك اليسرى فإنك تدركها. وثانيها فاجعل عين الشمس على مؤخر عينك اليسرى عند الزوال فإنك تصيبها. وثالثها فاجعل الشمس على مقدم عينك اليمنى مما يلي الأنف عند صيرورة ظل كل شيء مثليه بعد زوالها فإنك تدركها ورابعها فاجعل عين الشمس على مؤخر عينك اليمنى عند غروب الشمس فإنك تدركها. ووجه آخر أنه إذا كان قبل المهرجان بشهر فاستقبل العقرب وقت صلاة العشاء الأخيرة فإنك تدركها. وإذا جعلت بنات نعش الصغرى على أذنك اليمنى وانحرفت قليلاً إلى شمالك فإنك تدركها. وذكر بعضهم أن أقوى الأدلة القطب وهو نجم صغير في بنات نعش الصغرى بين الفرقدين والجدي إذا جعله الواقف خلف أذنه اليمنى كان مستقبلاً القبلة إن كان بناحية الكوفة وبغداد و همدان و قزوین و طبرستان وجرجان وما والاها إلى نهر الشاش، ويجعله من بمصر على عاتقة الأيسر، ومن بالعراق على عاتقة الأيمن، فيكون مستقبلاً باب الكعبة، وباليمن قبالة المستقبل مما يلي جانبه الايسر وبالشام وراءه وفي معرفة الجهة أقوال أخرى مذكورة في الخانية وغيرها.
And in al-Mubtagha: There are four ways to know the direction. One: on the shortest day of the year at sunrise, place the sun at its rising on the top of your left ear, and you will face it. Second: place the sun on the back of your left eye at noon, and you will hit it. Third: place the sun on the front of your right eye near the nose when the shadow of everything is twice its length after noon, and you will face it. Fourth: place the sun on the back of your right eye at sunset, and you will face it. Another way: one month before the festival (Mihrajan), face the Scorpion at the time of the last Isha prayer, and you will face it. And if you place the Little Dipper (Banat Na'sh al-Sughra) on your right ear and lean slightly to your left, you will face it. Some mentioned that the strongest evidence is the Pole Star (al-Qutb), which is a small star in the Little Dipper between al-Farqadain and al-Jady. If the person places it behind his right ear, he will face the qibla if he is in the region of Kufa, Baghdad, Hamadan, Qazwin, Tabaristan, Jurjan, and what borders them up to the River al-Shash. For someone in Egypt, he places it on his left shoulder; for someone in Iraq, on his right shoulder, and he will face the door of the Ka'ba. In Yemen, it is opposite the face on its left side; in Syria, behind him. And there are other statements about knowing the direction mentioned in al-Khaniyya and elsewhere.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage provides practical methods for determining the qibla direction, primarily for travelers or those without access to established mihrabs. The first four methods rely on the position of the sun at specific times (shortest day sunrise, noon, afternoon when shadows are double, and sunset). These align the body with the qibla direction for certain regions. Additional methods use stars: the Scorpion constellation a month before the Mihrajan festival, and the Little Dipper (Ursa Minor) with specific positioning relative to the ear. The Pole Star (al-Qutb) is highlighted as the strongest evidence, with specific instructions for different regions: behind the right ear for Iraq and Persia, on the left shoulder for Egypt, on the right shoulder for Iraq, opposite the left side for Yemen, and behind for Syria. These methods are practical knowledge for Muslims who need to pray in unfamiliar places. The passage concludes that there are other opinions mentioned in al-Khaniyya and other works, indicating a rich scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
القطب (al-qutb): The Pole Star (Polaris), used as an astronomical indicator for qibla.
بنات نعش الصغرى (banat na'sh al-sughra): The Little Dipper (Ursa Minor), a constellation used for navigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Pole Star (al-Qutb)
C) The moon phase
D) The compass

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides practical astronomical methods for qibla, with the Pole Star being the strongest evidence, applied regionally.

Intention of the Ka'ba (Niyyah) Not Required in Hanafi
Clarifies that intending the exact Ka'ba is not necessary; facing the direction suffices.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention of the exact Ka'ba in prayer and explain the reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
Intention of the exact Ka'ba is not a condition; facing the qibla direction suffices.

This lesson examines a key point in Hanafi prayer fiqh: whether one must specifically intend (niyyah) to face the Ka'ba itself when praying. The relied-upon position is that such intention is not required; it is sufficient to intend to face the qibla direction. We will explore the reasoning of the majority, the contrary view of al-Jurjani, and the practical advice from al-Bada'i'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the main ruling: intention of exact Ka'ba is not required; facing direction suffices.
The passage states: 'نية استقبال القبلة ليست بشرط'.
2
Identify the opposing view
Al-Jurjani's view that intention is necessary because the far person must face the exact Ka'ba.
Al-Jurjani is a minority within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the basis of the opposing view
Understand the reasoning: since the far person cannot physically face the exact Ka'ba, intention substitutes.
This is based on the premise that the obligation is to face the exact Ka'ba.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The majority reject the premise; the obligation is to face the direction, not the exact building.
They cite that facing direction is achieved without intending the exact Ka'ba.
5
Note the practical advice from al-Bada'i
Al-Bada'i recommends not intending the exact Ka'ba because of potential misalignment.
This precaution ensures the prayer is not invalidated if direction is slightly off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق في الاكتفاء بالجهة فأفاد أنه لا يشترط نية الكعبة، وشرطها الجرجاني بناء على أن الفرض إصابة العين للقريب والبعيد، ولا يمكن إصابة العين للبعيد إلا من حيث النية فانتقل ذلك إليها . وذهب العامة إلى عدم اشتراط إصابة العين فلا يشترط نيتها لعدم الحاجة إلى ذلك فإن إصابة الجهة تحصل من غير نية العين فالحاصل أن نية استقبال القبلة ليست بشرط على الصحيح من المذهب سواء كان الفرض إصابة العين في حق المكي. أو إصابة الجهة في حق غيره كما صححه في التحفة والتنجيس والخلاصة وغيرها حتى قال في البدائع : الأفضل أن لا ينوي الكعبة لاحتمال أن لا تحاذي هذه الجهة الكعبة فلا تجوز
He made absolute in sufficing with the direction, so it indicates that intention of the Ka'ba is not a condition. Al-Jurjani conditioned it based on the view that the obligation is to face the exact Ka'ba for both near and far, and facing the exact Ka'ba for the distant is only possible through intention, so it transfers to it. The general body of scholars held to the non-requirement of facing the exact Ka'ba, so intention of it is not required because there is no need for that, since facing the direction is achieved without intending the exact Ka'ba. The conclusion is that intention of facing the qibla is not a condition in the correct view of the school, whether the obligation is facing the exact Ka'ba for the Meccan or facing the direction for others, as confirmed in al-Tuhfa, al-Tanjees, al-Khulasa, and others. Until he said in al-Bada'i: It is better not to intend the Ka'ba because it is possible that this direction does not exactly align with the Ka'ba, and then the prayer would not be valid.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage settles the issue of whether one must intend (niyyah) to face the Ka'ba itself when praying. The relied-upon (sahih) Hanafi position is that such intention is not required. It suffices to intend to face the qibla direction, whether one is in Mecca or elsewhere. Al-Jurjani had conditioned intention on the view that the far person must face the exact Ka'ba, but the majority hold that facing the direction is sufficient. The passage cites multiple authorities: al-Tuhfa, al-Tanjees, al-Khulasa, and al-Bada'i'. Interestingly, al-Bada'i' suggests that it is actually better not to intend the exact Ka'ba, because if the direction one faces does not actually align with the Ka'ba, then intending the Ka'ba would invalidate the prayer. This is a practical precaution: by intending the direction rather than the exact building, one avoids potential invalidation. This ruling reflects the Hanafi emphasis on ease and avoidance of excessive rigor.

Key Terms
نية استقبال القبلة (niyyat istiqbal al-qibla): The intention to face the qibla in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, is it necessary to intend the exact Ka'ba when praying?
A) Yes, always
B) Only for the Meccan
C) No, it is not a condition
D) Only if one is certain of the direction

Key Takeaway
Intention of the exact Ka'ba is not a condition for prayer in the Hanafi school; facing the correct direction suffices, and it is even better not to intend the exact Ka'ba due to the risk of misalignment.

Determining Qibla Direction: Evidence from Mihrabs to Stars
Practical rulings on determining qibla direction through various signs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of evidence for qibla direction according to the Hanafi school and apply the Pole Star method to determine qibla in different regions.

Core Idea
For qibla, rely first on established mihrabs; when absent, celestial signs like the Pole Star guide.

The qibla is a condition for the validity of salah. The Hanafi school provides a clear hierarchy of how to determine its direction. This lesson examines the methods described in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, from the authoritative mihrabs of the Companions to the use of the sun, stars, and the Pole Star, with region-specific instructions.

Guided Path
1
Identify primary evidence
In cities and villages, the primary evidence is the mihrabs erected by the Companions and Followers. Following them is obligatory ('alayna ittiba'uhum).
This is the strongest evidence; one must rely on it when available.
2
Identify secondary evidence
If no mihrab exists, the next step is to ask the local people (ahl) who know the qibla direction.
Asking locals is a valid method when mihrabs are absent.
3
Identify tertiary evidence for seas and deserts
For seas and deserts, where no mihrab or locals are available, the evidence is the stars. The text then details specific sun and star methods.
The Pole Star (al-Qutb) is considered the strongest celestial indicator.
4
Apply region-specific Pole Star method
The Pole Star method varies by region: for Iraq, place it behind the right ear; for Egypt, on the left shoulder; for Yemen, opposite the left side; for Syria, behind the back.
These instructions are tailored to the geographic location relative to Makkah.
5
Understand the concept of jihah
The goal is to face the direction (jihah) of the Kaaba, not the exact building. This is sufficient for distant locations.
The distinction between 'ayn and jihah is key in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : وجهة الكعبة تعرف بالدليل والدليل في الأمصار والقرى المحاريب التي نصبها الصحابة والتابعون رضي الله عنهم أجمعين، فعلينا اتباعهم في استقبال المحاريب المنصوبة، فإن لم يكن فالسؤال من الأهل. أما البحار والمفاوز فدليل القبلة النجوم إلى آخره . وفي المبتغى : في معرفة الجهة أربعة أوجه أحدها في أقصر يوم من السنة وقت طلوع الشمس فاجعل عين الشمس عند مطلعها على رأس أذنك اليسرى فإنك تدركها. وثانيها فاجعل عين الشمس على مؤخر عينك اليسرى عند الزوال فإنك تصيبها. وثالثها فاجعل الشمس على مقدم عينك اليمنى مما يلي الأنف عند صيرورة ظل كل شيء مثليه بعد زوالها فإنك تدركها ورابعها فاجعل عين الشمس على مؤخر عينك اليمنى عند غروب الشمس فإنك تدركها. ووجه آخر أنه إذا كان قبل المهرجان بشهر فاستقبل العقرب وقت صلاة العشاء الأخيرة فإنك تدركها. وإذا جعلت بنات نعش الصغرى على أذنك اليمنى وانحرفت قليلاً إلى شمالك فإنك تدركها. وذكر بعضهم أن أقوى الأدلة القطب وهو نجم صغير في بنات نعش الصغرى بين الفرقدين والجدي إذا جعله الواقف خلف أذنه اليمنى كان مستقبلاً القبلة إن كان بناحية الكوفة وبغداد و همدان و قزوین و طبرستان وجرجان وما والاها إلى نهر الشاش، ويجعله من بمصر على عاتقة الأيسر، ومن بالعراق على عاتقة الأيمن، فيكون مستقبلاً باب الكعبة، وباليمن قبالة المستقبل مما يلي جانبه الايسر وبالشام وراءه وفي معرفة الجهة أقوال أخرى مذكورة في الخانية وغيرها .
And in Fatawa Qadikhan: The direction of the Kaaba is known by evidence, and the evidence in the cities and villages are the mihrabs erected by the Companions and the Followers (may Allah be pleased with them all). It is upon us to follow them in facing the erected mihrabs. If not, then asking from the locals. As for the seas and deserts, the evidence for the qibla is the stars, etc. And in al-Mubtagha: There are four ways to know the direction. One: on the shortest day of the year at sunrise, place the sun's disk at its rising point on the top of your left ear, you will face it. Two: place the sun's disk on the back of your left eye at noon, you will hit it. Three: place the sun on the front of your right eye near the nose when the shadow of everything is twice its length after noon, you will face it. Four: place the sun's disk on the back of your right eye at sunset, you will face it. Another way: if it is one month before the festival, face Scorpio at the time of the last Isha prayer, you will face it. And if you place the Little Dipper on your right ear and turn slightly toward your north, you will face it. Some mentioned that the strongest evidence is the Pole Star, which is a small star in the Little Dipper between the two Guards and the Kid. If the person standing places it behind his right ear, he will be facing the qibla if he is in the region of Kufa, Baghdad, Hamadan, Qazvin, Tabaristan, Jurjan, and what adjoins them to the River Syr. And he who is in Egypt places it on his left shoulder, and he who is in Iraq places it on his right shoulder, thus facing the door of the Kaaba. In Yemen, it is opposite facing his left side, and in Syria behind him. There are other sayings regarding knowing the direction mentioned in al-Khaniyyah and elsewhere.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains how to determine the qibla direction. It begins by citing Fatawa Qadikhan that the direction is known by evidence (dalil). The primary evidence in populated areas is the mihrabs erected by the Companions and Followers; we must follow them. If no mihrab exists, one should ask the locals. For seas and deserts, the stars serve as evidence. The text then quotes al-Mubtagha listing four methods using the sun at different times of the year: at sunrise on the shortest day, at noon, when shadows double, and at sunset. Additional methods involve Scorpio a month before a festival, the Little Dipper (Ursa Minor), and the Pole Star (al-Qutb). The Pole Star method is region-specific: for those in Iraq and surrounding areas, placing it behind the right ear faces the Kaaba; for Egypt on the left shoulder; for Yemen to the left; for Syria behind. Other sayings exist in al-Khaniyyah. This passage is a practical guide for those who cannot rely on established mihrabs.

Key Terms
الجهة (al-jihah): The direction of the Kaaba, not necessarily the exact building itself
الدليل (al-dalil): The evidence or sign by which qibla is known, including mihrabs and celestial bodies
القطب (al-qutb): The Pole Star, used as a strong indicator for qibla direction

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The stars
B) The mihrabs erected by the Companions and Followers
C) Asking the locals
D) The sun's position

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes the mihrabs of the Companions as the strongest evidence for qibla; celestial methods are reliable subsidiaries.

Is Intention of the Kaaba Required for Qibla?
Resolves intra-Hanafi dispute on niyyah of Kaaba for qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether niyyah of the exact Kaaba is required for qibla, explain the proof via qiyas on wudu, and identify the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is a condition; like wudu, it needs no separate intention.

When you pray, you face the qibla. But do you need to intend in your heart that you are facing the exact Kaaba structure? The Hanafi school has an intra-madhhab dispute on this point. This lesson unpacks the correct view (al-sahih) from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: intention of the exact Kaaba is not required; facing the direction suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed element
Determine what exactly is being contested: is niyyah of the exact Kaaba (al-‘ayn) a condition for the validity of prayer when facing qibla?
The dispute is about whether the obligation is to face the exact building or its direction.
2
State the Hanafi correct view and its proof
State that the correct view in the madhhab is that intention is not required. The proof is qiyas (analogy) on wudu: just as wudu is a condition without needing separate intention, facing qibla is also a condition and does not require niyyah.
The text also notes that the majority (al-‘ammah) hold this view.
3
Contrast with the opposing view within the madhhab
Al-Jurjani and some later Hanafis required intention. Their reasoning: for a distant person, hitting the exact ‘ayn is impossible without intention, so intention becomes necessary. The Hanafi response: the obligation for the far person is to face the direction (jihah), not the exact ‘ayn.
Recognize that this is an intra-Hanafi dispute, not a cross-madhhab one, though the Shafi‘i school also requires intention.
4
Explore the subsidiary rulings (furu‘)
The text discusses several scenarios: intending the building of the Kaaba (invalid unless meaning direction), intending the mihrab (invalid), intending the Station of Ibrahim (valid on the correct view). These illustrate the application of the principle.
These furu‘ are direct applications of the rule that direction suffices.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
The practical difference appears in cases of slight deviation: on the view requiring exact ‘ayn, a slight deviation invalidates prayer; on the direction view, it remains valid.
This shows why the correct view is more lenient and easier to practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق في الاكتفاء بالجهة فأفاد أنه لا يشترط نية الكعبة، وشرطها الجرجاني بناء على أن الفرض إصابة العين للقريب والبعيد، ولا يمكن إصابة العين للبعيد إلا من حيث النية فانتقل ذلك إليها . وذهب العامة إلى عدم اشتراط إصابة العين فلا يشترط نيتها لعدم الحاجة إلى ذلك فإن إصابة الجهة تحصل من غير نية العين فالحاصل أن نية استقبال القبلة ليست بشرط على الصحيح من المذهب سواء كان الفرض إصابة العين في حق المكي. أو إصابة الجهة في حق غيره كما صححه في التحفة والتنجيس والخلاصة وغيرها حتى قال في البدائع : الأفضل أن لا ينوي الكعبة لاحتمال أن لا تحاذي هذه الجهة الكعبة فلا تجوز . وإنما كان هذا الصحيح لأن استقبالها شرط من الشرائط فلا يشترط فيه النية كالوضوء وغيره. وعلى هذا فقولهم لو نوى بناء الكعبة لا يجوز لأن المراد بالكعبة العرصة لا البناء إلا أن يريد بالبناء جهة الكعبة فيجوز. ذكره في المحيط وغيره. وقولهم لو نوى أن قبلته محراب مسجده لا يجوز لأنه علامة وليس بقبلة كما في الخانية. وقولهم لو نوى مقام ابراهيم ولم ينو الكعبة قيل لا يجوز إلا أن ينوي الجهة. وقيل إن لم يكن الرجل أتى مكة أجزأه وإلا لا يجوز، واختاره في الخانية والبدائع والمحيط مبني على الضعيف الشارط للنية . أما على الصحيح فيجوز كما ذكره ابن أمير حاج. وذكر عن بعضهم أن ثمرة الخلاف عند أصحابنا تظهر أيضاً في الانحراف قليلاً؛ فمن قال الفرض التوجه إلى العين لم تصح صلاته، ومن قال الجهة صححها وسيأتي في باب الصلاة في الكعبة أن الصواب أن يقال : القبلة هي العرصة لا الكعبة لأنها البناء.
He considered sufficiency of direction, indicating that intention of the Kaaba is not required. Al-Jurjani required it based on the view that the obligation is hitting the exact 'ayn for the near and far, and hitting the exact 'ayn for the far is only possible through intention, so it transfers to that. And the majority went to not requiring hitting the exact 'ayn, so its intention is not required due to no need for it, because hitting the direction occurs without intending the exact 'ayn. So the result is that intention of facing the qibla is not a condition on the correct view of the madhhab, whether the obligation is hitting the exact 'ayn for the Meccan, or hitting the direction for others, as verified in al-Tuhfa, al-Tanjis, al-Khulasa, etc., until he said in al-Bada'i: 'It is better not to intend the Kaaba, because it is possible that this direction does not align with the Kaaba, so it would not be permissible.' And this is correct because facing it is a condition among conditions, so intention is not required in it, like wudu and others. Based on this, their statement that if one intended the building of the Kaaba it is not permissible because what is meant by Kaaba is the courtyard, not the building, unless by building he means the direction of the Kaaba, then it is permissible. This is mentioned in al-Muhit and elsewhere. And their statement that if one intended that his qibla is the mihrab of his mosque, it is not permissible because it is a sign, not a qibla, as in al-Khaniyyah. And their statement that if one intended the Station of Ibrahim without intending the Kaaba, it is said it is not permissible unless he intends the direction. And it is said that if the man has not come to Mecca, it suffices him, otherwise not. This was chosen in al-Khaniyyah, al-Bada'i, and al-Muhit, based on the weak view that requires intention. As for the correct view, it is permissible, as mentioned by Ibn Amir Haj. And it is mentioned from some that the fruit of the difference among our scholars appears also in slight deviation: whoever says the obligation is facing the exact 'ayn, his prayer is not valid; whoever says the direction, validates it. And it will come in the chapter of prayer in the Kaaba that the correct statement is: the qibla is the courtyard, not the Kaaba, because it is the building.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses an important intra-Hanafi dispute: whether one must intend the exact Kaaba (al-‘ayn) when facing the qibla. The author begins by stating that the text (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) considered direction (jihah) sufficient, implying intention is not required. Al-Jurjani, however, required intention based on the view that the obligation is 'hitting the 'ayn' for both near and far, and for the far, intention substitutes. The majority (al-‘ammah) disagreed, holding that hitting the 'ayn is not required; thus intention is unnecessary. The correct view (al-sahih) in the madhhab is that intention of the qibla is not a condition. The proof is qiyas: just as wudu and other conditions do not require separate intention, facing the qibla is a condition and does not require niyyah. The text then discusses several subsidiary rulings: if one intends the building of the Kaaba (the structure), it is not valid because 'Kaaba' in this context means the courtyard (al-‘arsah); if one intends the mihrab of his mosque, it is not valid as it is a sign, not the qibla; if one intends the Station of Ibrahim, there are two views: on the weak view requiring intention, it is not valid unless he intends the direction; on the correct view, it is valid. The practical difference (thamarah) appears in cases of slight deviation: those who require hitting the exact 'ayn would invalidate the prayer, while those who accept direction would validate it. The passage concludes by noting that the correct definition of qibla is the courtyard, not the building.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): Intention in the heart to face the Kaaba specifically
العرصة (al-arsah): The courtyard or the entire area of the Kaaba, not the building itself
الجهة (al-jihah): The direction of the Kaaba, not the exact spot

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the Hanafi madhhab, which of the following best describes the ruling on intending the exact Kaaba when facing qibla?
A) It is required
B) It is recommended
C) It is neither required nor recommended; facing the direction suffices
D) It is invalid

Key Takeaway
Intention of the exact Kaaba is not a condition for facing qibla in the Hanafi madhhab; facing the direction suffices, and this is supported by qiyas on wudu.

Deviation from Qibla: Face vs Chest — The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute regarding chest vs face turning from qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between turning the face and turning the chest away from qibla, and state the Hanafi relied-upon position that turning the chest invalidates prayer without excuse.

Core Idea
Turning the face from qibla does not invalidate prayer; turning the chest does.

In this passage, Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates a key intra-Hanafi dispute: does turning the chest away from qibla invalidate prayer? Abu Hanifa held that as long as one remains in the mosque without intention to reject, it does not invalidate. His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, disagreed. The later madhhab adopted the disciples' view as the operative ruling. We will trace this dispute, its proofs, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the contested element
The act is deviation (inhiraf) from qibla during prayer. The contested element is whether turning the chest (tahwil al-sadr) invalidates prayer, while turning the face is agreed not to invalidate.
The passage cites al-Tanjis: 'If he turns his face, his prayer is not invalidated, but it is invalidated by his chest.'
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa: turning the chest does not invalidate if done without rejection intent and while still in the mosque. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn): turning the chest invalidates regardless.
The text says 'according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is not invalidated in either case... contrary to the two.'
3
Examine the basis of Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa considers istidbar (turning away) without intent of rejection as not removing the condition of facing qibla, as long as one remains in the physical mosque space.
The mosque is a place of devotion; turning away without rejection is excused.
4
Examine the basis of the Sahibayn's view
They consider turning the chest as a clear departure from the qibla direction, which is a fard condition. Location (mosque) does not excuse it.
The text adopts the Sahibayn's view as the madhhab.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its rationale
The later madhhab adopted the Sahibayn's view, stating 'al-madhhab anna idha hawala sadrahu fasidat' (the madhhab is that if he turns his chest, it is invalidated). This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Most books follow this; excuse is permitted for genuine reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى : الانحراف المفسد أن يجازو المشارق إلى المغارب. وفي التنجيس : وإذا حول وجهه لا تفسد صلاته وتفسد بصدره قيل هذا أليق بقولهما أما عنده فلا تفسد في الوجهين بناء على أن الاستدبار إذا لم يكن على قصد الرفض لا تفسد ما دام في المسجد عنده خلافاً لهما، حتى لو انصرف عن القبلة على ظن الإتمام فتبين عدمه بنى ما دام في المسجد عنده خلافاً لهما اهـ . وفي فتح القدير : ولقائل أن يفرق بينهما بعذره هناك وتمرده هنا. والحاصل أن المذهب أنه إذا حول صدره فسدت وإن كان في المسجد إذا كان من غير عذر كما عليه عامة الكتب. وفي الظهيرية ومن صلى إلى غير جهة الكعبة متعمداً لا يكفر هو الصحيح لأن ترك جهة الكعبة جائز في الجملة بخلاف الصلاة بغير طهارة لعدم الجواز بغير طهارة بحال، واختاره الصدر الشهيد والحاصل أن حكم الفرض لزوم الكفر يجحده لا (وذكر عن بعضهم الخ) هو ابن هبيرة في الإفصاح كما في الحلية. قوله : (وفي الفتاوى الانحراف المفسد أن يجاوز المشارق إلى المغارب. كذا نقله في فتح القدير وهو مشكل فإن مقتضاه أن الانحراف إذا لم يوصله إلى هذا القدر لا يفسد وعبارة التنجيس التي نقلها المؤلف بعده أعم من ذلك فإنه جعل المفسد انحراف الصدر فيصدق بما دون ذلك أي بأن ينحرف بصدره بحيث لا يصل إلى استقبال المشرق أو المغرب. ويؤيده ما في منية المصلي عن أمالي الفتاوى ونصه وذكر في أمالي الفتاوى حد القبلة في بلادنا يعني سمرقند ما بين المغربين مغرب الشتاء ومغرب الصيف، فإن صلى إلى جهة خرجت من المغربين فسدت صلاته .اهـ قال شارحها ابن أمير حاج وذكر هذه العبارة في الملتقط مع زيادة وهي». وقال أبو منصور : ينظر إلى أقصر يوم في الشتاء وإلى أطول يوم في الصيف فيعرف مغربيهما، ثم يترك الثلثين عن يمينه والثلث عن يساره ويصلي فيما بين ذلك، وهذا استحباب والأوّل للجواز اهـ ومشى على الأوّل الرستغفني وجعل في مجموع النوازل ما ذكره أبو منصور هو المختار اهـ. قوله : ( وفي فتح القدير ولقائل أن يفرق الخ) قال في شرح المنية الكبير قال البحر الرائق ج ١ م ٣٢
And in al-Fatawa: The corrupting deviation is that which goes beyond the east to the west. And in al-Tanjis: If he turns his face, his prayer is not invalidated, but it is invalidated by his chest. It is said this is more appropriate to the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), but according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is not invalidated in either case, based on the fact that turning away when not with the intent of rejection does not invalidate as long as he is in the mosque, contrary to the two. Even if he turned away from the qibla thinking he had completed, then it became clear he had not, he may continue as long as he is in the mosque, according to him, contrary to the two. End quote. And in Fath al-Qadir: One might distinguish between them by his excuse there and his rebellion here. The conclusion is that the madhhab is that if he turns his chest, it is invalidated even if he is in the mosque if there is no excuse, as is the case in most books. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Whoever prays facing a direction other than the Kaaba deliberately does not become a disbeliever; this is the correct view, because leaving the direction of the Kaaba is permissible in general, unlike prayer without purification, which is not permissible under any circumstances. This was chosen by al-Sadr al-Shahid. And the conclusion is that the ruling of the obligation is that denial of it necessitates disbelief. (And it is mentioned from some...) He is Ibn Hubayrah in al-Ifsah, as in al-Hilyah. His statement: (And in al-Fatawa: the corrupting deviation is that which goes beyond the east to the west) Thus it was transmitted in Fath al-Qadir, but it is problematic, because its implication is that deviation if it does not reach this extent does not invalidate, while the wording of al-Tanjis quoted by the author after it is more general than that, for he made the corrupting factor the turning of the chest, which applies to less than that, i.e., that he turns his chest so that he does not reach facing east or west. This is supported by what is in Munyat al-Musalli from Amali al-Fatawa, its text: 'And it is mentioned in Amali al-Fatawa: The limit of the qibla in our land, meaning Samarkand, is between the two settings: the winter setting and the summer setting. If he prays facing a direction that leaves the two settings, his prayer is invalidated.' End quote. Its commentator Ibn Amir Haj said: 'This wording is mentioned in al-Multaqat with an addition: And Abu Mansur said: One should look at the shortest day in winter and the longest day in summer to know their settings, then leave two-thirds on his right and one-third on his left, and pray within that. This is recommended, and the first is for permissibility.' End quote. Al-Rustaghfani followed the first, and in Majmu' al-Nawazil what Abu Mansur mentioned is the chosen view. End quote. His statement: (And in Fath al-Qadir: One might distinguish...) said in Sharh al-Munyat al-Kabir: said al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, volume 1, page 32.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses when deviation from the qibla invalidates prayer. It begins by citing al-Fatawa that corrupting deviation is turning past the east to the west (i.e., reversing direction entirely). Then from al-Tanjis, we learn that turning the face alone does not invalidate, but turning the chest does. There is a difference within the Hanafi school: according to Abu Hanifa, turning the chest does not invalidate as long as one remains in the mosque and does not intend rejection; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), it does invalidate. However, the relied-upon position (al-madhhab) is that turning the chest invalidates when done without excuse. The passage also addresses a separate issue: deliberately praying to a direction other than the Kaaba does not make one a disbeliever, because turning from the qibla is permissible in some contexts (e.g., when lost or unaware), unlike abandoning purity, which is never permissible. The commentator then discusses the text from Fath al-Qadir noting a conflict between al-Fatawa's definition (exceeding the east-west line) and al-Tanjis's (turning the chest). He reconciles by citing Amali al-Fatawa, which defines the qibla limit in Samarkand as between the winter and summer settings. A further recommendation from Abu Mansur is to leave two-thirds to the right and one-third to the left within that range. The passage concludes with references to later authorities.

Key Terms
الانحراف (al-inhiraf): Turning away from the direction of qibla during prayer
الاستدبار (al-istidbar): Facing completely away from qibla, i.e., with one's back to qibla

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi madhhab (mufta bihi), which action invalidates the prayer if done without excuse?
A) Turning the face away from qibla
B) Turning the chest away from qibla
C) Both turning the face and chest
D) Only facing completely opposite (east to west)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi madhhab, turning the chest away from qibla without excuse invalidates the prayer, while turning the face alone does not.
