Qibla is the Area, Not the Building; Intention Not Required
Expands the correct view that qibla is area, not building, and intention not required.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi position that the qibla is the area of the Kaaba (al-arsa) rather than the building itself, and explain that intention (niyya) is not a condition for facing it.

Core Idea
The qibla is the area of the Kaaba, not its structure; intention for the exact building is not required.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a fundamental point about the qibla. The correct Hanafi position is that the qibla is defined as the entire area (al-arsa) surrounding the Kaaba, not the stone building itself. Consequently, when a person faces the general direction of the Kaaba, his prayer is valid even if he does not explicitly intend the exact building. The author supports this with an analogy to other conditions of prayer, like wudu, which do not require intention. The passage also addresses specific scenarios and refutes a weaker opinion that demands intention of the exact entity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that the qibla is the area (al-arsa) and intention is not required for facing it.
This is the correct (sahih) view according to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the proof by analogy
The author compares facing qibla to other conditions (shurut) like wudu: conditions do not require intention. Therefore, facing qibla does not require intention.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
3
Apply the ruling to given examples
Analyze the examples provided: intending the building of the Kaaba is valid if meant as direction; intending the mihrab is invalid; intending Maqam Ibrahim is valid on the correct view.
These illustrate the principle in practice.
4
Recognize the weaker opinion
Note that there is a weak view (daif) that requires intention of the exact qibla, but it is rejected in favor of the sound view.
The weaker view is not relied upon for fatwa.
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
On the correct view, slight deviation from the exact Kaaba building does not invalidate the prayer; the area suffices.
This is an important practical relief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو صلاته. وإنما كان هذا الصحيح لأن استقبالها شرط من الشرائط فلا يشترط فيه النية كالوضوء وغيره. وعلى هذا فقولهم لو نوى بناء الكعبة لا يجوز لأن المراد بالكعبة العرصة لا البناء إلا أن يريد بالبناء جهة الكعبة فيجوز. ذكره في المحيط وغيره. وقولهم لو نوى أن قبلته محراب مسجده لا يجوز لأنه علامة وليس بقبلة كما في الخانية. وقولهم لو نوى مقام ابراهيم ولم ينو الكعبة قيل لا يجوز إلا أن ينوي الجهة. وقيل إن لم يكن الرجل أتى مكة أجزأه وإلا لا يجوز، واختاره في الخانية والبدائع والمحيط مبني على الضعيف الشارط للنية . أما على الصحيح فيجوز كما ذكره ابن أمير حاج. وذكر عن بعضهم أن ثمرة الخلاف عند أصحابنا تظهر أيضاً في الانحراف قليلاً؛ فمن قال الفرض التوجه إلى العين لم تصح صلاته، ومن قال الجهة صححها وسيأتي في باب الصلاة في الكعبة أن الصواب أن يقال : القبلة هي العرصة لا الكعبة لأنها البناء.
He is the one who prays. And this correct (view) is because facing it is one of the conditions, so intention is not required in it, like wudu and others. Based on this, their saying: 'If he intends the building of the Kaaba, it is not valid' because what is meant by Kaaba is the area, not the building, unless he intends by 'building' the direction of the Kaaba, then it is valid. It is mentioned in al-Muhit and others. And their saying: 'If he intends that his qibla is the niche of his mosque, it is not valid' because it is a sign and not a qibla, as in al-Khaniyya. And their saying: 'If he intends the Station of Ibrahim and does not intend the Kaaba,' it is said it is not valid unless he intends the direction. And it is said: if the man has not come to Mecca, it suffices him, otherwise it is not valid. And this is chosen in al-Khaniyya, al-Bada'i, and al-Muhit, based on the weak view that requires intention. But on the correct view, it is valid, as mentioned by Ibn Amir Haj. And it is reported from some of them that the fruit of the disagreement among our companions also appears in slight deviation: whoever says the obligation is facing the exact entity, his prayer is not valid, and whoever says the direction, his prayer is valid. And it will come in the chapter of prayer in the Kaaba that the correct is to say: the qibla is the area, not the Kaaba, because it is the building.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the correct view regarding the qibla. The author explains that facing the qibla is a condition (shart) of prayer, and like other conditions such as wudu, it does not require intention (niyya). Therefore, if one faces the general area of the Kaaba (al-'arsa) without intending the exact building, his prayer is valid. The text then clarifies various examples: If one intends the building of the Kaaba but the intention is for the area, it is valid; if one intends the mihrab (prayer niche) of his local mosque, that is invalid because it is only a marker; and regarding Maqam Ibrahim, if one intends it without the Kaaba, there is a difference of opinion: the weak view requires intention of the direction, but the sound view (al-sahih) is that it is valid without specific intention. The passage concludes by stating that the correct position is that the qibla is the area (al-'arsa) of the Kaaba, not the structure itself, and this has practical consequences for slight deviation from the exact building.

Key Terms
العرصة (al-arsa): The area or courtyard surrounding the Kaaba, as distinct from the actual structure (al-bina').
النية (al-niyya): Intentional purpose; here it refers to the specific intention of facing the exact Kaaba building.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Invalid because the mihrab is only a sign and not a qibla.
C) Valid only if he also intends the Kaaba.
D) Invalid only if he is far from Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi view is that the qibla is the area of the Kaaba (al-arsa), and intention of the exact building is not required.

Deviation from Qibla: Invalidating and Kufr Rulings
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidation and kufr due to qibla deviation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on when turning from qibla invalidates prayer, and state the condition under which intentional deviation from qibla leads to kufr.

Core Idea
Turning the chest invalidates prayer; intentional deviation alone does not cause kufr without contempt.

This lesson examines two connected issues: what constitutes invalidating deviation from qibla, and whether deliberately facing a wrong direction makes one a disbeliever. You will learn the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and the critical role of intention and contempt (istihana) in determining kufr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage addresses two distinct rulings: (1) when deviation from qibla invalidates the prayer, and (2) whether intentional deviation leads to kufr. Separate these before analyzing the dispute.
These rulings have different conditions and consequences.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position on invalidation
According to Abu Hanifa, turning the chest from qibla invalidates the prayer, even if the face remains towards qibla. This applies even if the person remains in the mosque, unless there is an excuse.
The chest is the primary indicator of direction (jiha).
3
State the Sahibayn's position on invalidation
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that only turning the face invalidates; turning the chest alone does not, unless accompanied by intent to reject the prayer.
They consider the face more significant for direction.
4
Identify the mufta bihi on invalidation
The relied-upon position (madhhab) is that of Abu Hanifa: turning the chest invalidates the prayer. This is stated in most authoritative books (e.g., Fath al-Qadir).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Analyze the ruling on kufr
Intentional deviation from qibla alone does not cause kufr. Kufr occurs only if the deviation is accompanied by istihana (contempt or mockery). The passage contrasts this with prayer without wudu, which is never permissible and thus denial leads to kufr.
The key differentiator is the presence or absence of istihana.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الفتاوى : الانحراف المفسد أن يجازو المشارق إلى المغارب. وفي التنجيس : وإذا حول وجهه لا تفسد صلاته وتفسد بصدره قيل هذا أليق بقولهما أما عنده فلا تفسد في الوجهين بناء على أن الاستدبار إذا لم يكن على قصد الرفض لا تفسد ما دام في المسجد عنده خلافاً لهما، حتى لو انصرف عن القبلة على ظن الإتمام فتبين عدمه بنى ما دام في المسجد عنده خلافاً لهما اهـ . وفي فتح القدير : ولقائل أن يفرق بينهما بعذره هناك وتمرده هنا. والحاصل أن المذهب أنه إذا حول صدره فسدت وإن كان في المسجد إذا كان من غير عذر كما عليه عامة الكتب. وفي الظهيرية ومن صلى إلى غير جهة الكعبة متعمداً لا يكفر هو الصحيح لأن ترك جهة الكعبة جائز في الجملة بخلاف الصلاة بغير طهارة لعدم الجواز بغير طهارة بحال، واختاره الصدر الشهيد والحاصل أن حكم الفرض لزوم الكفر يجحده لا بتركه. وإنما قال أبو حنيفة بالكفر في هذه المسائل بمجرد الترك عمداً للزوم الاستهزاء به والاستخفاف وهو يقتضي أنه لا فرق في المسائل إذ لا أثر لعدم الجواز في شيء من الأحوال، بل الموجب للإكفار هو الاستهانة وهو ثابت في الكل وإلا فهو منتف في الكل. وألحق في فتح القدير الصلاة في الثوب النجس كالصلاة بغير طهارة وهو مشكل، فإن بعض أئمة المالكية يقول بأن إزالتها سنة لا فرض ولا يكفر بجحد المختلف فيه، فكيف بتركه من غير جحد كما أشار إليه قاضيخان في فتاواه وحكى في الذخيرة الاختلاف فيما إذا صلى بغير طهارة ثم قال : ولو ابتلي انسان بذلك لضرورة بأن كان مع قوم فأحدث واستحيا أن يظهر فكتم ذلك وصلى هكذا أو كان بقرب العدوّ فقام يصلي وهو غير طاهر قال بعض مشايخنا : لا يكون كافراً لأنه غير مستهزىء. ومن ابتلى بذلك لضرورة أو الحياء ينبغي أ أن لا يقصد بالقيام قيام الصلاة ولا يقرأ شيئاً، وإذا حتى ظهره لا يقصد الركوع ولا يصير كافراً بالإجماع .
In al-Fatawa: The invalidating deviation is that one goes beyond the east to the west. And in al-Tanqih: If he turns his face, his prayer is not invalid, but it is invalidated by his chest. It is said this is more in line with their (Sahibayn) view, but according to him (Abu Hanifa), it does not invalidate on either count based on the principle that if the turning away is not with the intent of rejection, it does not invalidate as long as he is in the mosque, contrary to them. So much so that if he turns away from the qibla assuming completion, then it becomes clear that he has not completed, he builds (continues) as long as he is in the mosque according to him, contrary to them. And in Fath al-Qadir: One can say that there is a difference between them due to his excuse there and his defiance here. The summary is that according to the madhhab, if he turns his chest, it invalidates even if he is in the mosque, if it is without excuse, as in most books. And in al-Zahiriyya: Whoever prays to other than the direction of the Kaaba intentionally does not become a disbeliever; this is the correct view, because abandoning the direction of the Kaaba is permissible in general, unlike prayer without wudu, because there is no permissibility at all without wudu. And this was chosen by al-Sadr al-Shahid. The summary is that the ruling of the precept—that kufr necessarily follows its denial—does not... by omitting it. And Abu Hanifa only declares kufr in these matters due to mere intentional omission, because it implies mockery and contempt. But this implies there is no difference among the matters since the absence of permissibility has no effect in any situation; rather, the cause for declaring kufr is disdain (al-istihana), which is established in all, otherwise it is absent in all. And Fath al-Qadir annexed prayer in a najis garment to prayer without wudu, which is problematic, because some Maliki imams say removing it is sunna, not fard, and one does not become a disbeliever by denying what is disputed, so how about omitting it without denial, as Qadi Khan indicated in his Fatawa. And al-Dhakhira narrated the difference regarding prayer without wudu, then said: If a person is afflicted with that due to necessity, such as being with a group and he becomes impure and is too shy to show it, so he conceals it and prays like that, or he is near an enemy and stands to pray while not pure, some of our scholars said: he does not become a disbeliever because he is not mocking. And one who is afflicted due to necessity or shyness should not intend the standing of prayer and should not recite anything, and even if he bends his back he should not intend bowing, and he does not become a disbeliever by consensus.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage addresses two main issues: (1) What constitutes invalidating deviation from qibla, and (2) whether intentionally praying to a wrong direction leads to kufr. On the first, the author presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to the relied-upon view (al-madhhab), turning the chest from qibla invalidates the prayer even if one remains in the mosque, unless there is an excuse. This is stricter than the view of the Sahibayn, who make a distinction between turning the face and the chest. On the second issue, the passage clarifies that intentionally praying to a wrong direction does not by itself make one a disbeliever, because abandoning the qibla direction is permissible in some circumstances (e.g., travel). This contrasts with prayer without wudu, which is never permissible, so denying its obligation leads to kufr. However, Abu Hanifa holds that if one intentionally omits a fard out of contempt, it may cause kufr. The discussion extends to comparing with prayer in najis clothes, and concludes with exceptions for those under duress or shyness, where kufr is not declared.

Key Terms
الانحراف المفسد (al-inhiraf al-mufsid): Deviation from qibla that invalidates prayer; defined as turning the chest from qibla.
الاستهانة (al-istihana): Contempt or mockery towards religious obligations; the criterion for kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon madhhab position regarding turning the chest from qibla without excuse?
A) The prayer is not invalidated because the face may still be towards qibla.
B) The prayer is invalidated because the chest is the primary indicator of direction.
C) The prayer is invalidated only if the person intended to reject the prayer.
D) The prayer remains valid if he is in the mosque.

Key Takeaway
Turning the chest from qibla invalidates prayer; kufr requires istihana (contempt), not mere intentional deviation.

The Excused Person May Pray Without Facing Qibla
Ruling on the excused person's prayer direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which an excused person may omit facing the qibla and distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on being turned by another.

Core Idea
Facing qibla is a condition that drops when genuinely unable, even if another could turn you.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the excused person (khaif) who cannot face the qibla due to fear, illness, or other genuine obstacles. The key principle is that facing the Kaaba is a test, not an end in itself; when the test becomes impossible, the condition lifts. We also explore a nuanced intra-Hanafi difference regarding whether the ability to be turned by another person counts as ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the ruling: The excused person may pray to any direction he is able to face. Understand that this applies when he cannot face qibla due to fear, illness, or any valid excuse.
The ruling is absolute; the text explicitly includes fear from enemy, thief, or danger to mount.
2
Understand the rationale
The passage explains that facing qibla is an additional condition (shart za'id) that falls away when one is incapable. Worship is for Allah, who is beyond direction; the command to face the Kaaba is a test (ibtilā'). When the test is impossible due to a valid excuse, the condition drops.
The rationale is derived rationally (dalil 'aqli): the Kaaba itself is not worshipped, so the obligation to face it is situational.
3
Analyze the scope of 'excuse'
The author extends the ruling to cover any valid excuse, including: fear from enemy or thief, illness where turning causes harm or is impossible, being on a ship where turning risks drowning, being in deep mud preventing prostration, or being on an unruly animal.
The term 'khaif' (one who fears) is interpreted broadly to include all excused persons.
4
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute
Identify the point of disagreement: According to Abu Hanifa, if someone else can turn the person toward qibla, the person is still considered able (qadir) and must face it. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if the person cannot turn himself without harm, the excuse applies even if someone else could turn him. The text suggests the relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn.
This mirrors the rule in tayammum: one who has power through another is not considered able.
5
Apply the rules of ima' (gesture)
If the excused person cannot perform full ruku' and sujud, they may gesture (ima') with head or body. The text provides specific scenarios: on an animal while stationary or moving, or on ground where prostration is impossible. Gesturing must make sujud lower than ruku'.
Ima' is a substitute; the person must still face qibla if possible without harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والخائف يصلي إلى أي جهة قدر لأن استقبال القبلة شرط زائد يسقط عند العجز والفقه فيه أن المصلي في خدمة الله تعالى ولا بد من الإقبال عليه والله سبحانه منزه عن الجهة فابتلاه بالتوجه إلى الكعبة لأن العبادة ليست لها ولهذا لو سجد للكعبة نفسها كفر فلما اعتراه الخوف تحقق العذر فأشبه حالة الاشتباه في تحقق العذر فيتوجه إلى أي جهة قدر لأن الكعبة لم تعتبر لعينها بل للابتلاء وهو حاصل بذلك . أطلقه فشمل الخوف من عدوّ أو لص، وسواء خاف على نفسه أو على دابته. وأراد بالخائف من له عذر فيشمل المريض إذا كان لا يقدر على التوجه وليس عنده من يحوله إليها أو كان التحويل يضره . والتقييد بعدم وجود من يحوله جرى على قولهما، أما عنده فالقادر بقدرة غيره ليس بقادر كما عرف في التيمم، ويشمل ما إذا كان على لوح في السفينة يخاف الغرق إذا انحرف إليها، وما إذا كان في طين وردغة لا يجد على الأرض مكاناً يابساً أو كانت الدابة جموحاً لو نزل لا سبع الفقير وهذا هو الصواب قوله : (وما إذا كان في طين وردغة (الخ الردغة بالتحريك وكذا بالتسكين : الماء والطين والوحل الشديد كما في الصحاح. وفي شرح الشيخ اسمعيل: لو كان في طين لا يقدر على النزول عن الدابة جاز له الإيماء على الدابة واقفة إن قدر وإلا فسائرة متوجهة إلى القبلة إن قدر وإلا فلا. وإن قدر على النزول ولم يقدر على الركوع والسجود نزل وأوماً قائماً، وإن قدر على القعود دون السجود أومأ قاعداً ولو كانت الأرض ندية مبتلة بحيث لا يغيب وجهه في الطين صلى على الأرض وسجد كما في التبيين. وفي صورة عدم القدرة على النزول يجعلون السجود أخفض من الركوع مستقبلين القبلة لأنه لا ضرر في الاستقبال ههنا فلزمهم الاستقبال. قال في
His statement: And the one who fears prays to whichever direction he is able, because facing the qibla is an additional condition that drops when there is incapacity. The fiqh of it is that the worshipper is in the service of Allah Almighty, and it is necessary to turn towards Him, and Allah is transcendent above direction, so He tested him by facing the Kaaba, because worship is not for it; therefore if he were to prostrate to the Kaaba itself, he would disbelieve. So when fear comes over him, the excuse is realized, so it resembles the state of confusion in realizing the excuse. So he faces whichever direction he is able, because the Kaaba is not considered for its own sake but for the test, and that is achieved by that. He (the author) gave it absolutely, so it includes fear from an enemy or a thief, and whether he fears for himself or his mount. And by 'one who fears' he means one who has an excuse, so it includes the sick person if he cannot face it and there is no one to turn him towards it, or if turning harms him. And the restriction of not having someone to turn him follows the view of them (Sahibayn); as for him (Abu Hanifa), one who has power through another is not considered able, as known in tayammum. And it includes the case of being on a plank in a ship fearing drowning if he turns towards it, and the case of being in mud and slime (tin wa radgha) where he cannot find a dry place on the ground, or the mount is unruly such that if he dismounts, he cannot... and this is the correct. His statement: And the case of being in mud and slime, the word radgha with fatha and also with sukun: water, mud, and severe slime as in al-Sihah. And in Sharh al-Shaykh Isma'il: If he is in mud and cannot dismount from the mount, it is permissible for him to gesture (ima') on the mount while it is standing if he can, otherwise while moving, facing the qibla if he can, otherwise no. And if he can dismount but cannot bow and prostrate, he dismounts and gestures while standing; if he can sit but cannot prostrate, he gestures while sitting. And if the ground is moist and wet such that his face does not sink into the mud, he prays on the ground and prostrates as in al-Tabyin. And in the case of inability to dismount, they make the prostration lower than the bowing while facing the qibla, because there is no harm in facing here, so facing is necessary. He said in...

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for one who is excused from facing the qibla due to fear or difficulty. The key principle is that facing the qibla is a condition that falls away when one is genuinely unable. The author explains the rationale: worship is directed to Allah, who is beyond direction, so the command to face the Kaaba is a test; when one is unable due to a valid excuse, the condition drops. The excuse includes fear of an enemy or thief, illness where turning is harmful, being on a ship where turning may cause drowning, or being in mud where one cannot prostrate properly. The text also discusses the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the ability to be turned by someone else: according to Abu Hanifa, if one can be turned by another person, he is still considered able and must face qibla; the Sahibayn disagree. Practical details are provided for gestures (ima') when one cannot perform full bowing and prostration, including cases of being on an animal or in mud.

Key Terms
الخائف (al-kha'if): One who fears for his life, property, or mount due to enemy, animal, or other threat; includes any excused person.
الإيماء (al-ima'): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) when unable to perform them physically.
شرط زائد (shart za'id): An additional condition that is not a pillar; it falls away when there is genuine incapacity.

Key Takeaway
The excused person may pray to any direction he is able, and facing qibla is a condition that drops upon genuine incapacity, with the mufta bihi position following the Sahibayn that personal inability is sufficient excuse even if another could help.

Abandoning Prayer and Disbelief: The Role of Mockery
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the criterion for kufr in abandoning salah/purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa distinguishes between mere abandonment of prayer and abandonment accompanied by mockery, and apply this distinction to scenarios involving necessity or shyness.

Core Idea
Mere abandonment of prayer is a major sin, not kufr; only mockery (istihānah) or denial (jahd) causes disbelief.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a critical nuance in Hanafi creed: not every act of abandoning a fard leads to kufr. Abu Hanifa's position hinges on the presence of istihānah (disdain) or istikhfāf (mockery). We will unpack his reasoning and see how later scholars applied it to cases of necessity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa rules that mere intentional abandonment of prayer without denial (juhud) does not make one a disbeliever. The key is that mockery (istihānah) is absent.
This is the zahir riwayah position from the six core books.
2
Identify the effective cause (illah)
The author explains that the factor necessitating kufr is istihānah (contempt/disdain). If the act does not imply contempt, kufr does not occur.
This is a talil (reasoning) approach, identifying the illah for takfir.
3
Analyze the expansion from Fath al-Qadir
Fath al-Qadir equates praying in a najis garment to praying without purity, suggesting both could cause kufr. The author finds this problematic because the illah of mockery is not necessarily present in the case of najis garment.
Intra-Hanafi dispute: some later scholars extended the ruling, but the author rejects the extension.
4
Consider the exception for necessity or shyness
The text cites Qadi Khan: if one prays without purity due to necessity or shyness, they do not become a disbeliever because they are not mocking. This is a key practical application.
The person should not intend the actions as actual prayer, thus avoiding the imputation of kufr by consensus.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a Muslim who abandons prayer without mockery does not become a disbeliever, though it is a grave sin. This is supported by Qadi Khan and others.
Authority weight: nawadir (later fatwa collections) but widely accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بتركه. وإنما قال أبو حنيفة بالكفر في هذه المسائل بمجرد الترك عمداً للزوم الاستهزاء به والاستخفاف وهو يقتضي أنه لا فرق في المسائل إذ لا أثر لعدم الجواز في شيء من الأحوال، بل الموجب للإكفار هو الاستهانة وهو ثابت في الكل وإلا فهو منتف في الكل. وألحق في فتح القدير الصلاة في الثوب النجس كالصلاة بغير طهارة وهو مشكل، فإن بعض أئمة المالكية يقول بأن إزالتها سنة لا فرض ولا يكفر بجحد المختلف فيه، فكيف بتركه من غير جحد كما أشار إليه قاضيخان في فتاواه وحكى في الذخيرة الاختلاف فيما إذا صلى بغير طهارة ثم قال : ولو ابتلي انسان بذلك لضرورة بأن كان مع قوم فأحدث واستحيا أن يظهر فكتم ذلك وصلى هكذا أو كان بقرب العدوّ فقام يصلي وهو غير طاهر قال بعض مشايخنا : لا يكون كافراً لأنه غير مستهزىء. ومن ابتلى بذلك لضرورة أو الحياء ينبغي أ أن لا يقصد بالقيام قيام الصلاة ولا يقرأ شيئاً، وإذا حتى ظهره لا يقصد الركوع ولا يصير كافراً بالإجماع .
By abandoning it. And Abu Hanifa said that disbelief occurs in these issues by mere intentional abandonment due to the implication of mockery and disdain, and this requires that there is no difference between the issues since the effect of non-permissibility has no role in any of the situations. Rather, the factor that necessitates disbelief is disdain, and it is established in all of them; otherwise it is absent in all. And in Fath al-Qadir, he annexed prayer in a najis garment to prayer without purity, which is problematic. For some Maliki imams say that removing it is sunnah, not fard, and one does not become a disbeliever by rejecting something disputed, so how about abandoning it without rejection, as Qadi Khan indicated in his Fatawa. And in al-Dhakhira, he reported the difference of opinion regarding one who prayed without purity. Then he said: If a person is tested by that out of necessity, such as being with a group and he had an event (hadath) and felt shy to show it, so he concealed it and prayed like that, or he was near the enemy and stood to pray while not in a state of purity, some of our shaykhs said: He does not become a disbeliever because he is not a mocker. And one who is tested by that out of necessity or shyness should not intend by his standing the standing of prayer, and should not recite anything, and when he bends his back he should not intend bowing, and he does not become a disbeliever by consensus.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling about disbelief and abandoning prayer or its conditions. The author discusses Abu Hanifa's position that merely intentionally abandoning prayer or praying without purity does not necessarily make one a disbeliever. The key factor is whether the act involves mockery (istihzā') and disdain (istikhfāf). If one abandons these acts out of necessity or shyness, without intending to mock, then according to the Hanafi school, such a person does not become a disbeliever. The text also references a Maliki view that removing filth is sunnah, not fard, and therefore rejecting it does not cause disbelief. The author concludes that if someone is in a dire situation, they should not intend the movements as actual prayer, and thus escape disbelief by consensus.

Key Terms
الاستهانة (al-istihānah): Disdain or contempt towards the commands of Allah; the underlying cause of kufr in this context.
الجحد (al-jahd): Denial of an obligation known by necessity; explicit rejection of a ruling.
المستهزىء (al-mustahzi'): One who mocks or makes light of religious duties; such person becomes a disbeliever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Whether the person was in a state of purity

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, abandoning a fard act only leads to kufr if accompanied by mockery or denial; necessity and shyness are mitigating factors.

Facing the Qibla in Fear: When the Condition Drops
Explains the ruling that the fearful person may pray facing any direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla for a fearful person and explain the rationale including the intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla is a condition that drops when genuinely unable; the test (ibtilā') is the essence, not the Ka'bah itself.

This lesson unpacks the ruling that a fearful person may pray without facing the qibla. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the underlying fiqh insight: worship is directed to Allah, not to the Ka'bah. When fear prevents one from fulfilling the test of facing the Ka'bah, the condition drops. We will explore the conditions, the intra-Hanafi differences, and practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the prayer of a fearful person. The ruling: valid without facing the qibla, facing any direction possible.
2
Understand the legal insight (fiqh)
The text explains that the Ka'bah is a test, not an object of worship. Facing it is a condition that drops under inability.
3
Note the conditions for dropping
The person must have a genuine excuse: fear of enemy, thief, drowning, harm, illness, etc. Also inability to turn by oneself or with help (with dispute).
4
Compare Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa: ability via another is not true ability; Sahibayn: it is ability. The text presents the dispute.
5
Apply to scenarios
Various cases: on a mount in mud, on a ship, etc. The ruling varies based on whether the mount is standing or moving, ability to dismount, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

العبادة ليست لها ولهذا لو سجد للكعبة نفسها كفر فلما اعتراه الخوف تحقق العذر فأشبه حالة الاشتباه في تحقق العذر فيتوجه إلى أي جهة قدر لأن الكعبة لم تعتبر لعينها بل للابتلاء وهو حاصل بذلك . أطلقه فشمل السجود أومأ ،قاعداً ولو كانت الأرض ندية مبتلة بحيث لا يغيب وجهه في الطين صلى على الأرض وسجد كما في التبيين. وفي صورة عدم القدرة على النزول يجعلون السجود أخفض من الركوع مستقبلين القبلة لأنه لا ضرر في لم تجزئهم إذا قدروا أن يوقفوها. كذا في الكرخي وكذا في التنبيه . قال في الفتح ولو كان على الدابة يخاف النزول للطين والردغة يستقبل قال في الظهيرية وعندي هذا إذا كانت واقفة فإن كانت سائرة يصلي حيث شاء . His saying: (And the fearful person prays toward any direction he can, because facing the qibla is an additional condition that drops when unable. The fiqh insight thereof is that the one praying is in the service of Allah Almighty and must turn towards Him, and Allah is exalted above direction. So He tested him by facing the Ka'bah, because worship is not for it [the Ka'bah] itself; thus if one prostrated to the Ka'bah itself, he would disbelieve. When fear overcomes him, the excuse is realized, resembling the case of confusion (ishtibah) in the realization of the excuse. So he turns to any direction he can, because the Ka'bah is not considered for its own essence but for the test, and that is achieved by it. He (the author) made it absolute, so it includes fear of an enemy or a thief, and whether he fears for himself or his mount. And he intended by 'the fearful' one who has an excuse, so it includes the sick person when he is unable to turn and there is no one to turn him towards it, or if turning would harm him. And the restriction of not having someone to turn him is according to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view; as for him (Abu Hanifa), one who is able through the ability of another is not considered able, as known in tayammum. And it includes the case of being on a plank in a ship where he fears drowning if he turns towards it, and the case of being in mud and mire where he finds no dry place on the ground, or the mount is unruly such that if he dismounts, he cannot [manage]. This is the correct view. His saying: (And when he is in mud and mire...) — al-radghah with tashkil and sukūn means water, mud, and severe mire, as in al-Sihah. And in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il: If he is in mud and cannot dismount from the mount, then it is permissible for him to gesture (ima') while on the mount if it is standing; if not, then while it is moving, facing the qibla if possible; otherwise not. If he can dismount but cannot bow and prostrate, he dismounts and gestures while standing. If he can sit but not prostrate, he gestures while sitting. And if the ground is moist and wet such that his face would not sink into the mud, he prays on the ground and prostrates, as in al-Tabyin. In the case of inability to dismount, they make the prostration lower than the bowing, facing the qibla, because there is no harm in facing the qibla here, so facing it is obligatory for them. He said in al-Fatawa: If they are in mud or mire, they pray facing the qibla when their mounts are standing. Others said: They pray facing the qibla even if their mounts are moving. Muhammad said: If they hold the reins and the mounts are walking, it does not suffice them if they are able to stop them. Likewise in al-Karkhi and al-Tanbih. He said in al-Fath: Even if he is on a mount and fears dismounting due to mud and mire, he faces the qibla. He said in al-Zahiriyyah: According to me, this applies when the mount is standing; if it is moving, he prays wherever he wishes. And someone may distinguish between the case where if he stops it for prayer he fears being left behind by the group or not; in the second case, it is not permissible unless he stops it, as from Abu Yusuf regarding tayammum: if he is such that if he goes to water the caravan would leave and he would be cut off, it is permissible; otherwise he goes to water, and they deemed it good. End. I say: Al-Tabyin referred to this with his words 'if they are able', and al-Siraj with his words 'because there is no harm', and the author referred to it with his words 'lastly, if it is not possible for him', and it should be restricted further to the case where he is unable to dismount from the mount, as we have learned from what we earlier presented from Shaykh Isma'il.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding the prayer of a fearful person (al-kha'if). It opens by explaining that facing the qibla is a condition (shart) that drops when one is genuinely unable to fulfill it. The underlying wisdom (fiqh) is that the worshipper is turning to Allah, who is beyond direction; the Ka'bah is merely a test of obedience. When fear prevents one from facing it, the condition is lifted, and the person may pray in any direction. The text then elaborates on various scenarios: fear from an enemy or beast, fear for oneself or one's property, illness, being on a ship, or being in mud. It discusses the differences between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding whether ability through another counts as ability. For example, if someone can be turned by another person, Abu Hanifa says he is still unable, while the two disciples disagree. The commentary also covers the rulings for praying on a mount in mud: whether to gesture, face the qibla, etc. It cites multiple authorities including Shaykh Isma'il, al-Fatawa, al-Karkhi, al-Tanbih, al-Fath, and al-Zahiriyyah. The commentator (Ibn al-Humam? Actually al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) adds a summary stating that the author (al-Kanz) indicated the condition of inability, and that this should be restricted to when one cannot dismount at all.

Key Terms
الخائف (al-khā'if): One who has a valid excuse (fear) preventing him from facing the qibla; includes fear of enemy, beast, drowning, or harm.
الابتلاء (al-ibtilā'): The test or trial by which Allah commands facing the Ka'bah; the essential purpose behind the command.
الإيماء (al-īmā'): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate bowing and prostration when physically unable to perform the full movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, why is a fearful person allowed to pray without facing the qibla?
A) Because the qibla is not important at all
B) Because the qibla is only a test of obedience, and when unable to fulfill it, the condition drops
C) Because fear automatically invalidates the prayer
D) Because the person can pray in any direction without restriction

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla is a condition that drops when one is genuinely unable; the Ka'bah is a test, not an end in itself.

Dropping of Qiblah for the Elderly or Sick Rider
Ruling on facing qiblah for one who cannot ride without assistance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which facing the qiblah is dropped in Hanafi fiqh and apply the analogy (qiyas) from the dropping of pillars.

Core Idea
Obedience is according to ability: if a person cannot face the qiblah due to genuine incapacity, the requirement drops.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the principle that obligations are scaled to capacity. The text addresses a very old or sick person who cannot ride without assistance. By analogy with the dropping of physical pillars, the requirement to face the qiblah is also waived. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Focus on the person described: one who can only ride with an assistant (bi-mu‘īn) or is a very old man (shaykh kabīr) who cannot ride without help and cannot find anyone to assist.
This is the triggering condition for the concession.
2
Note the existing ruling for pillars
The text establishes that such a person may pray on a mount even for obligatory prayers, and the essential pillars (e.g., standing) are dropped (tasquṭ al-arkān). This is the podstaw (asl) for the analogy.
The dropping of pillars is already a well-known concession.
3
Apply the qiyas (analogy) to facing qiblah
The commentator extends the same logic: just as the pillars are dropped due to inability, so too facing the qiblah (tawajjuh ilā al-qiblah) is dropped when the person cannot manage it. The effective cause (illah) is genuine incapacity (‘adam al-qudra).
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (evident analogy).
4
Consequence: no recompense
The text explicitly states there is no recompense (lā i‘āda) when the person later becomes able. The prayer performed without facing qiblah is valid and need not be repeated.
This contrasts with cases where a wajib is omitted due to forgetfulness requiring sajdah al-sahw.
5
Formulate the general principle
The passage concludes: 'al-ṭā‘atu bi-ḥasabi al-ṭāqah' – obedience is according to capacity. This is a core Hanafi maxim governing dispensations (rukhaṣ).
Memorize this maxim; it applies in many areas of fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لا يمكنه أن يركب إلا بمعين ولا يجده، فكما تجوز له الصلاة على الدابة ولو كانت فرضاً وتسقط عنه الأركان كذلك يسقط عنه التوجه إلى القبلة إذا لم يمكنه ولا إعادة عليه إذا ،قدر، فالحاصل أن الطاعة الطاقة .بحسب
He can ride except with an assistant or he is a very old man who cannot ride except with an assistant and does not find one. So just as prayer on the mount is permissible for him even if it is obligatory, and the pillars are dropped, similarly facing the qiblah is dropped for him if he cannot, and there is no recompense upon him when he is able. So the conclusion is that obedience is according to ability.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about a person who is either too old or too sick to ride without help. The commentator expands on the principle that obligations are measured by capacity. The author states that such a person may pray on a mount even for obligatory prayers, and the essential pillars (such as standing) are waived. By analogy, if he cannot face the qiblah due to his condition, that requirement is also dropped. If he later recovers ability, he does not need to repeat those prayers. This is a clear application of the Hanafi maxim 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).

Key Terms
الركوب إلا بمعين (al-rukūb illā bi-mu‘īn): Riding only with an assistant – the person cannot mount or ride alone.
تسقط عنه الأركان (tasquṭ ‘anh al-arkān): The essential pillars of prayer (e.g., standing) are dropped due to excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he is on a long journey and fears missing the caravan.
B) When he is an old man who cannot ride except with an assistant and cannot find one.
C) When he is in a desert and does not know the qiblah direction.
D) When he is in a mosque and cannot find someone to ask.

Key Takeaway
When genuine incapacity prevents facing the qiblah, the obligation is lifted, and no recompense is required.

Basic Ruling of Taharri When Qiblah Is Ambiguous
Ruling on performing taharri when qiblah direction is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make taharri wajib and identify when a superior method (istikhbar or natural signs) precludes taharri.

Core Idea
Taharri is only permissible when no superior method of determining the qiblah is available.

This lesson examines the basic ruling of taharri—exerting maximum effort to find the qiblah direction. The Hanafi school teaches that taharri is not the first resort; one must first ask a knowledgeable person (istikhbar) or use obvious natural signs like the sun. When such superior means are available, taharri is not allowed. We will analyze the proof from the Quran and the practice of the Companions, and explore an intra-Hanafi dispute about the availability of stars.

Guided Path
1
Define taharri and its condition of obligation
First, understand the meaning of taharri and when it becomes wajib. The passage states that taharri is required only when one is unable to determine the qiblah by any other means.
The condition is 'inability to recognize except by it'.
2
Identify the two superior methods: istikhbar and natural signs
Next, recognize that asking a knowledgeable person (istikhbar) is superior to taharri because it is binding on all, not just the individual. Also, using obvious natural signs like the sun and moon is superior to taharri.
If the sky is clear, the sun is a common sign that must be used.
3
Analyze the primary evidence
The passage cites Quran 2:115 and the practice of the Companions as proof for taharri. Understand the wajh al-dalalah (the legal implication) that this verse permits prayer in any direction when the qiblah is unknown.
The verse's generality is restricted to cases of ambiguity.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
When the sky is clear but the person does not know astronomy, there is a dispute. Al-Marghinani permits taharri, while others forbid it because ignorance of common signs is not excused. Understand the arguments on both sides.
The text preponderates the stricter view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
Based on the author's conclusion, the relied-upon view is that taharri is not allowed when the sky is clear, even if the person is ignorant of astronomy. The proper course is to use the sun or ask.
Taharri is only for when landmarks are obliterated, darkness, or clouds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة (تحرى أي إذا عجز عن تعرف القبلة بغير التحري لزمه التحري وهو بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود لأن الصحابة تحروا وصلوا. وقيل في قوله تعالى فأينما تولوا فثم وجه الله ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۱٥] أي قبلته أنها نزلت في الصلاة حالة الاشتباه. قيدنا بالعجز عن التعرف إلا به لأنه لو قدر على تعرف القبلة بالسؤال من أهل ذلك الموضع ممن هو عالم بالقبلة فلا يجوز له التحري لأن الاستخبار فوقه لكون الخبر ملزماً له ولغيره، والتحري ملزم له دون غيره فلا يصار إلى الأدنى مع إمكان الأعلى بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن من أهله فإنه لا يقلده لأن حاله كحاله، فإن لم يخبره المستخبر حين سأله فصلى بالتحري ثم أخبره يعيد ولو كان مخطئاً. وبناء هذا ما ذكر في التنجيس : تحرى فأخطأ فدخل في الصلاة وهو لا يعلم ثم علم وحول وجهه إلى القبلة فدخل رجل في صلاته وقد علم حالته الأولى لا تجوز صلاة الداخل لعلمه أن الإمام كان على الخطأ في أوّل الصلاة اهـ. وكذا إذا كان في المفازة والسماء مصحية وله علم بالاستدلال بالنجوم على القبلة لا يجوز له التحري لأن ذلك فوقه. وفي الظهيرية : رجل صلى بالتحري إلى جهة في المفازة والسماء مصحية لكنه لا يعرف النجوم فتبين أنه أخطأ القبلة هل يجوز ؟ قال رضي الله عنه قال أستاذنا ظهير الدين المرغيناني : يجوز وقال غيره : لا يجوز لأنه لا عذر لأحد في الجهل بالأدلة الظاهرة المعتادة نحو الشمس والقمر وغير ذلك، أما دقائق علم الهيئة وصور النجوم الثوابت فهو معذور في الجهل بها اهـ. فالحاصل أن محل التحري أن يعجز عن الاستقبال بانطماس الأعلام وتراكم الظلام وتضام الغمام كما ذكره المصنف في كافيه، وهو يرجح ما في الظهيرية من أن السماء إذا كانت مصحية لا يجوز التحري ولا يعذر بالجهل.
He said: (And for whom the qiblah is ambiguous, he performs taharri), meaning that if he is unable to recognize the qiblah except by taharri, taharri is incumbent upon him. Taharri is exerting maximum effort to reach the intended goal because the Companions performed taharri and prayed. It is said regarding His saying 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' [Al-Baqarah 2:115] that it was revealed concerning prayer in the case of ambiguity. We restricted it with 'inability to recognize except by it' because if he can recognize the qiblah by asking the people of that place who are knowledgeable of the qiblah, then taharri is not permissible for him, because inquiry (istikhbar) is superior to it, since news is binding on him and others, while taharri is binding only on him and not others, so one should not resort to the lower when the higher is possible. This differs from when he is not from its people, because he does not follow him, as his state is like his state. If the person asked does not inform him when he asked, and he prayed by taharri then he was informed, he repeats even if he was mistaken. The basis of this is what was mentioned in the book on impurities: He performed taharri and erred and entered prayer not knowing, then he knew and turned his face to the qiblah, then a person entered his prayer having known his initial state — the prayer of the entrant is not valid because he knew that the imam was in error at the beginning of the prayer. Likewise, if he is in a desert and the sky is clear and he has knowledge of deducing the qiblah from the stars, taharri is not permissible for him because that is superior to him. In al-Zahiriyyah: A man prayed by taharri in a certain direction in a desert, the sky clear, but he does not know the stars, and then it became clear that he was wrong about the qiblah — is it valid? He said — Radiyallahu 'anh — our teacher Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani said: It is valid. Others said: It is not valid, because there is no excuse for ignorance of obvious common indicators like the sun and moon etc. As for the subtleties of astronomy and the figures of fixed stars, he is excused in ignorance of them. So the conclusion is that the place of taharri is when one is unable to face the qiblah due to obliteration of landmarks, accumulation of darkness, and compression of clouds, as the author mentioned in his Kafi. This gives preponderance to what is in al-Zahiriyyah that when the sky is clear, taharri is not allowed and ignorance is not excused.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling of taharri when the qiblah direction is unknown. The commentator explains that if a person cannot determine the qiblah except through effort (taharri), then taharri becomes obligatory. The proof includes the practice of the Companions and the Qur'anic verse 2:115, which is interpreted as referring to prayer when direction is unclear. The key condition is that the person must be unable to find out by asking a knowledgeable person. If someone capable of giving reliable information is available, inquiry (istikhbar) takes precedence because it is binding on all, whereas taharri is only binding on the individual. If the person asked does not answer, then taharri is permissible, but if he later learns the correct direction, he must repeat the prayer even if he was mistaken. The passage also discusses the use of stars: if the sky is clear and the person knows astronomy, he must use that knowledge, not taharri. However, if he is ignorant of stars but the sky is clear, there is a difference: al-Marghinani allows taharri, others disallow it, saying common signs like the sun are accessible. The commentator favors the view that taharri is permissible only when landmarks are obliterated, it is dark, or clouds block the sky. If the sky is clear, taharri is not allowed and ignorance is not an excuse. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Exerting maximum effort to determine the qiblah direction when it is unknown.
الاستخبار (al-istikhbār): Asking a knowledgeable person about the qiblah; a superior method to taharri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is taharri NOT permissible?
A) When the sky is overcast and landmarks are obliterated.
B) When a knowledgeable person is available to ask about the qiblah.
C) When the person is in a desert and does not know the stars.
D) When the person is in a mosque and no one is there.

Key Takeaway
Taharri is a last resort; if any reliable method of determining the qiblah is available, it must be used.

Taharri Inside a Mosque and the Authority of Mihrabs
Intra-Hanafi dispute on taharri in a mosque and mihrab authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on taharri in a mosque and identify the preponderant view based on the text, and explain why the Madinah mihrab is treated as definitive.

Core Idea
Taharri in a mosque is valid when no one is present to ask, but the Madinah mihrab is definitive by revelation.

Imagine you enter a mosque at night, cannot see the qibla, and there is nobody to ask. Can you estimate the direction (taharri) and pray? Hanafi scholars disagreed. This passage presents the dispute and also clarifies that while most mihrabs are built by ijtihad, the Madinah mihrab was set by the Prophet ﷺ through revelation, so it is binding unlike others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The text addresses whether taharri is permissible inside a mosque when no one is available to inform the qibla.
The general rule is that taharri is not permissible with mihrabs, but this passage discusses an exceptional situation.
2
Extract the two Hanafi positions
The majority (al-Usul) permits taharri, analogizing to a desert. The Balkh school (Abu Ja'far) forbids it, analogizing to seeking help from neighbors in worldly matters.
Note the different qiyas applications.
3
Analyze the authority of mihrabs
The mihrab of Madinah is definitive (qat'i) because the Prophet set it by revelation. Other mihrabs, even in Mina, are based on taharri.
This affects the ruling for residents of Madinah: they must hit the exact qibla direction.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The preponderant view allows taharri when unable to ask. Regarding repetition after error in Makkah/Madinah, Imam Muhammad's view of no repetition is preferred over al-Razi's obligatory repetition.
Referenced from Qadikhan and al-Zahiriyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الشارح أنه لا يجوز التحري مع المحاريب. وفي الظهيرية : رجل اشتبهت عليه القبلة في المسجد ولم يكن أحد يعرفه القبلة قال في الأصول : يجوز له التحري لأنه عجز عمن يسأله فصار كالمفازة. وقال أئمة بلخ منهم الفقيه أبو جعفر : لا تجوز له الصلاة بالتحري وعلل فقال : إن هذه نائبة العقبي فتعتبر بنائبة الدنيا ولو حدثت به نائبة الدنيا فإنه يستغيث بجيران المسجد كذلك ههنا يجب أن يستغيث بهم. وإن كان في مسجد نفسه قال بعضهم هو كالبيت لا يجوز له التحري. وقال بعضهم : مسجده ومسجد غيره سواء. وروى أبو جعفر عن سلام بن حكيم أنه قال : محاريب خراسان كلها منصوبة إلى الحجر الأسود والحجر الأسود إلى ميسرة الكعبة ومن توجه إلى الكعبة ومال بوجهه إلى ميسرة الكعبة وقع وجهه إلى جبل أبي قبيس، ومن مال بوجهه إلى يمينها وقع وجهه إلى الكعبة، ولهذا قيل يجب أن يميل إلى يمينها . قال : ومحاريب الدنيا كلها نصبت بالتحري حتى منى ولم يزد عليه شيئاً، وهذا خلاف ما نقل عن أبي بكر الرازي في محراب المدينة أنه مقطوع به فإنه إنما نصبه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالوحي بخلاف سائر البقاع حتى قيل أن محراب منى نصب بالتحري والعلامات وهو أقرب المواضع إلى مكة .اهـ. وبهذا تبين أن قولهم «لغير المكي أصابة جهتها ليس على إطلاقه بل في غير المدني فإن المدني كالمكي يفترض عليه إصابة عينها صرح به في السراج الوهاج أيضاً. وأطلق في الاشتباه فشمل ما إذا كان بمكة أو بالمدينة بأن كان محبوساً ولم يكن بحضرته من يسأله فصلى بالتحري ثم تبين أنه أخطأ، روي عن محمد أنه لا إعادة عليه، وكان الرازي يقول : تلزمه الإعادة لأنه تيقن بالخطأ إذا كان بمكة أو بالمدينة والأول أحسن كذا في الظهيرية وفي فتاوى قاضيخان رجل صلى في المسجد في ليلة مظلمة بالتحري فتبين أنه صلى إلى غير القبلة جازت صلاته لأنه ليس له أن يقرع أبواب
And the commentator mentioned that taharri is not permissible with the presence of mihrabs. In al-Zahiriyyah: A man for whom the qiblah was ambiguous in a mosque and there was no one to tell him the qiblah. He said in al-Usul: Taharri is permissible for him because he is unable to find someone to ask, so he becomes like [someone in] a desert. The fuqaha of Balkh, among them al-Faqih Abu Ja'far, said: His prayer by taharri is not permissible, and he gave the reason: This is a matter of the afterlife, so it is considered by analogy to a worldly matter. If a worldly matter occurred to him, he would seek help from the mosque neighbors; likewise, here he should seek help from them. If he is in his own mosque, some said it is like a house, taharri is not permissible. Some said: His mosque and another mosque are the same. Abu Ja'far narrated from Salam ibn Hakim that he said: The mihrabs of Khurasan are all constructed facing the Black Stone, and the Black Stone is towards the left side of the Ka'bah. Whoever turns to the Ka'bah and leans his face to the left side of the Ka'bah, his face will fall on Mount Abu Qubais; whoever leans his face to its right, his face will fall on the Ka'bah. For this reason it is said that one should lean to its right. He said: The mihrabs of the whole world were constructed by taharri, even Mina, and nothing more was added to it. This contradicts what was narrated from Abu Bakr al-Razi regarding the mihrab of Madinah that it is definitive because the Prophet set it up by revelation, unlike other places, to the extent that it was said that the mihrab of Mina was set up by taharri and signs, and it is the closest place to Mecca. So by this it is clear that their saying 'for a non-Makkan, his direction is correct' is not absolute; rather, for a non-Madani, the Madani is like the Makkan — he is required to hit the exact direction, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And he spoke generally about ambiguity, so it includes whether one is in Makkah or Madinah, such as when he is imprisoned and there is no one near him to ask, and he prays by taharri then it becomes clear that he was wrong. It is narrated from Muhammad that there is no repetition, and al-Razi used to say: Repetition is incumbent upon him because he is certain of error when in Makkah or Madinah — and the first is better. Likewise in al-Zahiriyyah and in the Fatawa of Qadikhan: A man prayed in a mosque on a dark night by taharri, and it became clear that he prayed in a direction other than the qiblah — his prayer is valid because he cannot knock on doors.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage addresses taharri inside a mosque. The commentator states the general rule that taharri is not permissible when mihrabs exist (since the mihrab indicates the direction). However, in a mosque where no one is present to ask, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. According to al-Usul, taharri is allowed because the person is like someone in a desert. But the fuqaha of Balkh (Abu Ja'far) forbid it, analogizing to worldly matters: one would ask neighbors, so here one should seek help from mosque neighbors. The discussion extends to the mihrabs themselves: the mihrab of Madinah is said to be set by revelation (waḥy), so it is definitive; other mihrabs were set by taharri. Therefore, for a resident of Madinah, it is obligatory to hit the exact qiblah (like a Makkan), whereas for others, following the mihrab suffices. If someone in Makkah or Madinah is imprisoned and cannot ask, and prays by taharri, then later finds error, Imam Muhammad says no repetition; al-Razi says repetition is required. The correct view is the first. Qadikhan's fatwa confirms: if one prays by taharri in a dark mosque and finds error later, the prayer is valid because he could not knock on doors to ask.

Key Terms
المحراب (al-miḥrāb): The niche in a mosque indicating the qiblah direction; its authority is based on revelation (Madinah) or taharri (elsewhere).
نائبة العقبي (nā’ibat al-‘uqbī): A matter of the afterlife (here: determining qiblah for prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling for a person who prays by taharri in a mosque on a dark night and later finds he prayed in the wrong direction?
A) His prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) His prayer is valid because he could not knock on doors to ask.
C) He must repeat if he was in Makkah or Madinah.
D) He must ask the neighbors before praying.

Key Takeaway
When no knowledgeable person is present in a mosque, taharri is valid per the preponderant Hanafi view, and the Madinah mihrab is uniquely definitive by revelation.

Facing Qiblah When Praying on a Mount in Mud: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer on mount in mud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the different Hanafi positions on facing qiblah when praying on a mount in mud and apply the mufta bihi ruling based on fear of separation from the caravan.

Core Idea
Facing qiblah on a mount in mud is required unless stopping risks losing the caravan.

In the Hanafi school, the obligation to face the qiblah is generally strict, but necessity can relax it. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents multiple Hanafi opinions on whether a rider in mud must face Makkah or may pray in any direction. The dispute turns on the ability to stop the mount and the fear of separation from the caravan. Understanding this nuance helps you apply the rule correctly in real travel scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario is a person praying on a mount (e.g., a horse or camel) while in mud or dirt (radgha). The key variable is whether the mount is stationary or moving, and whether the rider can dismount.
Mud is considered a legitimate hardship (mashaqqa) that may excuse normal requirements.
2
List the different Hanafi positions
Several opinions appear: (1) Some say face qiblah if mount is standing; (2) Others say face qiblah even if moving; (3) Muhammad says if moving and can stop, must stop; (4) Al-Zahiriyyah differentiates: if moving, pray any direction; (5) Abu Yusuf analogizes to tayammum: fear of losing caravan permits the relaxation.
The positions are reported in Fatawa, al-Karkhi, al-Tanbih, al-Fath, etc.
3
Analyze the key condition: fear of separation
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) and Abu Yusuf highlight that the decisive factor is whether stopping the mount for prayer would cause the rider to be separated from the caravan (inqita' 'an al-rifqa). If yes, one may pray without facing qiblah; if not, one must stop and face it.
This condition is analogized to the ruling on tayammum when one would miss the caravan by fetching water.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that stopping the mount to face qiblah is required unless one fears being cut off from the caravan. This is supported by the later Hanafi masters and considered the most sound.
The author indicates that this is the position adopted in the later works.
5
Apply to a concrete example
Consider a traveler on a muddy road during a journey. His mount is moving slowly. If he stops to pray facing Makkah, the caravan will move ahead and he may lose them. According to the mufta bihi, he may pray in the direction the mount is facing, without turning toward the qiblah.
If there is no fear of separation, he must stop and face Makkah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا الفتاوى : إذا كانوا في طين أو ردغة صلوا إلى القبلة إذا كانت دوابهم واقفة. وقال غيره : يصلون إلى القبلة ولو كانت دوابهم سائرة. وقال محمد: إذا زموا والدواب تسير لم تجزئهم إذا قدروا أن يوقفوها. كذا في الكرخي وكذا في التنبيه . قال في الفتح ولو كان على الدابة يخاف النزول للطين والردغة يستقبل قال في الظهيرية وعندي هذا إذا كانت واقفة فإن كانت سائرة يصلي حيث شاء . ولقائل أن يفصل بين كونه لو أوقفها للصلاة خاف الانقطاع عن الرفقة أو لا يخاف فلا يجوز في الثاني إلا أن يوقفها كما عن أبي يوسف في التيمم إن كان بحيث لو مضى إلى الماء تذهب القافلة وينقطع جاز وإلا ذهب إلى الماء واستحسنوها .اهـ. أقول: وقد أشار إلى هذا في التبيين بقوله «إن قدروا» وفي السراج بقوله لأنه لا ضرر وأشار إليه المؤلف بقوله «آخراً إذا لم يمكنه وينبغي تقييد ذلك أيضاً بما إذا لم يقدر على النزول عن الدابة كما علم مما قدمناه عن الشيخ اسمعيل قوله : (قيدنا بالعجز مع قوله وكذا إذا كان في المفازة (الخ قال في النهر : قيد القدوري بأن لا يكون بحضرته من يسأله فإن كان وهو من أهل ذلك المكان مقبول الشهادة قدم على التحري وحد الحضرة أن يكون بحيث لو صاح به سمعه وقيده غيره بأن تكون السماء مغيمة، فإن كانت مصحية لا يجوز ولو جاهلاً لأنه ليس بعذر، وكان المصنف استغنى عن القيد الأوّل بذكر الاشتباه، وذلك أن تحققه إنما يكون عند
In the Fatawa: If they are in mud or dirt, they pray facing the qiblah if their mounts are standing. Others said: They pray facing the qiblah even if their mounts are moving. Muhammad said: If they are urged and the mounts are moving, it does not suffice if they are able to stop them. Similarly in al-Karkhi and in al-Tanbih. Al-Fath said: Even if on a mount he fears descending into mud or dirt, he faces the qiblah. In al-Zahiriyyah: In my view, this is when it is standing; if it is moving, he prays wherever he wishes. One may differentiate between whether, if he stops it for prayer, he fears being separated from the caravan or he does not fear; in the second, it is not permissible unless he stops it, as from Abu Yusuf regarding tayammum: if by going to water the caravan would leave and he would be cut off, it is permissible; otherwise he goes to the water and they approved this. I say: This was indicated in al-Tabyin by his saying 'if they are able' and in al-Siraj by his saying 'because there is no harm', and the author indicated it by his saying 'finally if he cannot'. And it should be restricted also to when he is unable to dismount from the mount, as learned from what we previously presented from Shaykh Isma'il. He said: (We restricted it with inability along with his saying: and likewise if he is in a desert (etc.)) He said in al-Nahr: al-Quduri restricted it by saying that there must not be someone near him to ask; if there is, and he is from that place and his testimony is acceptable, it takes precedence over taharri. The limit of being near is such that if he shouted, he would hear him. Others restricted it that the sky must be cloudy; if it is clear, it is not permissible even if ignorant, because it is not an excuse. And the author dispensed with the first restriction by mentioning ambiguity, because its realization occurs only when...
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings: first, praying on a mount in mud or dirt while riding; second, the conditions for taharri. For the first: several Hanafi opinions exist. The Fatwa says if the mounts are standing, one must face the qiblah; if moving, some say still face qiblah, but Muhammad says if the mount is moving, it does not suffice if they could stop it. Al-Fath and al-Zahiriyyah differentiate: if the mount is standing, face qiblah; if moving, pray in any direction, especially if stopping would cause separation from the caravan. Abu Yusuf's analogy to tayammum supports: if going for water would lose the caravan, tayammum is allowed; similarly, facing qiblah may be dropped. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) adds that this is restricted to when the person cannot dismount. Then the passage returns to the earlier topic of taharri conditions. Referring to al-Nahr, it states al-Quduri's condition: one must not have someone nearby to ask; if such a person exists and is reliable, he must be asked. The range is voice range. Another condition: the sky must be cloudy; if clear, taharri is not allowed even if one is ignorant, as the signs are present. The author of Kanz (the matn) dispensed with the first condition by simply saying 'when it is ambiguous', which implies impossibility of determination. The passage ends mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الردغة (al-radgha): Dirt or mud that would soil the clothes; a valid excuse for not dismounting.
الانقطاع عن الرفقة (al-inqitā‘ ‘an al-rifqa): Being separated from the caravan; a reason to allow not stopping the mount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the discussed Hanafi opinions, when is it permissible to pray on a moving mount in mud without facing the qiblah?
A) Always, because the mount is moving.
B) Only if the person is elderly and cannot dismount.
C) When stopping the mount would cause fear of separation from the caravan.
D) Only if the person is in a desert and the sky is cloudy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits praying without facing qiblah on a mount in mud only when stopping would cause fear of separation from the caravan; otherwise, facing qiblah is required.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for Using Taharrī for Qibla
Explains conditions for taharrī permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which taharrī is permissible and identify when it is prohibited.

Core Idea
Taharrī is only allowed when you cannot determine qibla; not when sky is clear or a mihrab exists.

When you are uncertain about the qibla, Islamic law provides a method called taharrī (estimation). However, this method is not always permitted. This lesson examines the conditions that make taharrī valid, drawing from the Hanafi legal tradition as explained in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause of uncertainty
Determine whether the person genuinely cannot face the qibla due to lost landmarks, darkness, or clouds. The passage states that the place for taharrī is when one is unable to face the qibla due to these reasons.
This is the sabab (trigger) for taharrī.
2
Check for clear sky
If the sky is clear (mus'hiah), taharrī is not permissible and ignorance is not excused. The text references al-Zahiriyya for this rule.
3
Check for presence of mihrabs
Taharrī is not permissible when a reliable mihrab (prayer niche) is present. The commentator explicitly states this.
This means if you are in a mosque with a mihrab, you must follow it without taharrī.
4
Confirm the ability to ask someone
If someone knowledgeable is available to ask, you must ask rather than do taharrī. The passage later discusses the mosque scenario where no one is available.
Taharrī becomes permissible only when asking is impossible.
5
Derive the ruling
If all conditions are met, taharrī is permissible and the prayer performed with taharrī is valid (sahih). If any condition is missing, taharrī is not allowed, and praying without proper direction may require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب شروط الصلاة
والقمر وغير ذلك، أما دقائق علم الهيئة وصور النجوم الثوابت فهو معذور في الجهل بها اهـ. فالحاصل أن محل التحري أن يعجز عن الاستقبال بانطماس الأعلام وتراكم الظلام وتضام الغمام كما ذكره المصنف في كافيه، وهو يرجح ما في الظهيرية من أن السماء إذا كانت مصحية لا يجوز التحري ولا يعذر بالجهل. وذكر الشارح أنه لا يجوز التحري مع المحاريب. وفي الظهيرية : رجل اشتبهت عليه القبلة في المسجد ولم يكن أحد يعرفه القبلة قال في الأصول : يجوز له التحري لأنه عجز عمن يسأله فصار كالمفازة. وقال أئمة بلخ منهم الفقيه أبو جعفر : لا تجوز له الصلاة بالتحري وعلل فقال : إن هذه نائبة العقبي فتعتبر بنائبة الدنيا ولو حدثت به نائبة الدنيا فإنه يستغيث بجيران المسجد كذلك ههنا يجب أن يستغيث بهم. وإن كان في مسجد نفسه قال بعضهم هو كالبيت لا يجوز له التحري. وقال بعضهم : مسجده ومسجد غيره سواء. وروى أبو جعفر عن سلام بن حكيم أنه قال : محاريب خراسان كلها منصوبة إلى الحجر الأسود والحجر الأسود إلى ميسرة الكعبة ومن توجه إلى الكعبة ومال بوجهه إلى ميسرة الكعبة وقع وجهه إلى جبل أبي قبيس، ومن مال بوجهه إلى يمينها وقع وجهه إلى الكعبة، ولهذا قيل يجب أن يميل إلى يمينها . قال : ومحاريب الدنيا كلها نصبت بالتحري حتى منى ولم يزد عليه شيئاً، وهذا خلاف ما نقل عن أبي بكر الرازي في محراب المدينة أنه مقطوع به فإنه إنما نصبه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالوحي بخلاف سائر البقاع حتى قيل أن محراب منى نصب بالتحري والعلامات وهو أقرب المواضع إلى مكة .اهـ. وبهذا تبين أن قولهم «لغير المكي أصابة جهتها ليس على إطلاقه بل في غير المدني فإن المدني كالمكي يفترض عليه إصابة عينها صرح به في السراج الوهاج أيضاً. وأطلق في الاشتباه فشمل ما إذا كان بمكة أو بالمدينة بأن كان محبوساً ولم يكن بحضرته من يسأله فصلى بالتحري ثم تبين أنه أخطأ، روي عن محمد أنه لا إعادة عليه، وكان الرازي يقول : تلزمه الإعادة لأنه تيقن بالخطأ إذا كان بمكة أو بالمدينة والأول أحسن كذا في الظهيرية وفي فتاوى قاضيخان رجل صلى في المسجد في ليلة مظلمة بالتحري فتبين أنه صلى إلى غير القبلة جازت صلاته لأنه ليس له أن يقرع أبواب
الناس للسؤال عن القبلة، ولا يعرف القبلة بمس الجدار والحيطان لأن الحائط لو كانت منقوشة لا يمكنه تمييز المحراب من غيره وعسى يكون ثم هامة مؤذية فجاز له التحري
