Understanding Sifah and Wasf: The Foundation of Defining Prayer
Defining the term 'sifah' in the chapter heading and its relation to 'wasf'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the linguistic and terminological meanings of 'sifah' and 'wasf', list the six necessary components for establishing any entity, and apply them to define 'sifat al-salah'.

Core Idea
Sifah and wasf are linguistically synonymous but terminologically distinct; 'sifat al-salah' means the rational parts that constitute the essence of prayer.

Before diving into the rulings of prayer, the Hanafi jurists clarify the precise meaning of the chapter heading 'Sifat al-Salah'. This opening discussion is not mere semantics—it establishes the methodological framework for defining any act of worship. By understanding the terms 'sifah' and 'wasf', and the six necessary components of a thing, you will be able to identify what truly constitutes the prayer and what is external to its essence.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic and terminological usage
Read the opening statement: 'al-sifah wa al-wasf fi al-lughah wahid'. Understand that in language they are synonyms, but the mutakallimun differentiate. Note the basis for this differentiation: wasf subsists in the describer, sifah in the described.
Pay attention to the quote from al-Sihah and al-Qamus confirming the linguistic synonymy.
2
Identify the six necessary components
From the quotation of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, list the six things: 'ayn (essence), rukn (pillar), hukm (ruling), mahall (locus), shart (condition), sabab (cause). Understand each definition.
These components are universal for establishing any entity in Hanafi legal theory.
3
Apply the six components to prayer
The author explicitly applies them: 'ayn = prayer itself, rukn = standing, recitation, bowing, prostration, mahall = mukallaf, shart = purification, hukm = permissibility/corruption/reward, sabab = prayer times.
This application is found in the final paragraph of the source.
4
Define 'sifat al-salah' in Hanafi fiqh
Synthesize: 'sifat al-salah' refers to the rational parts (ajza' aqliyyah) that constitute the quiddity (mahiyyah) of prayer, not merely external descriptions. It is these essential internal components.
This definition resolves the technical meaning behind the chapter heading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفة الصلاة
شروع في المقصود بعد الفراغ من مقدماته . قيل : الصفة والوصف في اللغة واحد وفي عرف المتكلمين بخلافه والتحرير أن الوصف لغة ذكر ما في الموصوف من الصفة والصفة هي ما فيه ولا ينكر أنه يطلق الوصف ويراد الصفة وبهذا لا يلزم الاتحاد لغة إذ لا شك في أن الوصف مصدر صفه إذا ذكر ما فيه. ثم المراد هنا بصفة الصلاة الأوصاف النفسية لها وهي الأجزاء العقلية الصادقة على الخارجية التي هي أجزاء الهويه من القيام الجزئي والركوع والسجود. كذا في فتح القدير. وليس هذا من باب قيام العرض بالعرض لأن الأحكام الشرعية لها حكم الجواهر ولهذا توصف بالصحة والفساد والبطلان والفسخ . كذا في غاية البيان. وفي السراج الوهاج ثم اعلم أنه يشترط لثبوت الشيء ستة أشياء العين وهي ماهية الشيء، فلا يكون الشيء، والركن وهو جزء الماهية والحكم وهو الأثر الثابت بالشيء، ومحل ذلك الشيء، وشرطه وسببه فلا يكون الشيء ثابتاً إلا بوجود هذه الأشياء الستة.
باب صفة الصلاة
قوله : (قيل الصفة والوصف في اللغة واحد قال في معراج الدراية ثم الوصف والصفة مصدران كالوعظ والعظة والوعد والعدة والوزن والزنة وفي الصحاح : وصف الشيء وصفاً وصفة فالهاء عوض عن الواو كما في الوعد والعدة. وفي اصطلاح المتكلمين: الوصف ما قام بالواصف وهو قوله زيد عالم والصفة ما قام بالموصوف .اهـ. ونحوه في النهاية والعناية. وفي القاموس : وصفه يصفه وصفاً وصفة نعته فاتصف والصفة كالعلم والسواد اهـ. وفي شرح العيني : والصفة والوصف مصدران من وصف والصفة الأمارة اللازمة للشيء ، ثم اعترض على المتكلمين بقوله : وليت شعري من أين التخصيص ..اهـ. وقد ظهر من هذا أن الصفة تكون مصدراً كالوصف وتكون اسماً لما قام بالموصوف كالعلم مثلاً، وحينئذ فمخالفة المتكلمين من حيث تخصيص الصفة باستعمالهم إياها اسماً . الأمارة اللازمة مع أنها قد تكون في اللغة مصدراً. والجواب عما قاله بمعنى
ثم
فالعين هنا الصلاة، والركن القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود، والمحل للشيء هو الآدمي المكلف، والشرط هو ما تقدم من الطهارة وغيرها والحكم جواز الشيء وفساده وثوابه، والسبب الأوقات. ومعنى صفة الصلاة أي ماهية الصلاة
Chapter on the description of prayer. Start of the intended after completion of its preliminaries. It is said: Sifah and wasf are one in language, but in the terminology of the scholastics (mutakallimun) it is otherwise. The correct view is that wasf (description) linguistically is mentioning what is in the described from the attribute (sifah), and sifah is what is in it. And it is not denied that wasf is used and by it sifah is meant, and by this there does not necessarily follow unity in language, since there is no doubt that wasf is a masdar (verbal noun) of 'wasafa' when he mentions what is in it. Then what is intended here by 'description of prayer' are the essential (nafsiyyah) attributes of it, which are the rational (aqliyyah) parts that apply to the external parts that are the parts of identity (hawiyyah), such as the particular standing, bowing, and prostration. This is as in Fath al-Qadir. And this is not a case of an accident subsisting in an accident because the legal rulings have the ruling of substances (jawhar), and for this they are described with validity, corruption, nullity, and rescission. This is as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Then know that for the establishment of something six things are necessary: the essence ('ayn) which is the quiddity (mahiyyah) of the thing, otherwise the thing does not exist; the pillar (rukn) which is part of the quiddity; the ruling (hukm) which is the effect established by the thing; the locus (mahall) of that thing; its condition (shart); and its cause (sabab); so the thing is not established except by the existence of these six things.

Chapter on the description of prayer. His saying: (it is said sifah and wasf are one in language). He said in Miraj al-Diraya: Then wasf and sifah are both masdars like wa'z and 'izah, wa'd and 'iddah, wazn and zinnah. And in al-Sihah: 'wasafa al-shay'a wasfan wa sifatan' so the ha' is a substitute for the waw as in wa'd and 'iddah. And in the terminology of the scholastics: wasf is what subsists in the describer (wasif) such as his saying 'Zayd is knowledgeable', and sifah is what subsists in the described (mawsuf). End. And similar in al-Nihayah and al-Inayah. And in al-Qamus: 'wasafahu yasifuhu wasfan wa sifatan' he described him, so he became described, and sifah is like knowledge and blackness. End. And in Sharh al-Ayni: sifah and wasf are both masdars from wasafa, and sifah is the distinctive mark (amarah) necessary for the thing. Then he objected to the scholastics by saying: I wish I knew where this specification comes from? End. And it has become apparent from this that sifah is used as a masdar like wasf and also as a noun for what subsists in the described, like knowledge for example. Then, the disagreement with the scholastics is regarding their specification of sifah as being used as a noun, the necessary distinctive mark, while it can also be a masdar in language. And the response to his saying...

Then: So the essence ('ayn) here is prayer, the pillar (rukn) is standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration, the locus (mahall) is the legally responsible person (al-adami al-mukallaf), the condition (shart) is what has preceded of purification and other things, the ruling (hukm) is the permissibility of the thing, its corruption, its reward, and the cause (sabab) is the times. And the meaning of 'description of prayer' (sifat al-salah) is the quiddity of prayer.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and terminological discussion about the word 'sifah' (attribute) and 'wasf' (description) as they appear in the chapter heading 'Bab Sifat al-Salah'. The author, Zayla'i in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, begins by stating that in the Arabic language, 'sifah' and 'wasf' are synonymous, both being verbal nouns (masdars) derived from 'wasafa' (to describe). However, the scholastics (mutakallimun) differentiate: they use 'wasf' for the description that subsists in the describer (e.g., saying 'Zayd is knowledgeable' is a description of Zayd by the speaker), and 'sifah' for the attribute that subsists in the described (e.g., knowledge itself in Zayd). The author clarifies that the correct view is that 'wasf' linguistically is the act of mentioning the attribute of the described, while 'sifah' is the attribute itself. He notes that although 'wasf' is sometimes used with the meaning of 'sifah', this does not imply complete unity in language because 'wasf' is primarily a masdar. The passage then explains that in this chapter, 'sifat al-salah' refers to the essential (nafsiyyah) attributes of prayer, which are the rational parts like standing, bowing, prostration, etc. The author also addresses a potential objection: these are accidents (a'rad), but they are described as subsisting in the prayer, which is itself an accident; however, legal rulings are treated like substances (jawahir) for the purpose of legal description. The passage then quotes al-Siraj al-Wahhaj stating that for any entity to be established, six things are needed: 'ayn (essence), rukn (pillar), hukm (ruling), mahall (locus), shart (condition), and sabab (cause). The passage then applies these to prayer. Finally, the author reiterates that sifah can be both a masdar and a noun for the attribute, and the disagreement with the scholastics is about their exclusive use of sifah as a noun. The response to their objection is indicated but not fully given. This discussion is foundational for understanding the precise meaning of 'sifat al-salah' and the methodology of defining legal concepts in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الصفة (al-ṣifah): Attribute that subsists in the described; in this text, the essential parts of prayer like standing, bowing, etc.
الوصف (al-waṣf): Description; the act of describing or the description itself; in scholastic terminology, what subsists in the describer.
الأجزاء العقلية (al-ajzā' al-'aqliyyah): Rational parts; the conceptual components of prayer as distinct from physical parts.
العين (al-'ayn): Essence/quiddity of the thing; here the essence of prayer.
الركن (al-rukn): Pillar; part of the quiddity; its omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are completely identical.
B) Wasf is used for describing Allah, sifah for creation.
C) Wasf subsists in the describer, sifah in the described.
D) Sifah is only used in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'sifat al-salah' is defined by the rational parts that constitute the essence of prayer, understood through the six necessary components of any entity.

Takbirat al-Ihram: Condition or Pillar? The Hanafi Position
Determining the legal status of the opening takbir in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on takbirat al-ihram as a condition, explain its evidence, and distinguish it from the pillar view.

Core Idea
Takbirat al-ihram is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar — omission invalidates the prayer altogether.

The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is the first 'Allahu Akbar' that marks the beginning of prayer, transforming permissible actions into forbidden ones. While all scholars agree it is obligatory (fard), there is a dispute over its precise legal nature: is it a condition (shart) or one of its pillars (rukn)? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its proofs, and how it differs from the minority view within the school and from Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is takbirat al-ihram, and its ruling is fard (obligatory) by definitive proof. Understand the Hanafi definition of fard as something obligated by qat'i evidence.
Fard in Hanafi includes both conditions and pillars.
2
Examine the primary evidence
The imperative in Qur'an 74:3 (wa rabbaka fakabbir) and the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification; its tahrim is takbir; its tahlil is taslim.'
Hanafi usul: the imperative (amr) indicates obligation.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
The majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) consider it a condition; a minority (e.g., Isam ibn Yusuf, al-Tahawi) consider it a pillar. Note the Shafi'i agreement with the minority.
The difference is within the Hanafi school itself.
4
Analyze the Hanafi tarjih
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that it is a condition. The key evidence is the conjunction in Surah al-A'la (87:15) 'And mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed', which implies that takbir is separate from prayer.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and others support this.
5
Determine the practical consequence
As a condition, omission invalidates prayer; there is no compensation (sajdah al-sahw) — the prayer must be restarted from the beginning.
The practical effect is the same even if considered a pillar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فرضها التحريمة) أي ما لا بد منه فيها فإن الفرض شرعاً ما لزم فعله بدليل قطعي أعم من أن يكون شرطاً أو ركناً، والتحريم جعل الشيء محرماً. وخصت التكبيرة الأولى بها لأنها تحرم الأشياء المباحة قبل الشروع بخلاف سائر التكبيرات والدليل على فرضيتها قوله تعالى وربك فكبر [المدثر : ٣] جاء في التفسير أن المراد به تكبيرة الافتتاح ولأن الأمر للإيجاب وما وراءها ليس بفرض فتعين أن تكون مرادة لئلا يؤدي إلى تعطيل النص. وما رواه أبو داود وغيره عن علي رضي الله عنه عن النبي الله أنه قال «مفتاح الصلاة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم (۱). اختلفوا هل هي شرط أو ركن؛ ففي الحاوي هي شرط في أصح الروايتين، وجعله في البدائع قول المحققين من مشايخنا. وفي غاية البيان قول عامة المشايخ وهو الأصح، واختار بعض مشايخنا منهم عصام بن يوسف والطحاوي أنها ركن وبه قال الشافعي لأنها ذكر مفروض في القيام فكان ركناً كالقراءة ولهذا شرط لها ما شرط لسائر الأركان من الطهارة وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة ووجه الأصح وهو المذهب عطف الصلاة عليها في قوله تعالى وذكر اسم ربه فصلى [الأعلى : ١٥] ومقتضى العطف المغايرة والمغايرة وإن كانت ثابتة على القول بركنيتها أيضاً لأنه حينئذ يكون من باب عطف الكل على الجزء وهو نظير عطف العام
His saying (its fard is the tahrimah) meaning that which is indispensable in it. For the fard in Shariah is that which its action is obligated by a definitive proof, general as to whether it is a condition or a pillar. And tahrim is making something forbidden. And the first takbir is specifically designated with it because it forbids the permissible things before starting, unlike the rest of the takbirs. The proof for its obligatory status is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3). It came in the exegesis that what is meant by it is the opening takbir. And because the command is for obligation, and what is beyond it is not fard, so it is determined that it is intended lest it lead to suspension of the text. And what was narrated by Abu Dawud and others from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition (tahrim) is the takbir, and its opening (tahlil) is the taslim.' They differed as to whether it is a condition or a pillar. In al-Hawi, it is a condition in the more correct of the two narrations. And in al-Bada'i', he made it the saying of the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqun) among our shaykhs. And in Ghayat al-Bayan, it is the saying of the general body of shaykhs, and it is the most correct. And some of our shaykhs chose it as a pillar, among them 'Isam ibn Yusuf and al-Tahawi, and al-Shafi'i also said so because it is a dhikr (remembrance) that is prescribed in standing, so it is a pillar like recitation. For this reason, what is required for other pillars (like purification, covering the private parts, facing the qibla) is also required for it. The aspect of the most correct (al-asahh), which is the madhhab, is the conjunction of prayer with it in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed' (87:15). The requirement of conjunction is difference, and difference is established even on the view that it is a pillar, because that would be a case of conjoining the whole to the part, and it is similar to conjoining the general...
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling regarding the status of the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) in prayer. The author explains that 'tahrimah' refers to the first takbir, which makes forbidden what was previously permissible. The proof for its obligatory status is from the Qur'an (74:3) and the hadith of 'Ali that the key to prayer is purification, its tahrim is takbir, and its tahlil is taslim. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the majority of Hanafi scholars (including the muhaqqiqun and 'ammah al-mashayikh) consider it a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer, while some like 'Isam ibn Yusuf and al-Tahawi consider it a pillar (rukn). The latter view is also held by al-Shafi'i. The argument for it being a pillar is that it is a dhikr prescribed in standing, like recitation. The response of the majority is that the conjunction in 'mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed' implies difference, which is maintained even if takbir is a pillar, as it would be conjoining the whole (prayer) to its part (takbir). The relied-upon position (al-mukhtar) in the Hanafi school is that it is a condition, and this is the basis for fatwa.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that prohibits previously permissible actions
الفَرْض (al-farḍ): That which is obligated by a definitive proof
الشَّرْط (al-sharṭ): A condition for validity; an external element required for prayer to be valid
الرُّكْن (al-rukn): A pillar; an integral part that must be performed; omission invalidates

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A pillar (rukn)
B) A condition (shart)
C) A sunnah
D) A wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's authoritative position is that takbirat al-ihram is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar, and its omission invalidates the prayer entirely.

The Opening Takbir: Condition or Pillar?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on condition vs pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the legal status of the opening takbir and distinguish between the condition (shart) and pillar (rukn) views with their proofs and practical consequences.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn) — and this distinction changes how we combine prayers.

The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is universally recognized as obligatory, but its precise nature — whether it is a condition or a pillar — has been debated within the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks that debate, examining the proofs from Quran and hadith, and shows why the majority Hanafi view (and the mufta bihi position) treats it as a condition. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying rulings on building one prayer upon another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal category
The author first defines 'fard' as an obligation established by a definitive proof, which can be either a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn). Note that the opening takbir is called 'tahrimah' because it makes previously permissible acts prohibited during prayer.
Fard here is broader than shart/rukn; it simply means obligatory.
2
Locate the proofs for fardiyyah
The author cites Quran 74:3 ('And your Lord magnify') interpreted as the opening takbir, and a hadith from Ali (ra) stating 'its tahrimah is the takbir'. The imperative in the verse indicates obligation (amr yufidu al-wujub).
The Quranic proof is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding the specific takbir.
3
Follow the intra-Hanafi dispute
The author reports that some Hanafis (e.g., 'Isam ibn Yusuf, al-Tahawi) and al-Shafi'i hold it is a pillar (rukn). Their proof: it is a dhikr performed in standing, like recitation, and conditions of purity, covering, and qibla are required for it as for other pillars.
The opposing view within the school is a minority, but it has been taken by Imam al-Shafi'i as well.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority Hanafi view uses Quran 87:15 ('mentions the name of his Lord and prays') — the conjunction (عطف) implies separation between the takbir (part of dhikr) and prayer. Thus the takbir is not part of prayer but a condition. Additionally, the conditions required for the takbir are actually for the standing (qiyam) that follows, not the takbir itself.
The author refutes the opposing proof by denying that conditions are observed for the takbir, citing practical examples.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if it is a condition, one can build a supererogatory prayer (nafl) upon the tahrimah of a fard prayer (e.g., change intention from fard to nafl without a new takbir). If it is a pillar, this is not allowed.
This ruling is contested even within the Hanafi school, as some condition-view scholars disagree.

His statement (its fard is the tahrimah): meaning what is indispensable in it, for fard in Sacred Law is what is obligated by a definitive proof, whether it be a condition or a pillar. Tahrimah is making something prohibited. The first takbir was singled out because it prohibits permissible things before commencing, unlike other takbirs. The proof of its being fard is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And your Lord magnify' [al-Muddaththir: 3]; in exegesis it is said that it means the opening takbir, and because command indicates obligation, and what is after it is not fard, so it must be intended so as not to void the text. And what Abu Dawud and others narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet [Allah?] that he said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its tahrimah is the takbir, and its tahlil is the taslim.' They differed whether it is a condition or a pillar. In al-Hawi it is a condition in the sounder of the two narrations, and in al-Bada'i' it is made the statement of the verifying scholars among our shaykhs. In Ghayat al-Bayan, it is the statement of the generality of the shaykhs and it is the most correct. Some of our shaykhs, including 'Isam ibn Yusuf and al-Tahawi, chose that it is a pillar, and al-Shafi'i held that too because it is a dhikr made obligatory in standing, so it is a pillar like recitation, and for this, what is made a condition for other pillars, like purification, covering the 'awrah, and facing the qibla, are made conditions for it. The more correct view—and it is the madhhab—is the conjunction of prayer to it in His saying 'and mentions the name of his Lord and prays' [al-A'la: 15], and the requirement of conjunction is difference, and difference is established even on the view that it is a pillar because then it would be of the type of conjunction of the whole to the part, which is like conjoining the general to the specific, but its permissibility is for a rhetorical subtlety which is not apparent here, so it necessarily follows that the takbir is not from it (prayer), thus it is a condition, and that is what is sought. And observing the aforementioned conditions is not for it but for the standing connected to it, which is a pillar—if we grant that it is observed, otherwise it is rejected. So presenting the objection before the concession is better, as in al-Talwih. So it is better to say: we do not grant that they are observed, for if he proclaims the tahrimah while carrying impurity, then throws it away when finished from it, or facing away from the qibla then faces it when finished, or with uncovered 'awrah then covers it after the takbir with a slight action, or begins the takbir before the time of zuhur appears then it appears when he finishes it, it is permissible. In al-Hawi: what supports that it is a condition is the validity of the congregation in Friday prayer despite the congregation not participating with the imam in it. And the fruit of the difference appears in building a nafl (supererogatory prayer) upon the tahrimah of a fard: it is permissible according to those who hold it is a condition, and not permissible according to those who hold it is a pillar. And the statement of the commentator that it is permissible by consensus among our companions requires reflection, for those among our companions who hold it is a pillar do not permit it. As for building a fard upon a fard or upon a nafl, it is permissible according to Sadr al-Islam because it is known that it is a condition like purification, but it is not permissible on the apparent of the madhhab. This is not permissible: performing a prayer with the intention of another prayer by consensus. As for performing [building?] like the intention is not among the pillars, and with nafl by a tahrimah of nafl, there is no doubt about its validity by agreement because the entire [act] is one prayer, evidenced by that the sitting does not...
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the legal nature of the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). It begins by stating that the fard (obligatory element) of the prayer is the tahrimah, which is the act that renders previously permissible things forbidden during the prayer. The author distinguishes between fard as a definitive obligation that can be either a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn). The proof from the Quran (74:3) is cited, with the interpretation that 'magnify your Lord' refers to the opening takbir, and the command indicates obligation. A hadith from Ali (ra) is also quoted. The main discussion is the dispute among Hanafi scholars: is the opening takbir a condition or a pillar? According to al-Hawi, it is a condition in the sounder narration; in al-Bada'i', it is the view of the verifying scholars; in Ghayat al-Bayan, the generality of scholars hold it is a condition and that is the most correct. However, some Hanafis like 'Isam ibn Yusuf and al-Tahawi, as well as Imam al-Shafi'i, consider it a pillar, arguing that it is a dhikr in the standing posture, similar to recitation. The author then provides a detailed argument for the condition view based on the conjunction in verse 87:15, concluding that the takbir is not part of the prayer itself but a condition. The practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) is significant: if the takbir is a condition, one can supererogatory upon a fard tahrimah (e.g., building nafl on fard), but if it is a pillar, it is not allowed. The commentator criticizes a claim of consensus on this issue and discusses the views of Sadr al-Islam. The passage ends with a discussion about building prayers and the role of intention (niyyah), emphasizing that the niyyah is not a pillar and that building nafl upon nafl is agreed upon. The author urges precision in understanding the distinction between condition and pillar, as it affects the validity of combining prayers.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The act that makes normally permissible actions prohibited during prayer; specifically the opening takbir.
الفرض (al-fard): An obligation established by a decisive proof (dalil qat'i), encompassing both conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan).
الشرط (al-shart): A condition external to the essence of the prayer, whose absence prevents validity but is not part of the prayer's constitution.
الركن (al-rukn): A part of the prayer's essence; its omission invalidates the prayer and cannot be compensated except by repetition.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a scholarly disagreement; here, whether one can build a nafl upon a fard's tahrimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (mufta bihi), the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is considered a:
A) Pillar (rukn) of the prayer.
B) Condition (shart) of the prayer.
C) Recommended sunnah.
D) Part of the intention (niyyah).

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is a condition (shart) for prayer in the Hanafi school, and this distinction from a pillar (rukn) affects whether one can change the prayer type after the takbir.

Takbirat al-Ihram: Condition or Pillar? Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on takbirat al-ihram's nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute over takbirat al-ihram, identify the evidence for the condition view, and apply the ruling to building a nafl prayer upon a fard takbir.

Core Idea
Takbirat al-ihram is a condition, not a pillar — building nafl on a fard takbir is valid.

The takbir that opens the prayer seems integral, but Hanafi scholars debate whether it is a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the dominant view that it is a condition, and the practical difference it makes when linking prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the exact point of contention: Is takbirat al-ihram a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn) of the prayer?
This affects how we understand the takbir's relation to the rest of the prayer.
2
Analyze the evidence for condition view
List the proofs: (1) one can rectify impurity, qibla, or awrah during the takbir with slight action; (2) in Friday prayer, women do not join the imam's takbir yet the prayer is valid. These show the takbir is separate from the prayer itself.
Condition can be perfected after the act has begun; a pillar cannot be separated.
3
Understand the opposing view
Some Hanafi scholars consider it a pillar, meaning the takbir is part of the prayer and cannot be used for another prayer.
The text from al-Hawi supports the condition view, rejecting consensus claimed by the commentator.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
If a person says the takbir intending a fard prayer, then changes intention to nafl, is it valid? Under condition view, yes, because the takbir is separate and can be reused. Under pillar view, no, because the takbir belongs to the first prayer.
This is called 'building nafl upon the takbir of fard'.
5
Evaluate the dispute's resolution
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that takbirat al-ihram is a condition, supported by the evidence and later Hanafi authorities.
The passage also discusses building fard upon fard/nafl, which is another layer, but the core dispute remains the nature of the takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الخاص لكن جواز لنكتة بلاغية وهي غير ظاهرة هنا فيلزم أن لا يكون التكبير منها فهو شرط وهو المطلوب ومراعاة الشرائط المذكورة ليس لها بل للقيام المتصل بها وهو ركن إن سلمنا مراعاتها وإلا فهو ممنوع ، فتقديم المنع على التسليم أولى كذا في التلويح . فالأولى أن يقال : : لا نسلم مراعاتها فإنه لو أحرم إلى آخره ولئن سلمنا فهي ليس لها بل إلى آخره فإنه لو أحرم حاملاً للنجاسة فالقاه عند فراغه منها أو منحرفاً عن القبلة فاستقبلها عند الفراغ منها أو مكشوف العورة فسترها عند فراغه من التكبير بعمل يسير أو شرع في التكبير قبل ظهور الزوال ثم ظهر عند فراغه منها جاز . وفي الحاوي: والذي يؤيد أنها شرط انعقاد الجمعه مع عدم مشاركة القوم الإمام فيها . وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في بناء النفل على تحريمة الفرض، فيجوز عند القائلين بالشرطية، ولا يجوز عند القائلين بالركنية وقول الشارح إنه يجوز بالإجماع بين أصحابنا فيه نظر، فإن القائلين بالركنية من أصحابنا لا يجوزونه وأما بناء الفرض على الفرض أو على النفل فهو جائز عند صدر الإسلام لما علمت أنها شرط كالطهارة، ولا يجوز على الظاهر من المذهب هذا لا يجوز أداء صلاة بنية صلاة أخرى إجماعاً. وأما أداء كالنية ليست من الأركان ومع النفل بتحريمة النفل فلا شك في صحته اتفاقاً لما أن الكل صلاة واحدة بدليل أن القعود لا يفترض إلا في آخرها على الصحيح. وقولهم إن كل ركعتين من النفل صلاة لا يعارضه لأنه في أحكام دون أخرى.
On the specific [matter], but its permissibility [is] for a rhetorical subtlety which is not apparent here, so it necessitates that the takbir is not from it [the prayer], so it is a condition, and that is what is required. And observance of the mentioned conditions is not for it [the takbir] but for the standing connected to it, which is a pillar if we concede its observance, otherwise it is denied. So giving precedence to denial over concession is better, as in al-Talwih. So it is better to say: We do not concede its observance; for if he enters the prayer [with takbir] while carrying impurity, then discards it upon completing [the takbir], or [if he is] deviating from the qibla, then faces it upon completing it, or [if he] has his 'awrah exposed, then covers it upon completing the takbir with a slight action, or [if he] begins the takbir before the time of zawal [declination] then it appears upon completing it, [then] it is valid. And in al-Hawi: What supports that it is a condition is the validity of Friday prayer despite the community not sharing the imam in it. And the fruit of the disagreement appears in building a supererogatory [prayer] upon the obligatory takbir; it is valid according to those who say it is a condition, and invalid according to those who say it is a pillar. And the statement of the commentator that it is valid by consensus among our companions is subject to consideration, for those who say it is a pillar among our companions do not permit it. As for building an obligatory prayer upon another obligatory or upon a supererogatory, it is valid according to Sadr al-Islam because it is known that it is a condition like purity, but it is not valid according to the apparent [position] of the school. This: it is not valid to perform a prayer with the intention of another prayer by consensus. As for performing [a supererogatory prayer] like [i.e., with] the intention? The intention is not among the pillars, and with a supererogatory prayer [performed] with the takbir of a supererogatory [prayer], there is no doubt of its validity by agreement, because all are one prayer, as evidenced by the fact that sitting is only obligatory at the end of it, according to the correct [view]. And their saying that every two rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer are a separate prayer does not contradict it, because it is in some rulings and not others.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage discusses a key dispute within the Hanafi school: is takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir) a condition (shart) for the validity of prayer or a pillar (rukn) that is part of the prayer itself. The author argues that it is a condition, not a pillar. Evidence: if one begins the takbir while impure or facing the wrong direction, then rectifies these during the takbir with slight action, it is valid—showing the takbir is separate. Also, in Friday prayer, women do not perform the takbir with the imam, yet the Friday prayer is valid, indicating it is a condition external to the prayer. The practical consequence (thamara) is: if a person starts a supererogatory (nafl) prayer with the takbir of a fard prayer, it is allowed according to those who say it is a condition (because the takbir is separate and can be used for a different prayer), but not allowed by those who say it is a pillar. The author rejects the claim of consensus that it is valid, noting that those who consider it a pillar do not allow it. He then discusses building a fard prayer upon another fard or nafl: Sadr al-Islam allows it (since he considers takbir a condition), but the apparent madhhab position does not. Finally, he clarifies that the intention (niyyah) is not a pillar—so the analogy that because intention is not a pillar, building is not allowed is flawed. The whole discussion underscores the legal methodology of determining the nature of a component and its implications for prayer validity.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that marks the beginning of the prayer.
شرط (shart): A condition external to the act that must be present for validity but is not part of the act.
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of the prayer that must be performed; omission invalidates the prayer.
بناء النفل على تحريمة الفرض (bina' al-nafl 'ala tahrimat al-fard): Building a supererogatory prayer upon the opening takbir of an obligatory prayer (i.e., reusing the same takbir for a different prayer intention).
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'The takbir is a pillar'.
D) All schools agree it is a condition.

Key Takeaway
Takbirat al-ihram is a condition, not a pillar, so building a nafl prayer upon the takbir of a fard prayer is valid in the Hanafi school.

Ruling for the Mute and Illiterate: Opening Prayer with Intention Alone
Ruling that a mute or illiterate person may open the prayer with intention without moving the tongue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the mute and illiterate regarding the opening takbir and explain why intention alone suffices.

Core Idea
Intention substitutes for the opening takbir for those unable to speak or pronounce it correctly.

This passage clarifies a concession in Hanafi fiqh for two categories of people: the mute (akhras) who cannot speak at all, and the illiterate (ummi) who cannot correctly pronounce the Arabic takbir. It establishes that they may open their prayer with intention alone, without any verbal utterance. The discussion also addresses whether they must move their tongue for other takbirs during the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that the ruling applies to the mute (al-akhras) and the illiterate (al-ummi). The mute cannot speak, and the illiterate cannot pronounce the takbir correctly due to inability to read or articulate.
2
State the ruling
Both may open the prayer with intention (niyyah) alone; it suffices and the prayer is valid. No verbal takbir is required.
3
Understand the rationale
The ruling is based on the principle that they have done their utmost (aqsā mā fī wus'ihima). Since they cannot fulfill the verbal requirement, intention is accepted as a substitute.
This is a manifestation of the broader usul principle: 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysī' (hardship brings ease).
4
Differentiate the takbirs
For the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram), intention substitutes for the tongue. For all other takbirs during the prayer (e.g., for bowing, prostrating), they must move their tongue because those takbirs have no substitute.
The difference is that the opening takbir has a substitute (intention), while others do not.
5
Note the nuances
Some commentators require that the intention include standing (qiyam), and that intention cannot precede the action. Additionally, the author suggests that moving the tongue for the opening takbir is not even recommended (sunnah) for these individuals.
The phrase 'ta'ammal' (consider) indicates the author's cautious view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط الأخرس والأمي افتتحا بالنية أجزأهما لأنهما أتيا بأقصى ما في وسعهما. وفي شرح منية المصلي : ولا يجب عليهما تحريك اللسان عندنا وهو الصحيح. قوله : (وفي المحيط الأخرس والأمي الخ قال في النهر : ينبغي أن يشترط القيام في نيتهما لقيامها مقام التحريمة وأن تقديمها لا يصح ولم أره .لهم. قوله : (وفي شرح منية المصلي ولا يجب عليهما تحريك اللسان أي في تكبيرة الإحرام. وأما باقي التكبيرات ففي النهر عن طلاق الفتح أنه يحرك لسانه بها قال : وكان الفرق أن تكبيرة الإحرام لها خلف وهو النية بخلاف غيرها اهـ. أقول : يظهر من هذا أنه لا يسن أيضاً تحريك اللسان بتكبيرة الإحرام تأمل.
And in al-Muhit: The mute and the illiterate opened [the prayer] with intention; it suffices them because they did their utmost within their capacity. And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: They are not obliged to move the tongue according to us, and that is the correct [view]. He said: (And in al-Muhit, the mute and the illiterate, etc.) al-Nahr said: It should be required that standing be [included] in their intention, because it [intention] stands in place of the takbir, and that its precedence is not valid, but I have not seen [this ruling] for them. He said: (And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: They are not obliged to move the tongue) i.e., in takbirat al-ihram. As for the remaining takbirs, in al-Nahr from Talaq al-Fath: He moves his tongue with them. He said: The difference is that takbirat al-ihram has a substitute, which is the intention, unlike others. I say: It appears from this that it is not even recommended (sunnah) to move the tongue for takbirat al-ihram - consider.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling for two types of people: the mute (akhras) who cannot speak, and the illiterate (ummi) who cannot pronounce the Arabic takbir correctly (perhaps due to inability to read or articulate). According to al-Muhit, they may open their prayer with intention (niyyah) alone, without verbal takbir, and this suffices because they have done what they can. The author then quotes from Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that they are not even required to move their tongue (taḥrīk al-lisān) for the opening takbir; this is the correct view in the Hanafi school. The subsequent commentary by al-Nahr adds that they should include the intention of standing (qiyam) since the intention substitutes for the takbir, but he notes that precedence of intention (i.e., making intention before the action) is not valid. For other takbirs in the prayer (e.g., takbirs for bowing, prostrating), al-Nahr from Talaq al-Fath states that they should move their tongue for these, because the opening takbir has a substitute (intention) which others do not. The author (Ibn Nujaym) then expresses his own view: from this it appears that moving the tongue for takbirat al-ihram is not even recommended (sunnah) for these individuals, but he says 'consider' (ta'ammal), implying the matter is open to discussion.

Key Terms
الأخرس (al-akhras): A person who is mute and cannot speak.
الأمي (al-ummi): A person who is illiterate and cannot read or pronounce the Arabic takbir correctly.
تحريك اللسان (tahrik al-lisan): Moving the tongue to articulate the words of the takbir.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The opening takbir that begins the prayer, saying 'Allahu Akbar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for a mute person regarding the opening takbir?
A) He must move his tongue silently.
B) He may suffice with intention (niyyah) alone.
C) He must get someone else to say it for him.
D) He is exempt from the prayer entirely.

Key Takeaway
The mute and illiterate can open prayer with intention alone; for other takbirs, they must move the tongue.

Rulings on the Follower's Takbir: Timing and Disputes
Scenarios and rulings for a follower's takbir timing: joining imam in ruku', finishing before imam, starting before imam, and dealing with uncertainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a follower's takbir timing relative to the imam and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the follower finishing his takbir before the imam.

Core Idea
A follower may finish his takbir before the imam; the prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf disagrees.

This passage examines several scenarios involving the follower's takbir during congregational prayer. Central to the discussion is a dispute within the Hanafi school: if the follower completes his takbir before the imam finishes, does the prayer remain valid? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it is valid, while Abu Yusuf requires full synchronization. The text also covers when a follower is uncertain about the timing and the role of predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two positions
The text presents the case of a follower finishing his takbir before the imam finishes. Identify that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it valid (أجزأه على قياس قولهما), while Abu Yusuf holds it invalid (لا يجزئه).
The phrase 'قولهما' here refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
2
Understand the underlying reasoning (qiyas)
For the majority, the follower's intention to follow and commencement of prayer are key; finishing early does not break the connection because the imam's takbir is still in progress. For Abu Yusuf, synchronization is essential.
The text explicitly mentions 'على قياس قولهما' – according to their analogy.
3
Analyze the text's response to Abu Yusuf
The text states that according to the qiyas of their saying it is valid, implying that Abu Yusuf's view is weaker. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
Refer to al-Muhit and al-Tanjis cited in the passage.
4
Apply the rule of ghalabat al-zann
When the follower is uncertain whether his takbir preceded the imam's, he relies on predominant opinion. If his predominant opinion is that he said it after, the prayer is valid; otherwise invalid.
The text: 'فإن كان أكبر رأيه أنه كبر قبله لا يجزئه وإلا أجزأه'.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects whether many followers' prayers are valid in practice. The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is more accommodating, avoiding unnecessary repetition of prayers in congregations.
This is the operative difference for fatwa.

And if the author said 'its obligation is the opening takbir while standing,' it would be better, because opening [the prayer] is only valid in a standing state; even if he said the takbir sitting then stood, he does not become a starter [of prayer] because standing is obligatory at the time of opening, as after it. And if he comes to the imam while he is bowing, and he bends his back then says the takbir: if he is closer to standing, it is valid; if closer to bowing, it is not valid. And if he catches the imam bowing and says the takbir while standing, intending it as the takbir for bowing, his prayer is valid because his intention is invalidated (لغت), so the takbir remains in the state of standing. And if he says the takbir before his imam, his prayer is not valid unless he renews [the takbir], because he followed someone not in prayer, so he does not enter into his [the imam's] prayer nor into his own prayer according to the correct opinion, because he intended participation which is not solitary prayer. And if he opened with 'Allah' before his imam, he does not become a starter in his [the imam's] prayer because he became a starter in his own prayer before the imam's start. And if the imam prolonged the takbir and a man behind him omitted [part] and finished before the imam finished, it is valid according to the analogy of their saying (قولهما), and according to Abu Yusuf it is not valid. And if the follower said the takbir and does not know whether he said it before the imam or after, then if his predominant opinion is that he said it before, it is not valid; otherwise it is valid, because his matter is presumed valid until error is known with certainty or by predominant probability, as in al-Muhit. And what is meant by their saying (قولهما) is that starting [the prayer] is valid with 'Allah' alone without 'Akbar,' and Abu Yusuf said: it is valid only with both, as stated in al-Tanjis here. And from this it is known that what is in Fath al-Qadir from his statement 'the imam finished before him' is a slip of the pen; the correct is: the follower finished before him, i.e., before the imam's takbir, as in al-Tanjis and al-Muhit. And likewise he mentioned in the issue of when the imam prolonged the takbir and did not append to it the issue of when he said takbir before him. And the commentator mentioned in the chapter of ihram that starting the prayer is with the intention at the time of takbir, not with the takbir itself. As in al-Tanjis, the mentioned building [of prayer] because intention is not among the pillars, that it is not valid to perform a prayer by building on the intention of another prayer. He said: (Because he became a starter in his own prayer before the start of the imam) contradicts what he mentioned in the previous issue, that he does not enter into his own prayer according to the correct [view]. He said in al-Sharnabulaliyyah: unless it is interpreted as other than the correct [view], so consider. But in it, he mentioned from Qadikhan what suggests no difference in this [issue] unlike the previous one, for he said: The follower says takbir with... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage details various scenarios concerning the follower's (muqtadi) takbir relative to the imam, highlighting differences between the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (referred to as 'قولهما') and Abu Yusuf. The first ruling concerns joining the imam in ruku': if a person comes to the imam while he is bowing, and he bends his back (as if bowing) and then says the takbir, it must be determined whether his posture is closer to standing or bowing. If closer to standing, the takbir is valid for beginning the prayer; if closer to bowing, it is not. Next, if a person catches the imam bowing and says the takbir while standing, intending it as the takbir for bowing (takbir al-ruku'), his prayer is valid because his mistaken intention is nullified and the takbir counted as the opening takbir in the standing state. However, if the follower says the takbir before the imam, his prayer is invalid unless he renews the takbir, because he intended to follow someone not yet in prayer. Similarly, if he says 'Allah' (beginning the takbir) before the imam, he does not become a follower because he started his own prayer before the imam. Another scenario: if the imam prolongs his takbir and a follower behind him finishes his own takbir before the imam finishes, there is a difference of opinion: according to the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is valid; according to Abu Yusuf, it is not. If the follower is unsure whether his takbir preceded the imam's, he should rely on his predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann); if he thinks it came before, his prayer is invalid, otherwise valid, because the assumption is that the prayer is valid until proven otherwise. The text also clarifies a textual error in Fath al-Qadir: the statement 'the imam finished before him' is incorrect; the correct reading is 'the follower finished before him' (i.e., before the imam's takbir). Finally, a note on the starting of prayer: it is with niyyah at the time of takbir, not with the takbir itself. The passage ends with a cross-reference suggesting that the statement about becoming a starter before the imam may contradict an earlier ruling, and the author references al-Sharnabulali and Qadikhan for resolution.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
قولهما (qawluhuma): Their saying – refers to the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani together.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or belief that something is the case, based on evidence or probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Invalid; he must repeat the takbir.
B) Valid, because the follower intended to follow.
C) Invalid, because he cut off from the imam.
D) Valid only if he is ignorant of the imam's takbir.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the follower's takbir does not require exact synchronization with the imam; the majority view allows finishing before the imam, and ghalabat al-zann resolves uncertainty.

The Follower's Takbir: Finishing Before the Imam – An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of follower's takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the follower's takbir when he finishes before the imam, identify the dispute between the Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf, and apply the ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
A follower who finishes his takbir before the imam – valid according to the Sahibayn, invalid according to Abu Yusuf.

The opening takbir is the gateway into prayer. But what if the follower says 'Allahu Akbar' quickly and finishes before the imam? Is his prayer valid? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on this very question, revealing how the Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf differed on the precise timing requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Locate the key sentence: 'إذا مد الإمام التكبير وحذف رجل خلفه ففرغ قبل فراغ الإمام أجزأه على قياس قولهما، وعلى قول أبي يوسف لا يجزئه'. This sets up the disagreement between the Sahibayn and Abu Yusuf.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the follower's takbir is valid if he finishes before the imam. Their basis is qiyas (analogy): the follower's takbir is independent as long as it occurs after the imam has started.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf (in one narration) holds that the follower must say both 'Allah' and 'Akbar' after the imam has completed his takbir. Finishing early invalidates the entry into prayer.
4
Analyse the ruling on uncertainty
The passage also discusses when the follower does not know if he said takbir before or after the imam. The ruling depends on ghalabat al-zann (dominant opinion): if he is most likely before, it is invalid; otherwise valid.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the follower finishes before the imam, according to the Sahibayn his prayer is valid; according to Abu Yusuf it is not and he must renew his takbir.

Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the conditions of entering prayer via the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). The author begins by noting that the opening takbir is only obligatory at its end (presumably referring to the completion of the takbir phrase 'Allahu Akbar'). He then addresses the ruling for the mute and illiterate: they may begin with intention only, and it suffices because they have done their utmost. It is not necessary for them to move their tongue, according to the correct Hanafi view. The author then prefers that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq had stated that the obligation is the opening takbir while standing, because takbir is only valid when one is standing. Several scenarios are discussed: if one bows first then says takbir while closer to standing, it is valid; if closer to bowing, it is invalid. If one finds the imam bowing and says takbir intending the takbir of bowing, his intention is overridden and the takbir counts as the opening takbir while standing. The core dispute revolves around the follower who says takbir before his imam: according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if he finishes his takbir before the imam finishes his, it is valid, but according to Abu Yusuf (in one narration), it is not. The text also discusses the follower's uncertainty and the reliance on dominant opinion. The commentator clarifies that the correct interpretation of 'finishing before' refers to the follower finishing before the imam's takbir, not the imam finishing before the follower. The passage concludes with notes on the role of intention and the differentiation between the opening takbir and other takbirs regarding tongue movement.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower (person praying behind an imam).
غالب الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Dominant opinion or preponderant probability; a basis for ruling when certainty is lacking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a follower finishes his opening takbir before the imam finishes his takbir but after the imam started?
A) The prayer is invalid because the follower must complete the takbir exactly with the imam.
B) The prayer is valid because the follower started after the imam and his takbir is independent.
C) The prayer is valid only if the follower intended to pray alone.
D) The prayer is invalid unless the follower repeats the takbir after the imam finishes.

Key Takeaway
The follower's takbir is valid even if he finishes before the imam, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position of the Sahibayn.

Recitation as a Pillar in Prayer: The Hanafi Position
Ruling with proof on recitation as a pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation in prayer, cite the Quranic evidence, and explain the intra-madhhab difference over whether it is a pillar.

Core Idea
Recitation in prayer is fard and a pillar according to the majority Hanafi view.

Recitation (qira'ah) is a central act in salah. This lesson examines the ruling that it is obligatory (fard) and its status as a pillar (rukn). We will explore the Quranic proof and a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school that affects how we understand its role in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage says about recitation: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? Note the reported consensus on its obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic verse cited as evidence and understand its role as proof.
The verse is 73:20.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative 'اقرءوا' indicates obligation and the phrase 'ما تيسر' provides flexibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the two views within the Hanafi school: al-Ghaznawi (not a pillar) vs. the majority (is a pillar).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The majority view is supported by consensus and is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والقراءة) لقوله تعالى فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن [المزمل: ٢٠] وحكى الشارح الإجماع على فرضيتها وهكذا في غاية البيان حتى ادعى أن أبا بكر الأصم القائل بالسنية خرق الإجماع وهو دليل على انعقاد الإجماع قبله واختلف في كونها ركناً فذهب الغزنوي صاحب الحاوي القدسي إلى أنها ليست بركن والجمهور إلى أنها ركن غير أنهم قسموا الركن إلى أصلي وهو ما لا يسقط إلا لضرورة، وزائد وهو ما يسقط في بعض الصور الثالث أنه قائماً الإمام، فإن قال المقتدي «الله أكبر) وقوله (الله أكبر وقع قبل قول الإمام ذلك قال الفقيه أبو حفص رحمه الله : الأصح أنه لا يكون شارعاً عندهم. ثم قال: وأجمعوا على أن المقتدي لو فرغ من قوله «الله» قبل فراغ الإمام من ذلك لا يكون شارعاً في الصلاة في أظهر الروايات اهـ. فليتأمل. قوله: (أما الأولى) أي ما يستوي فيها القيام والقعود أقول ولها ثانية وهي الصلاة في السفينة على قول الإمام فإنه يجوز فيها أداء الفرض والواجب قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام قوله : (وأما الثانية) أي ما يتعين فيها ترك القيام قوله إلى أنها ليست بركن عبارة ابن أمير حاج في شرح المنية إلى أنها فرض وليست برکن قوله : (وهو ما يسقط في بعض الصور من غير تحقق ضرورة) قال في النهر : لقائل
His statement: (And recitation) due to His statement: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' [73:20]. The commentator reported consensus on its being obligatory, and likewise in Ghayat al-Bayan, so much so that he claimed that Abu Bakr al-Asamm, who said it is sunnah, breached consensus, which is evidence of consensus being established before him. And they differed on whether it is a pillar: al-Ghaznawi, author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi, held that it is not a pillar, and the majority held that it is a pillar, except that they divided the pillar into original (asli) which is not dropped except for necessity, and additional (za'id) which is dropped in some forms. Third, that he is standing, the imam, for if the follower says 'Allahu Akbar' and his saying 'Allahu Akbar' occurs before the imam's saying that, al-Faqih Abu Hafs said: The most correct is that he does not become an entrant according to them. Then he said: And they are unanimous that if the follower finishes his saying 'Allah' before the imam finishes that, he does not become an entrant in prayer in the most apparent narrations. So reflect. His statement: (As for the first) i.e., what is equal in standing and sitting. I say: and it has a second which is prayer in a ship according to the imam's view, for it is permissible to perform the obligatory and wajib prayer sitting with ability to stand. His statement: (As for the second) i.e., what necessitates leaving standing. His statement: that it is not a pillar. This is the expression of Ibn Amir Haj in Sharh al-Munya: that it is fard and not a pillar. His statement: (And it is that which is dropped in some forms without verified necessity) said in al-Nahr: 'a speaker'.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on recitation (qira'ah) in prayer. The proof is the Quranic verse 'So recite what is easy from the Qur'an' (73:20). The commentator reports consensus (ijma') that recitation is obligatory (fard), and that Abu Bakr al-Asamm's view that it is sunnah is a breach of that consensus, confirming that consensus existed before him. There is a difference of opinion on whether recitation is a pillar (rukn). Al-Ghaznawi holds it is not a pillar, while the majority (jumhur) hold it is a pillar, but they divide pillars into original (asli) – which is not dropped except for necessity – and additional (za'id) – which can be dropped in some forms. The passage then digresses into a discussion about the imam and follower, quoting al-Faqih Abu Hafs on the condition of the follower's entry into prayer, and then returns to commentary on earlier sections regarding standing and sitting, with a note from Ibn Amir Haj that recitation is fard but not a pillar. The text ends with a quote from al-Nahr. The overall lesson is that recitation is obligatory and its status as a pillar is debated, with the majority considering it a pillar.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of the Qur'an during prayer, specifically in the standing position after al-Fatihah.
ركن أصلي (rukn asli): A fundamental pillar that is not dropped except for absolute necessity.
ركن زائد (rukn za'id): A pillar that may be dropped in some forms of prayer without violating its essential nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of recitation (qira'ah) in prayer according to the majority of Hanafi scholars as mentioned in the passage?
A) It is sunnah and not obligatory.
B) It is fard but not a pillar.
C) It is fard and a pillar.
D) It is wajib only.

Key Takeaway
Recitation is fard by consensus and is considered a pillar by the majority of Hanafis; the minority view that it is not a pillar does not affect the operative ruling.

Ruling of Standing (Qiyam) in Prayer: Obligation, Definition, and Exceptions
Explanation of the obligation of qiyam, its definition, and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of qiyam in obligatory prayers, define its proper form, and identify the exceptional cases where standing is waived or optional.

Core Idea
Standing is a pillar of obligatory prayer, but the sick and those with valid excuses may sit — the ruling is not absolute.

Standing in prayer (qiyam) is a fundamental pillar, established by the Quranic command and consensus. However, the Hanafi school recognizes that this obligation is not unconditional. In this lesson, we examine the primary evidence, the precise definition of proper standing, and the specific cases where standing is excused or even prohibited.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its evidence
Identify the hukm (fard/pillar) of qiyam in obligatory prayers and the primary dalil from the Quran (2:238). Note the consensus of exegetes on its application to prayer.
The imperative 'qumu' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
2
Define proper standing (qiyam)
Extract the definition from the text: standing such that when one extends his hands, they do not reach his knees. Understand that this is the minimal requirement.
This is the standard Hanafi definition found in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
3
Identify the general principle and its exceptions
The general rule: qiyam is fard for the capable in obligatory prayers. But exceptions exist: cases where standing and sitting are equal, and cases where standing must be left.
The text gives multiple examples: sick person unable to bow/prostrate, fasting person weakened, incontinent old man, etc.
4
Analyze the specific intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation
Consider the ikhtilaf: should a person who can stand alone but not with the congregation pray alone standing or join sitting? Compare the views from al-Khulasa and Munyat al-Musalli.
The author prefers the view that standing (fard) cannot be left for congregation (sunnah).
5
Note the relative strength of pillars
The text concludes that the pillar of recitation (qira'ah) is stronger than the pillar of standing (qiyam), setting up the next discussion.
This suggests that in conflict, qira'ah takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والقيام) لقوله تعالى وقوموا لله قانتين ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۸] أي مطيعين. والمراد به القيام في الصلاة باجماع المفسرين وهو فرض في الصلاة للقادر عليه في الفرض وما هو ملحق به، واتفقوا على ركنيته وحد القيام أن يكون بحيث إذا مد يديه لا تنال ركبتيه، كذا في السراج الوهاج . ثم اعلم أن قولهم إن القيام فرض في الفرض للقادر عليه ليس على عمومه بل يخرج منه مسألة يستوي فيها القيام والقعود للقادر على القيام، ومسائل يتعين فيها ترك القيام. أما الأولى فما صرحوا به في باب صلاة المريض أن المريض لو قدر على القيام، دون الركوع والسجود فإنه يخير بين القيام والقعود وإن كان القعود وإن كان القعود أفضل فقد سقط عنه القيام مع قدرته عليه وأما الثانية فمنها ما في الذخيرة والمحيط في رجل إن ويصلي قاعداً صام رمضان يضعفه ويصلي وإن أفطر يصلي قائماً فإنه يصوم ويصلي قاعداً. ومنها ما في منية المصلي : شيخ كبير إذا قام سلس بوله أو به جراحة تسيل وإن جلس لا تسيل يصلي جالساً. قال شارحها حتى لو صلى قائماً لا يجوز. ومنها ما فيها أيضاً: لو كان الشيخ بحال لو صلى قائماً ضعف عن القراءة يصلي قاعداً بقراءة ومنها ما في الخلاصة وغيرها: لو كان بحال لو صلى منفرداً يقدر على القيام ولو صلى مع الإمام لا يقدر فإنه يخرج إلى الجماعة قاعداً وهو الأصح كما في المجتبى، لأنه عاجز عن القيام حالة الأداء وهي المعتبرة . وصحح في الخلاصة أنه يصلي في بيته قائماً قال : وبه يفتى واختار في منية المصلي القول وهو يشرع ثم يقعد فإذا جاء وقت الركوع يقوم ويركع والأشبه ما صححه في الخلاصة لأن القيام فرض فلا يجوز تركه لأجل الجماعة التي هي سنة بل يعد هذا عذراً في تركها. وقد علم مما ذكرنا أن ركنية القراءة أقوى من الركنية القيام وسيأتي ما فيه .
His statement (and standing) due to His statement, the Exalted, 'And stand before Allah devoutly obedient' [Al-Baqarah: 238], meaning obedient. What is intended by it is the standing in prayer by consensus of the exegetes, and it is an obligation in prayer for the one able to do so in obligatory prayer and what is annexed to it, and they agreed upon its being a pillar. The definition of standing is that it be such that if he extends his hands he does not reach his knees, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Then know that their statement that standing is obligatory in the obligatory prayer for the one able to do so is not general, but rather there is excluded from it a case in which standing and sitting are equal for one able to stand, and cases in which leaving standing is determined. As for the first: what they stated in the chapter on the prayer of the sick that if the patient is able to stand but not bow and prostrate, then he is given the choice between standing and sitting, although sitting is better, so standing has fallen from him despite his ability to stand. As for the second: among them is what is in al-Dhakhira and al-Muhit regarding a man who... and he prays sitting; he fasts Ramadan and it weakens him and he prays, and if he breaks fast he prays standing, so he fasts and prays sitting. Among them is what is in Munyat al-Musalli: an old man who if he stands his urine drips or he has a wound that flows, but if he sits it does not flow, then he prays sitting. Its commentator said: even if he prays standing it is not permissible. Among them is what is also in it: if the old man is in a condition that if he prays standing he becomes weak for recitation, he prays sitting with recitation. Among them is what is in al-Khulasa and others: if he is in a condition that if he prays alone he is able to stand, but if he prays with the imam he is not able, then he goes out to congregation sitting, and this is the soundest as in al-Mujtaba, because he is incapable of standing at the time of performance, which is the consideration. And in al-Khulasa it is corrected that he prays in his house standing; he said: and by it fatwa is given. And in Munyat al-Musalli he chose the saying: he begins standing then sits, then when the time of bowing comes he stands and bows. And the more appropriate is what was corrected in al-Khulasa, because standing is an obligation, so it is not permissible to leave it for the sake of congregation which is a sunnah; rather this is considered an excuse for leaving it. And it has been known from what we have mentioned that the pillarhood of recitation is stronger than the pillarhood of standing, and what is in it will come.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the standing (qiyam) in prayer. The author cites the Quranic verse (Al-Baqarah 2:238) as evidence for the obligation of standing, and notes the consensus on its being a pillar (rukn). The definition of proper standing is clarified: one's hands, when extended, should not reach the knees. However, the ruling is not absolute; there are exceptions. First, a sick person who can stand but not bow or prostrate has a choice between standing and sitting, with sitting being superior. Second, there are cases where standing must be abandoned: for example, a person who fasts Ramadan and is weakened by standing may pray sitting; an old man with incontinence or a flowing wound must pray sitting if standing worsens the condition; and if standing weakens one's ability to recite, he may sit. Additionally, if a person can stand alone but not with the congregation, the soundest view is that he joins the congregation sitting, though some authorities maintain he should pray alone standing. The author supports the view that standing cannot be abandoned for a sunnah act like congregation. The passage ends by noting that recitation (qira'ah) has a stronger pillar status than standing, setting up the next discussion.

Key Terms
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing upright in prayer, defined as a position where the hands when extended do not reach the knees.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act that is established by a definitive proof (qati' al-thubut) and denial of which is disbelief.
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of prayer whose omission nullifies the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of proper standing (qiyam) in prayer?
A) Standing upright with hands at the sides
B) Standing such that when extending the hands they do not reach the knees
C) Standing with feet together
D) Standing with the head bowed

Key Takeaway
Qiyam is a pillar of obligatory prayer, but the obligation is conditioned on the ability to perform all pillars and is waived in cases of genuine hardship or harm.
