Reciting al-Fatiha: Wajib or Fard? The Hanafi Position
Inter-madhhab dispute on the status of Fatiha recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers reciting al-Fatiha in prayer as wajib, not fard, and evaluate the opposing proof from the hadith 'la salata liman lam yaqra' bi-fatihati al-kitab'.

Core Idea
A solitary report cannot restrict a definitive Quranic text; thus Fatiha is wajib, not fard.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends the Hanafi position that reciting al-Fatiha in prayer is wajib (obligatory but not a pillar) against the claim of the three other imams that it is fard (pillar). The dispute hinges on the nature of the proof: the Hadith 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Opening of the Book' is a solitary report (khabar wahid), while the Quranic command 'recite what is easy' is general (amm) and definitive in transmission. The Hanafis argue that a solitary report cannot restrict the general meaning of a definitive text, lest that be a form of abrogation (naskh). Consequently, omitting Fatiha does not invalidate the prayer but requires sujood al-sahw if done forgetfully, and if done deliberately, the prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding recitation of al-Fatiha in prayer. Clarify that it is wajib, not fard, and state the consequence for deliberate or forgetful omission.
Wajib omission = compensation via sujood al-sahw; no invalidation.
2
Identify the opposing school and their evidence
State that the three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider reciting al-Fatiha as fard. Identify their primary proof: the hadith 'la salata liman lam yaqra' bi-fatihati al-kitab' found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
They interpret the negation as invalidation of prayer.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
Understand the Hanafi methodological critique: the hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid), which is zanni in transmission. The general Quranic command (73:20) is qat'i in transmission. Hanafi usul holds that a zanni text cannot restrict or abrogate a qat'i text. The negation in the hadith may mean 'no perfect prayer' rather than invalidity.
Also, the hadith 'recite what is easy' from Sahihayn supports generality.
4
Analyze the Hanafi second proof from consistency
The Prophet consistently recited al-Fatiha, but persistence alone (without proof of specification for fardiyyah) indicates wujub, not fard. Compare with consistent acts that are only sunnah.
If it were fard, a stronger proof would be needed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: If a worshipper deliberately omits al-Fatiha, the Hanafi prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi and repetition is recommended; other schools declare the prayer invalid and require repetition. For forgetful omission, Hanafis require sujood al-sahw.
The ruling also applies to any wajib left in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وواجبها قراءة الفاتحة وقالت الأئمة الثلاثة : إنها فرض لما في الصحيحين عنه صلى الله عليه وسلم «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب» ولنا قوله تعالى فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن [المزمل: ٢٠] وما في الصحيحين من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إذا قمت إلى الصلاة فاسبغ الوضوء، ثم استقبل القبلة، ثم اقرأ ما تيسر معك من القرآن» فقد أمر الله ورسوله بقراءة القرآن مطلقاً ووافق نص الكتاب القطعي نص السنة فلا يجوز تقييد نص الكتاب القطعي بما رووه من مع ما فيه من كونه ظني الثبوت والدلالة أو ظني الثبوت فقط بناء على أن النفي متسلط على الصحة لأن تقييد إطلاق نص الكتاب بخبر الواحد نسخ له وخبر الواحد لا يصلح ناسخاً للقطعي بل يوجب العمل به. وأيضاً ثبت عنه المواظبة على قراءة الفاتحة فيها ولم يقم دليل على تعيينها للفرضية والمواظبة وحدها كذلك من غير ترك ظاهر التقيد الوجوب فلا تفسد الصلاة بتركها عامداً أو ساهياً بل يجب عليه سجود السهو في السهو جبراً للنقصان الحاصل بتركها سهواً، والإعادة في العمد والسهو إذا لم يسجد لتكون مؤداة على وجه لا نقص فيه، فإذا لم يعدها كانت مؤداة أداء مكروهاً كراهة تحريم وهذا هو الحكم في كل واجب تركه عامداً أو ساهياً. وبهذا ظهر ضعف ما في المجتبى من قوله قال أصحابنا : إذا
His statement: 'And its wajib is recitation of al-Fatiha.' The three imams said: it is fard, because of his statement in the Sahihayn: 'No prayer for the one who does not recite the Opening of the Book.' And our proof is the statement of Allah Almighty: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' [73:20] and what is in the Sahihayn from his statement: 'When you stand for prayer, perform wudu completely, then face the qibla, then recite what is easy with you of the Quran.' So Allah and His Messenger commanded recitation of the Quran absolutely. And the text of the definitive Book agrees with the text of the Sunnah, so it is not permissible to restrict the definitive text of the Book by what they narrated, despite its being problematic in that it is zanni in transmission and meaning, or zanni in transmission only, based on the fact that the negation applies to validity, because restricting the absolute text of the Book by a solitary report abrogates it, and a solitary report is not suitable to abrogate the definitive, but rather necessitates acting upon it. Also, it is established that he consistently recited al-Fatiha in it, and no proof has been established for its specification for fardiyyah. Persistence alone, without apparent abandonment, indicates obligation, so the prayer is not invalidated by omitting it deliberately or forgetfully, but he must perform sujood al-sahw in case of forgetfulness to compensate for the deficiency resulting from omitting it forgetfully, and repetition in case of deliberate or forgetful omission if he did not perform sujood, so that it is performed in a manner without deficiency. If he does not repeat it, it is performed in a makruh tahrimi manner. This is the ruling for every wajib that is omitted deliberately or forgetfully. By this, the weakness of what is in al-Mujtaba becomes apparent from his statement: 'Our companions said: If...'
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and the other three imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) regarding the status of reciting al-Fatiha in prayer. The other imams consider it fard (obligatory, pillar), based on the hadith 'No prayer for the one who does not recite the Opening of the Book.' The Hanafis argue that it is only wajib (obligatory but not a pillar). They present two proofs: first, the Quranic verse 'so recite what is easy of the Quran' which is general, and the hadith 'then recite what is easy with you of the Quran,' which is also general. They argue that these general commands cannot be restricted by a solitary report (khabar wahid) like the hadith about al-Fatiha, because that would amount to abrogation of a definitive text (qat'i) by a probable one (zanni), which is not allowed. Second, the Prophet consistently recited al-Fatiha, but persistence alone indicates obligation (wujub) not fardiyyah. Therefore, omitting al-Fatiha does not invalidate the prayer; rather, it requires sujood al-sahw if done forgetfully, and repetition is recommended to avoid deficiency. If not repeated, the prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi. The passage also critiques the view in al-Mujtaba that suggests otherwise.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An act whose omission invalidates the prayer, established by definitive evidence.
واجب (wajib): An act whose omission does not invalidate but requires compensation (sujood al-sahw).
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for an unintentional omission of a wajib in prayer.
خبر الواحد (khabar wahid): A hadith transmitted by a single narrator chain, which is zanni in transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the hadith commanding it is weak.
C) Because the evidence for fardiyyah (a solitary hadith) cannot restrict a general Quranic command that is qat'i in transmission.
D) Because reciting any surah is sufficient even in fard prayers.

Key Takeaway
Reciting al-Fatiha is wajib in the Hanafi school; prayer is valid without it but requires sujood al-sahw for forgetful omission and is makruh tahrimi if deliberately omitted.

Choice in Prayer Actions for a Sleeping Person
Clarifies the ruling when a sleeping person performs prayer actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid prayer actions when sleep occurs, based on the condition of initiating with choice (ikhtiyar).

Core Idea
Initiate each prayer action with choice; sleep that follows does not invalidate, but adding a complete rak'ah asleep does.

Sleep can interrupt prayer, but not all sleep-related actions break it. This lesson clarifies that if you begin an action (like bowing) with full intention and then fall asleep during that posture, the action is valid. However, if you perform an entire extra rak'ah while asleep, your prayer becomes invalid. This distinction hinges on the legal condition of choice (ikhtiyar) at the moment of initiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for prayer actions
The passage states that prayer actions (bowing, prostrating, reciting) must be performed with conscious choice (ikhtiyar). Sleep after initiation does not remove the validity of that action.
The condition applies at the start of each action, not throughout.
2
Apply the condition to two scenarios
First scenario: one bows intentionally, then falls asleep while in bowing. This is valid. Second scenario: one performs a complete extra rak'ah while asleep. This invalidates the prayer.
The difference is whether the action was initiated with choice.
3
Analyze the reasoning from the sources
The passage cites al-Muhit: sleep during bowing or prostration does not require repetition because the raising and placing occurred with choice. For the extra rak'ah, it is an uncounted addition, so the prayer becomes invalid.
Consensus from al-Mubtagha is mentioned.
4
Derive the general principle
The ruling stems from the broader Hanafi principle that prayer actions require intention (niyyah) and choice for their initiation. Sleep is not a nullifier if the action began validly.
This is a branch (tafarra'a) of the condition of ikhtiyar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

With what the researcher in Fath al-Qadir preferred regarding if one recited while asleep. And it is so; moreover, in al-Mubtagha it is permissible by consensus. And in al-Muhit: that if he slept in his bowing and his prostrations, he does not repeat anything because the raising and placing occurred with choice. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the condition of choice (ikhtiyar) for the actions of prayer in a state of sleep. The author begins by referencing a preferred view in Fath al-Qadir about reciting while asleep. He then explains that if a person bows and then falls asleep during the bowing, it is valid because the action was initiated with choice. Relying on al-Muhit, sleep during the posture of bowing or prostration does not require repeating the action because the movements (raising and placing) were done intentionally. However, a complete extra rak'ah performed while asleep invalidates the prayer, as it constitutes an uncounted addition. This lesson is a specific branch (tafarra'a) of the broader principle that prayer actions require conscious intention (ikhtiyar).

Key Terms
اختيار (ikhtiyar): Conscious choice and intention at the time of performing an action, as opposed to being compelled or unaware.

Adding a Surah After al-Fatiha: Hanafi Wajib vs Others Sunnah
Ruling on adding a surah in prayer: Hanafi wajib vs others sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding a surah after al-Fatiha in prayer, explain the hadith proof, and contrast it with the view of the three other Imams.

Core Idea
Adding a surah after al-Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all nafl – Hanafis rely on a raised hadith.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools regarding the recitation of an additional surah in prayer. The Hanafis hold that it is wajib (obligatory) in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and all rak'ahs of nafl, witr, and Eid, while the three Imams consider it only sunnah. We will explore the Hanafi proof from a hadith in Tirmidhi, the opponent's view, and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Identify the exact ruling: adding a surah (at least three short verses) after al-Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and in all rak'ahs of nafl, witr, and Eid. Note that in the last two rak'ahs it is not wajib nor sunnah but merely permissible (mashru'). The proof is a hadith raised to the Prophet: 'No prayer for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in a fard or other prayer.'
The Hanafi interpretation of 'la salah' is that it indicates deficiency, not invalidity, so the prayer is valid but deficient if a surah is omitted.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
The three Imams (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider adding a surah sunnah, not wajib. They interpret the same hadith as indicating recommendation, not obligation, and may cite other evidences.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf in fiqh.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
The opponent's proof is not fully detailed here, but they consider the hadith's negation 'la salah' as indicating lack of perfection, not a legal obligation. They may also rely on other hadith or practice.
The Hanafi response is that the hadith clearly commands recitation of a surah, and in Hanafi usul, such a command indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school maintains that the hadith is evidence for wujub. They interpret 'la salah' as 'no perfect prayer' or 'no complete prayer' but still the command to recite a surah is obligatory. Additionally, the continuous practice of the Prophet (tawatur) shows he always recited a surah, reinforcing obligation.
The author also clarifies that 'surah' means at least three short verses, not the entire surah.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is that if a Hanafi forgetfully omits adding a surah in the first two rak'ahs, he must perform sajdah al-sahw. In the other schools, no sajdah is required because it is only sunnah.
Also, if one recites in the wrong rak'ah (e.g., last two instead of first two), the Hanafi rules on sajdah al-sahw apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وضم سورة) وعند الأئمة الثلاثة سنة ولنا رواية الترمذي مرفوعاً «لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة أو غيرها (۱) أطلق السورة وأراد بها ثلاث آيات لأن أقل سورة في كتاب الله تعالى ثلاث آيات قصار كسورة «أنا أعطيناك الكوثر» ولم يرد السورة بتمامها بدليل ما سيأتي صريحاً في كلامه. وهذا الضم واجب في الأوليين من الفرض وفي جميع ركعات النفل والوتر كالفاتحة وأما في الأخريين من الفرض فليس بواجب ولا سنة بل هو مشروع، فلو ضم السورة إلى الفاتحة في الأخريين لا يكون مكروهاً كما نقله في غاية البيان عن فخر الإسلام، وسيأتي بأوضح من هذا إن شاء الله تعالى. قوله : (وتعيين القراءة في الأوليين) أي وتعيين الأوليين من الثلاثية والرباعية المكتوبتين للقراءة المفروضة حتى لو قرأ في الأخريين من الرباعية دون الأوليين أو في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين ساهياً، وجب عليه سجود السهو بناء على أن محل القراءة المفروضة الأوليان عيناً وهو الصحيح كما سيأتي بيانه في باب الوتر والنوافل وعلى القول بعدم التعين لا فرضاً ولا واجباً لا يجب سجود السهو وسيأتي تضعيفه. ثم اعلم أن في مسألة القراءة الواجبة واجبين آخرين لم يذكرهما المصنف صريحاً: أحدهما وجوب تقديم الفاتحة على السورة لشبوت المواظبة منه كذلك. حتى قالوا : ا: لو قرأ حرفاً من السورة قبل الفاتحة ساهياً ثم تذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم السورة ويلزمه سجود السهو . وفي كلام المصنف ما يشير إلى ذلك حيث قال: وضم سورة لأنه يفيد وعليه فكل آية واجب اهـ قوله : وظاهره أن الفاتحة بتمامها (الخ قال في المنح أقول : لا يدل ظاهره على ما ذكر لأن إيجاب السجود إنما هو بتركها وهو إذا ترك أكثرها فقد تركها حكماً لأن للأكثر حكم الكل فيجب عليه السجود، وأما إذا ترك أقلها فلا يكون تاركاً لها حقيقة ولا حكماً اهـ. ولا يخفى عليك أن ما ذكره إنما هو وجه للفرق بين ترك الأكثر والأقل ولا نزاع فيه إذ فيه تسليم أن ترك
His statement: (And adding a surah) And according to the three Imams, it is sunnah. And we have the narration of al-Tirmidhi raised: 'There is no prayer for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in a fard or other prayer.' He used 'surah' absolutely, and he meant by it three verses, because the shortest surah in the Book of Allah is three short verses, like the surah 'Inna a'taynak al-kawthar.' And he did not mean the entire surah, as evidence by what will come explicitly in his speech. And this addition is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and in all rak'ahs of nafl and witr like al-Fatiha. As for the last two rak'ahs of fard, it is not wajib nor sunnah, but rather it is permissible (mashru'). So if he adds a surah to al-Fatiha in the last two, it is not disliked, as transmitted in Ghayat al-Bayan from Fakhr al-Islam. And clearer than this will come, God willing. His statement: (And designation of recitation to the first two rak'ahs) i.e., designation of the first two rak'ahs of the three or four-rak'ah obligatory prayers for the required recitation, such that if he recites in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer without the first two, or in one of the first two and one of the last two forgetfully, then sajdah al-sahw is obligatory, based on the fact that the place of the required recitation is specifically the first two, and this is the correct view as will be explained in the chapter on witr and nafl. And according to the view that there is no designation, neither as fard nor as wajib, sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory, and it (that view) will be weakened. Then know that in the matter of the required recitation, there are two other obligatory (wajib) matters that the author did not mention explicitly: one is the obligation of presenting al-Fatiha before the surah due to his continuous practice being established in that way, such that they said: If he recites a letter of the surah before al-Fatiha forgetfully, then recalls, he recites al-Fatiha then the surah, and sajdah al-sahw is required. And in the author's speech, there is indication of that where he said: 'and adding a surah' because it implies that every verse is wajib. End of quote. His statement: And its apparent meaning that al-Fatiha in its entirety... He said in al-Minh: I say: Its apparent meaning does not indicate what he mentioned because the obligation of prostration is due to leaving it, and if he leaves most of it, he has left it legally (hukman) because the majority holds the ruling of the whole, so sajdah is obligatory. But if he leaves less than it, he is not leaving it in reality nor legally. End. And it is not hidden from you that what he mentioned is only a way to differentiate between leaving the majority and the minority, and there is no dispute about it, because it concedes that leaving...
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This lesson comprises two connected rulings: first, the obligation (wajib) of adding a surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and in all rak'ahs of nafl, witr, and Eid, according to the Hanafi school. The three other Imams consider it sunnah. The Hanafi proof is the hadith from Tirmidhi: 'No prayer for the one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in a fard or other prayer.' The author explains that 'surah' here means at least three short verses, not the entire surah. Adding a surah in the last two rak'ahs of fard is neither wajib nor sunnah but merely permissible (mashru'), and it is not disliked to do so. Second, the lesson addresses the designation of the first two rak'ahs for the required recitation. If one recites in the last two instead of the first two forgetfully, sajdah al-sahw is obligatory on the correct view. The lesson also mentions two additional wajib acts implied by the author: (1) the obligation of reciting al-Fatiha before the surah, and (2) that this sequence is necessary; if one recites part of the surah before al-Fatiha forgetfully, he must recite correctly and perform sajdah al-sahw. Finally, it discusses a nuance about leaving most vs. less of al-Fatiha, relating to sajdah al-sahw. The passage ends mid-sentence on page 516, but the main rulings are clear.

Key Terms
ضم سورة (dam surah): Adding a surah (or three short verses) after reciting al-Fatiha in prayer.
مشروع (mashru'): Permissible and recommended, but not at the level of wajib or sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of adding a surah after al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard prayer?
A) It is wajib, and omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is permissible (mashru') and not disliked.
D) It is not permissible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that adding a surah after al-Fatiha is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all nafl, based on the hadith from Tirmidhi; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
